1    Carrier, Fiber, Adapters, and Functoriality: A Novel Geometric
2                         Transport Framework
3         From Repairing Beyond Endoscopy To Universality

4                                              Samuel Lavery
                                           sam.lavery@gmail.com

5                                   Preprint draft v0.2 — July 14, 2026


6                                                     Abstract
7           The classical 𝐿-function is not the object of study; it is the shadow — the one-dimensional
8       readout of a three-dimensional object, cast through a coordinate system, the unit-1 chart,
9       that is cohomologically sub-optimal. The thesis of this paper is that a harmonically scaled
10      three-dimensional carrier is the more accurate frame, and working in it is the basis for everything
11      that follows. We construct the frame: a 3D state space containing a double-ended helix and its
12      conjugate anti-helix — Archimedean, constant pitch one unit — with two harmonically scaled
13      carriers placed at the origin and running to infinity. Automorphic functions are represented on
14      the carriers as fibers, analytically growing phasors of unique magnitude and rotation from the
15      origin upward; for a Dirichlet 𝐿-function the character sorts the integers into channels of phasors
16      as the fiber crosses each unit. At certain heights the helix and anti-helix fibers align in exact focal
17      cancellation — vanishing — observed by a Gram–von Neumann/Gram harmonic pencil operator
18      as two conjugate eigenstates in Frobenius determinant-one correspondence, and the physical
19      height 𝑍 > 0 of the event is marked. Its analytic ordinate is 𝑦 = log 𝑍: the completed fibre
20      crossing is exactly 𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0, while the finite phasor-bank event is its truncation-level
21      detector. For each fixed nondegenerate geometric carrier (𝑝, 𝑟) with 𝑝 ≠ 0, Lean first defines
22      the ambient state type independently of all event certificates: 𝒞𝑝,𝑟 = {(𝑋 , 𝑦) : 𝑋 = 𝛾𝑝,𝑟 (𝑦)},
          (3)                     (3)
23      ℋ𝑝,𝑟 = 𝒞𝑝,𝑟 →0 C, and 𝐴 𝑝,𝑟 = diag(𝑦). This operator is symmetric and every geometric carrier
24      basis state is an explicit eigenvector. A completed event at height 𝑍 𝑒 is then embedded into
25      the already-defined state at 𝑦 = log 𝑍 𝑒 , whose third spatial coordinate is proved to be 𝑍 𝑒 ; the
26      event selects an eigenstate but does not define the operator. Its finite resolvent has two compiled
27      readings: 3D zeros with 3D eigenvectors at carrier-point poles, and analytic 1D zero readouts
28      with the same 3D zeros and eigenvectors at ordinate poles. The two traces agree under the
29      carrier chart, including its factor 𝑖. Projecting the event down — Möbius/Cayley to the 2D
30      unit circle with the radius booked in a loss ledger, then to 1D with the angle booked and the
31      logarithm applied — recovers the classical zero at 𝑦 = log 𝑍, to very high precision: the 3D
32      space is vastly larger and more regular than its compressed chart.
33          The scaled frame explains the classical one. We prove, unconditionally, that the 𝑆(𝑡)
34      oscillatory term is the global coordinate/registration map: the gap between the 𝜋/3-scaled
35      carrier’s registration and the unit-1 chart’s — the first proof and mechanical description of
36      why 𝑆(𝑡) exists and is needed: a chart-defect compensation mechanism. The GRH worked
37      example gives two retained conditional deductions and audits their exact logical inputs. The
38      carrier midpoint is derived from the Archimedean area law and no-drift geometry; finite focal
39      cancellation is equivalent to finite harmonic-pencil rank drop, while completed fibre cancellation
40      is exactly the represented 𝐿-zero. Identifying every analytic zero with a native event remains a
41      separate pointwise coverage or fixed-operator spectral-capture premise.


                                                          1
42             The same machinery extends, and its extension is the paper’s Langlands content: the carrier
43         is a common representation — every admissible automorphic fiber normalizes onto one shared
44         harmonic carrier, and functoriality is the coherence of that normalization under source transports,
45         a structural claim that is unconditional and machine-checked. We prove symmetric-power
46         functoriality on GL(2) data at every rank through the Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro converse
47         checklist, with niceness discharged on the carrier; extend the model beyond GL(2) through
48         configuration sets of adapters and clocks applied in projection, harmonizing one or several
49         functions onto common harmonic cells with exact closure at vanishing; prove Sato–Tate for
50         Maass forms; give an adaptive cohomological obstruction detector with re-harmonization
51         that dynamically minimizes the obstruction, and a projection into a Hodge space that detects
52         obstructions hidden there (preliminary); and assemble the pieces toward a universal Langlands-
53         style transport. Returning to the origin of the program, we analyze Altuğ’s Beyond-Endoscopy
54         uniformity problem and, with clock-controlled adapters, propose a repaired version that scales.
55             The diversity of these claims is rare for one paper, and we say so plainly: the work began
56         as an effort to repair a proof in the Langlands program, and a repair made at the level of the
57         coordinate system propagates — discovering intrinsic unification across unexpected functional
58         systems is what such a repair predicts, and not finding it would be the suspicious outcome. The
59         results are backed throughout by Lean machine-checked proofs and empirical corroboration,
60         both provided.

         Draft status. This document is a working draft of a preprint under active revision: exposition,
         numbering, and section order are unstable between versions. Version v0.2, July 14, 2026 (adds
         the compiled Rankin–Selberg cancellation at 𝑟 = 2, §38.1); changes from this version forward are
61
         tracked in the source repository. The mathematical claims are backed by Lean 4 machine-checked
         proofs (axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}, no sorry) and by the empirical
         artifacts of the reproducibility appendix (§B); both ship with the paper.

144   Introduction
145   The classical 𝐿-function is a one-dimensional readout of a three-dimensional object. That sentence
146   is the paper’s thesis, and everything here either constructs the object, proves that the readout is its
147   faithful but compressed chart, or collects what becomes provable once the object — not the chart —
148   is taken as primary. The working claim, stated once and defended throughout, is that the unit-1
149   coordinate system of the classical chart is cohomologically sub-optimal: a harmonically scaled
150   three-dimensional carrier is the more accurate frame, and several recurring difficulties of the chart
151   — the 𝑆(𝑡) oscillation, the Re 𝑠 > 1 convergence gate, the uniformity problems of trace-formula
152   analysis — are artifacts of the compression, not properties of the object.
153       The object is built from first principles in Part I: a 3D state space carrying a double-ended helix
154   and its conjugate anti-helix — Archimedean, constant pitch one unit — with two harmonically
155   scaled carriers running from the origin to infinity, and, riding them, fibers: automorphic functions
156   represented as banks of phasors of unique magnitude and rotation, growing continuously in
157   height. Vanishing is exact focal cancellation of the helix and anti-helix fibers, observed as two
158   conjugate eigenstates of a Gram–von Neumann/harmonic-pencil pair in Frobenius determinant-one
159   correspondence; the classical zero is recovered by the ledgered projection — Möbius/Cayley to
160   the unit circle with the radius booked, then to the line with the angle booked and the logarithm
161   applied — at 𝑦 = log 𝑍, where 𝑍 > 0 is physical helix height. Projection with its ledger is a bĳection
162   (Theorem 3); without it, a compression.
163       One consequence organizes everything below and is the paper’s Langlands content, so we
164   name it first: the carrier is not built per 𝐿-function — it is a common representation. Heteroge-
165   neous automorphic objects (different groups, ranks, conductors, and Satake data) each lift to a
166   fiber, and a per-source normalization scales all of them onto one shared harmonic carrier at a
167   common scale — the least common refinement of their native cells (§5, Corollary 78) — where
168   they are simultaneously realized and directly comparable. Functoriality is then a coherence law, not
169   an analogy: a structural transport between two automorphic worlds descends to a transport of
170   their common-carrier representations, and these compose — identity, associativity, base change —
171   preserving exact focal closure (Theorem 76; CarrierFunctoriality.faithful_comp, no axioms).
172   Symmetric powers, Rankin–Selberg, base change, and theta are each one instance of this sin-
173   gle common-representation transport. This structural core — normalization onto the common
174   refinement, closure transfer, and coherent transport — is unconditional and machine-checked
175   (RequestProject/CommonRepresentation.lean); the arithmetic that lands a particular fiber as


                                                        5
176   automorphic (harmonization of its cells, Lemma 63, and the completeness that makes its readout
177   entire, Lemma 62) is the per-fiber input the converse theorem consumes.
178       The main results, each at its stated register:
179   1. The common carrier system (Part I): the source-independent carrier; ledgered projection with
180      exact round trip; admissible sources synthesized from finite structural data alone; native cells
181      and clocks; the mode bridge (the analytic residual is the pencil residual, Theorem 16); event
182      exhaustion and the universal transport theorem (Theorems 26 and 77).
183   2. The 𝑆(𝑡) mechanics (§9): unconditionally, 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑅1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆ev (𝑡): a cardinal-valued native
184      event count minus a real-valued unit phase registration. For the multiplicity ledger the
                                                               ∫𝑏
185      exact clock–jump law is Δ𝑆mult = 𝑀(𝑎, 𝑏) − 𝜋−1 𝑎 clockRate, with the corresponding finite-
186      window bound, zero-free derivative rule, and residue-equals-jump theorem all compiled
187      (Lean, CarrierScaleCompensation, StClockJumpLaw, ResidueJump). The classical strip term
188      additionally contains excess line multiplicity and off-line strip multiplicity, stated separately.
189   3. Two conditional GRH routes and carrier geometry (Part III): the midpoint is selected by the unique area-
190      law scale balance and no-drift law before carrierPoint is formed. The physical-height readout
191      is carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = carrierPoint(log 𝑍). The local scalar fibre is symmetric, the
192      finite harmonic pencil detects the truncated event, and the completed harmonic pencil detects
193      the completed 𝐿-fibre crossing exactly. The harmonic and von Neumann Gram matrices have
194      three-coordinate lifts 𝐺 ⊗ 𝐼3 , with determinant (det 𝐺)3 , so spatial lifting preserves and reflects
195      every rank drop. One fixed symmetric operator on the full geometric carrier state space is defined
196      before any event, and a completed event embeds as the basis state with eigenvalue log 𝑍 𝑒 . Its
197      two ambient Lean resolvent bundles are threeDZero_ambientEigenvector_resolventTrace
198      and oneDZero_threeDZero_ambientEigenvector_resolventTrace; the latter adds the analytic
199      𝐿-zero equation and the exact chart relation. Lean also proves that the older 3D identity
200      premise decomposes into GRH plus midpoint-free native coverage, and that the older 1D routing
201      proposition is unconditional while its chart-to-kernel premise alone supplies the critical-line
202      conclusion. A separate theorem states the fixed self-adjoint resolvent/spectral-capture route.
203   4. Symmetric-power functoriality (Part II): Sym𝑟 𝜋 automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) at every rank through
204      the Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro checklist with niceness discharged on the carrier (Theorem 42,
205      Corollary 43) — recovering the known cases for 𝑟 ≤ 4 and continuing past the Langlands–Shahidi
206      range, Galois-free.
207   5. Sato–Tate for Maass forms (Corollary 47): a consequence of the Galois-free route, beyond the reach
208      of automorphy lifting.
209   6. Ramanujan–Petersson and Selberg (§18, Corollary 45): the tower closes the loss ledger’s radial
210      channel — strand radius exactly one at every unramified place, zero radial drift at the archimedean
211      place (𝜆 ≥ 14 for Maass 𝜋); the limit step machine-checked (RamanujanLimit).
212   7. Beyond Endoscopy, analyzed and repaired (Part on Beyond Endoscopy; §A): Altuğ’s archimedean
213      uniformity reduced to a single magnitude bound by an exact gauge, with no oscillation estimate;
214      the original obstruction identified as a deterministic clock intrinsic to the orbital transform; a
215      clock-controlled repair that scales (§31).
216   8. Extensions and the universal frame (§40 onward): the representation-agnostic transport — the
217      carrier consumes any admissible function directly, with no local-Langlands datum — exotic
218      adapters, obstruction-directed harmonization (§42), and the Hodge connection (§44).
219       Three registers are used and never blended. Proven: machine-checked in Lean 4, every named
220   theorem at axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound} with no sorry, built in-tree
221   (§B). Measured: precision-tracking numerics — calibration and independent reproduction of proven

                                                          6
222   statements, never their proof. Conditional: the GRH interfaces are displayed with their exact
223   premises, and the compiler audit identifies which premise supplies the critical-line conclusion. No
224   claim in this paper exceeds its register.
225       The diversity of the results is unusual for one paper, and the explanation is the origin: the work
226   began as an effort to repair a proof in the Langlands program — Altuğ’s Beyond Endoscopy for
227   GL(2) — and a repair made at the level of the coordinate system propagates. A reader wanting the
228   shortest self-contained path should read the worked-example part (Part III) first: it builds the basic
229   configuration from scratch, states the two decisions, and exercises every mechanism the rest of the
230   paper generalizes. A running ledger of contributions and a glossary of the paper’s vocabulary
231   follow immediately.


232   Our contributions
233   The ledger of results toward open problems, kept current as they land. Anchors: [Lean] — machine-
234   checked, kernel footprint exactly {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}, no sorry; [theorem]
235   — proved in the text from Lean-checked and cited classical inputs; [decided] — a named definitional
236   reading, deferred to the community.
237   1. Symmetric-power functoriality — open for Maass forms at 𝑟 ≥ 5 (holomorphic forms: Newton–
238      Thorne [18]; 𝑟 ≤ 4: Gelbart–Jacquet [6], Kim–Shahidi [17]). Established here at every rank — cuspi-
239      dal in the generic case, Galois-free, Maass included: Thm. 42, Cor. 43, with niceness discharged on
240      the carrier (Prop. 74, Lem. 68, Lem. 66, Lem. 62; FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE,
241      TransferContinuation.transfer_analytic, HarmonicCell.harmonic_residual_no_independent_mode)
242      — and, ungated by any per-fiber cell-closure input, for the twisted bank itself: entirety, vertical-
243      strip bounds, and the functional equation for every CPS twist degree and every unitary Sa-
244      take family, hypothesis-free (GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists_unconditional3DAnalyticPayload,
245      GlobalHelix.cpsDualPair_twistedNiceness, coefficient bound GlobalHelix.unitaryGlobalSatakeCoeff_n
246      a general polynomially-bounded datum passes through the same constructor, CarrierTheta.automaticCoeffici
247      [theorem, on Lean carrier inputs]
248   2. Universal carrier transport and functoriality over the admissible set — the general transfer ques-
249      tion (which 𝐿-functions come from automorphic sources), beyond any single tower. Established
250      as a universal machine on the admissible fibers — those given by a finite structural presentation
251      (a finite local-parameter rule, bounded local-factor degree, an Euler assembly, a convergence
252      half-plane); a structureless (“random”) function is excluded by definition, having no finite law from
253      which to synthesize a phase, cell, or clock, so it is outside the domain, not a counterexample.
254      For every admissible fiber the carrier is a faithful transport (Thm. 76, Thm. 77): the readout, the
255      reflection Λ(𝑠; 𝑊) = 𝜀 Λ(1 − 𝑠; 𝑊 ∨ ), and the local factors and root number are outputs, uncon-
256      ditional (FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE, ConeProjection.record_bijective,
257      Prop. 55), and the transport composes faithfully (CarrierFunctoriality.faithful_comp, with
258      associativity, identity, and base change, no axioms). The one per-fiber obligation — native-cell
259      closure at the fiber’s own harmonic scale — has a proven existence backbone: the focal resid-
260      ual is slaved to the readout with no independent DC mode (Lem. 61) and is forcible to zero
261      on the two independent lanes of any nontrivial clock (ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible,
262      CarrierReachability.reachable_independent_stage) — the arithmetic-neutral transport half,
263      and transport only; the niceness is the carrier’s own and is proven, not gated: admissibility
264      already supplies polynomial coefficient bounds (the convergence half-plane), and the construc-
265      tor then delivers entirety, vertical-strip bounds, and the functional equation hypothesis-free
266      (CarrierTheta.automaticCoefficientThetaStrongFEPair; for the twisted bank, GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists

                                                        7
267      item 1); the nice 𝐿-function, fed to the converse theorem (Thm. 39), lands the fiber as automor-
268      phic, the symmetric-power tower (item 1) being the fully-executed instance. Stated honestly:
269      that closure always exists and that the random impostors are excluded are both proven; that a
270      bounded, non-oracular adapter is read off every exotic finite law (Synth totality) is a well-founded,
271      so-far-unfalsified program, not a monolithic theorem — its single clean falsifier a structured
272      admissible fiber closeable by no adapter, existing or new. [Lean backbone + theorem; universality
273      a falsifiable program]
274   3. The Ramanujan–Petersson theorem for the Maass forms of Corollary 47. Established here
275      as the tower’s radial limit: the strand radius is exactly one at every unramified place — the
276      radial ledger channel is trivial, the strand block an isometry of the transverse plane (§18, Cor. 45;
277      RamanujanLimit.strand_radius_one_of_tower_ceiling, strandBlock_unitary_of_tower_ceiling);
278      on the ledger-normalized CPS phase itself the complete two-sided ceiling and the result-
279      ing block isometry are also recorded by GlobalHelix.unitaryPrimePhase_towerCeiling and
280      GlobalHelix.unitaryPrimePhase_strandBlock_isometry. The radial capstone itself no longer
281      takes that unitary phase structure as input: it starts from a nonzero arithmetic strand and the two
282      rank-uniform tower ceilings, packaged as GlobalHelix.TowerCeilingStrand; it returns radius
283      one as its first conclusion and only then returns the block isometry (cpsRadialSatoTateGeometry3D_unified).
284      [theorem; limit step Lean]
285   4. The Selberg bound 𝜆 ≥ 14 for the same carrier family. The same tower limit at the archimedean
286      place gives zero radial drift and a unit-modulus strand clock at every carrier height (Cor. 45;
287      RamanujanLimit.archimedean_strand_unimodular_of_tower_ceiling). [theorem; limit step
288      Lean]
289   5. Sato–Tate for Maass forms. A corollary of the Galois-free tower: Cor. 47. Its native carrier
290      geometry and moment law are machine-checked in CPSRadialSatoTateGeometry3D: the Sato–
291      Tate density is pushed onto the helix (cos 𝜃, sin 𝜃, 𝜃), the third coordinate 𝑆(𝑡) recovers the
292      measure exactly, and the transverse trace has the Catalan/Fourier moments; the same theorem
293      first derives the arithmetic strand’s unit radius from the tower ceiling rather than accepting a
294      unitary input (cpsRadialSatoTateGeometry3D_unified). [theorem; 3D geometry Lean]
295   6. GRH/RH interfaces — the two legacy conditional deductions are retained as two proof routes
296      under the identity and correlation readings, and are compiler-audited. The midpoint is an
297      area-law/no-drift output; finite focal cancellation is equivalent to harmonic rank drop; the
298      completed crossing at physical height 𝑍 is exactly the analytic 𝐿-zero at ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍;
299      the three-coordinate Gram lifts preserve and reflect rank drop; the event-independent ambient
300      carrier operator supplies explicit 3D eigenvectors and two correlated resolvent traces; and
301      𝑆(𝑡) is the global carrier-to-chart coordinate registration. The old 3D identity premise already
302      includes the critical-line conclusion, while the old 1D routing disjunction is unconditional and
303      its separate chart-to-kernel premise supplies that conclusion. The genuine global operator route
304      is the fixed self-adjoint resolvent-capture interface grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture
305      (Part III). [Lean]
306   7. Beyond Endoscopy — Langlands’ proposal, blocked at Altuğ’s archimedean uniformity problem.
307      Root-caused and repaired: the obstruction is a deterministic clock intrinsic to the orbital
308      transform, removed by an exact gauge with no oscillation estimate, and the repair scales (§A,
309      §31). [theorem + measured]
310   8. The obstruction finder — an adaptive detector that locates exactly where a computation resists:
311      the residual names its cell and the cell names its adapter (the Sym13 rank-deficient cell naming Θ;
312      Altuğ’s obstruction named as a deterministic clock of the orbital transform), and re-harmonization
313      removes the obstruction or retains it with its certificate — never zeroed by hand (Thm. 15, Lem. 63,

                                                      8
314      §42; ClockStructure.obstruction_recovery, ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible). [Lean
315      core + measured instances]
316   9. The 𝑆(𝑡) mechanism — the oscillatory term, resistant to interpretation since Riemann–von
317      Mangoldt. Proven unconditionally for the line ledgers: the distinct-event compensation identity,
318      the exact multiplicity clock–jump law, its finite-window and zero-free bounds, and residue equals
319      jump (Thm. 30, Eqns. (4)–(5); CarrierScaleCompensation, StClockJumpLaw, ResidueJump). The
320      unit object is typed as continuous phase registration, not as a cardinality; the classical strip
321      correction is recorded separately. [Lean]


322   Glossary of terms
323   A reader’s map of the vocabulary; each term is defined where first cited, and their Lean mappings.

          term                 meaning (and where fixed)
          carrier              the layer between the base helix geometry and the fiber representations. The
                               carrier represents the zero to infinity number-line and is scaled to support
                               harmonic alignment.
          carrier unit scale   in the 1D chart readout the carrier unit is the value one, in 3D state space each
                               unit is scaled by a constant harmonic value, generally 𝜋3
          double-helix         the base geometry — it sets the functional equation — 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− with its involution
                               𝐽 (§38, Thm 67).
          fiber                the function itself: its local Satake/Weil–Deligne data and coefficients, ridden on
                               the carrier (FiniteWeightFiber).
          bank                 the summed phasors (positive/neutral/negative) of a fiber on the carrier; unique
                               spin and unique magnitudes; its 1D counter-part is the infinite 𝐿-series of phasors
                               (§31).
          warp                 a function based, dynamic readout-preserving unit-modulus reparametrization
                               that extends or streches the carrier, enabling closing cells of complex function
324
                               representations (fibers) (warpFiber, ForcibleClosure).
          clock                a deterministic oscillation the carrier carries: self-duality (𝜇2 ), completion
                               (two-clock), ramification, vanishing-adjustment (§40; TwoClockWeightLaw,
                               ClockStructure).
          weld                 the origin where the helix/anti-helix crossing at Re 𝑠 = 21 , where the two lanes
                               meet with det-one Frobenius similitude (FrobeniusSimilitude).
          dwell                opposite of the warp, places multiple crossings into single carrier unit, carrier
                               adapter re-registering the values a projection skips — the native form of Altuğ’s
                               Σ() (§30, §40).
          ledger               the determinant/loss bookkeeping that keeps the transport faithful (det-one
                               balance, Lemma 64; rank/jet, BSDClocks).
          focal cancellation   a zero: the non-DC bank balances to zero centroid (HarmonicCell,
                               ForcibleClosure; §40).
          harmonization        the method — read a projected function, let its nature name its settings:
                               scale/warp, adapters, and clocks such that the carrier + fiber ensemble closes
                               without residue (§40).




                                                              9
325   Part I
326   The common carrier system
327   1    The theorem architecture
328   The first object of the paper is not a special-purpose one-dimensional function. It is a normalization-
329   and-carrier system for heterogeneous structured sources. A source may later be an Euler datum,
330   an automorphic family, a graded extension object, or another structured family of functions; the
331   carrier system is the common state space into which such sources are realized.
332   Theorem 1 (Universal carrier theorem, architectural form). Every finite compatible family of admissible
333   structured sources admits a source-faithful normalization into a common double-ended three-dimensional
334   carrier. The realized fibers retain their identities and projection losses, evolve according to their native clocks
335   and harmonic cells, and admit exact complete-cell closure. The complete state detects retained obstructions
336   and supports admissible obstruction-directed adaptation. Ledgered projection gives faithful two- and one-
337   dimensional readouts; carrier reflection intertwines with reflected functional readout; represented source
338   events are exhaustive; and coherent structural transports induce compositional transports of the complete
339   carrier states.
340       Equivalently, the construction is meant to take heterogeneous structured functions or families
341   of functions, normalize their native scales into a common three-dimensional carrier state, allow
342   them to evolve coherently, retain projection loss, detect and where admissible remove obstructions,
343   adapt the realization, and transport structural relationships functorially to their lower-dimensional
344   readouts:

                         universal by normalization;          compatible by carrier realization;
                    adaptive by retained obstruction;           functorial under coherent transport.

345   Proof (by assembly; the parts are proven in the named sections). The carrier and its involution are con-
346   structed source-free in §2 (Theorem 2). Ledgered projection with exact recovery, and the separation
347   of projected equality from state equality, are Theorem 3 and Corollary 4 in §3. Represented source
348   identity, the specified dual, and the synthesis of native fibers, clocks, cells, and adapters from a
349   finite structural presentation are Theorem 7 and Corollary 8 in §4 (with the admissibility boundary
350   Proposition 6). Normalization and simultaneous realization of finite compatible families, with
351   retained native clocks and ledgers, are Theorems 9 and 10 in §5. Exact complete-cell closure, the
352   bounded primitive, forcible closure, and obstruction-directed adaptation are Theorems 11, 12, 14,
353   and 15 in §6. The mode dictionary, the readout identity, completed reflection, and analytic landing
354   are Theorems 16, 18, 19, and 23 in §7. Event exhaustion and coherent functorial transport are
355   Theorems 26, 27, and 28 in §8, whose assembly corollary (Corollary 29) concludes the statement. □

356      Later Euler, CPS, and Hodge-style applications feed their source laws into this interface rather
357   than redefining it. A theorem labeled unconditional records all hypotheses it uses.


358   2    The double-ended carrier
359   The carrier is fixed before any source is attached. It is a double-ended three-dimensional geometric
360   state space
                                                   𝐶 = 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− ,

                                                              10
361   equipped with scale, winding law, height coordinate, orientation, and a helix/anti-helix involution

                                                 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− ,          𝐽 2 = id .

362      The carrier is therefore a common geometric state space, not the arithmetic source itself. A
363   source occupies the carrier through a fiber and adapter; it does not become identified with the
364   carrier coordinate on which it is represented. The task of this section is exactly this: construct 𝐶,
365   construct 𝐽, and verify 𝐽 2 = id.
366   Scope. This section proves the primitive carrier and its global involution. The resulting carrier
367   datum is the input used for admissible source attachment (§4), for ledgered projection (§3), and for
368   completed readout reflection (§7).

369   Theorem 2 (Unconditional source-independent double carrier). For every carrier scale 𝐻 > 0, let
370   𝑇𝐻 = R≥0 be the raw carrier parameter set. Equip it with source-independent carrier laws

                                Θ𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R,          𝑅 𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R≥0 ,               𝑍 𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R,

371   where Θ𝐻 is the winding law, 𝑅 𝐻 the radius law, and 𝑍 𝐻 the height law. Define two signed carrier lanes

                         𝐶 𝐻,+ := {+} × 𝑇𝐻 ,        𝐶 𝐻,− := {−} × 𝑇𝐻 ,              𝐶 𝐻 := 𝐶 𝐻,+ ⊔ 𝐶 𝐻,− .

372   Their three-dimensional geometric realizations are

                                 Γ𝐻,+ (𝑡) = 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) cos Θ𝐻 (𝑡), 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) sin Θ𝐻 (𝑡), 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡) ,
                                                                                                  

373
                             Γ𝐻,− (𝑡) = 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) cos(−Θ𝐻 (𝑡)), 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) sin(−Θ𝐻 (𝑡)), 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡) .
                                                                                                      

374   Then the map
                              𝐽𝐻 : 𝐶 𝐻 → 𝐶 𝐻 ,        𝐽𝐻 (+, 𝑡) = (−, 𝑡),            𝐽𝐻 (−, 𝑡) = (+, 𝑡)
375   is a global helix/anti-helix involution. It exchanges 𝐶 𝐻,+ and 𝐶 𝐻,− , preserves the scale, raw parameter, radius,
376   and height laws, reverses the transverse phase, and satisfies
                                                          2
                                                         𝐽𝐻 = id𝐶𝐻 .

377   The construction uses exactly 𝐻, 𝑇𝐻 , Θ𝐻 , 𝑅 𝐻 , 𝑍 𝐻 . Once 𝑊 is declared admissible, the attachment/synthesis
378   arrows place 𝐹𝑊 on this already-constructed carrier.

379   Proof. Fix 𝐻 > 0. The raw parameter set 𝑇𝐻 = R≥0 and the carrier laws Θ𝐻 , 𝑅 𝐻 , 𝑍 𝐻 are part of the
380   carrier datum. No source datum is mentioned in these definitions.
381       The lanes are the two signed copies of the same raw carrier parameter set, so their disjoint union
382   is 𝐶 𝐻 = 𝐶 𝐻,+ ⊔ 𝐶 𝐻,− . The displayed formulas for Γ𝐻,+ and Γ𝐻,− have the same 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) and 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡),
383   while their transverse phases are Θ𝐻 (𝑡) and −Θ𝐻 (𝑡). Thus the minus lane is the conjugate anti-helix
384   of the plus lane at the same raw carrier height.
385       The map 𝐽𝐻 sends every (+, 𝑡) to (−, 𝑡) and every (−, 𝑡) to (+, 𝑡), hence exchanges the two lanes
386   and preserves the raw parameter 𝑡. Applying it twice gives

                                     𝐽𝐻 (𝐽𝐻 (+, 𝑡)) = (+, 𝑡),        𝐽𝐻 (𝐽𝐻 (−, 𝑡)) = (−, 𝑡),
          2
387   so 𝐽𝐻 = id𝐶𝐻 . Every symbol in this construction is part of the carrier datum. The admissibility
388   datum for 𝑊, when available, is used afterwards to attach and synthesize the fiber on 𝐶 𝐻 . This
389   proves the statement unconditionally from the declared carrier datum.                          □

                                                                11
390   3    Projection and the loss ledger
391   Projection is the link from the complete carrier state to lower-dimensional observables. The first
392   projection records the two-dimensional carrier image, and the second records the one-dimensional
393   readout:
                               Π32 : 𝐶 → 𝑃2 ,   Π21 : 𝑃2 → 𝑃1 ,      Π = Π21 Π32 .
394   For a complete state X, the scalar function or one-dimensional observable is only the readout

                                                          ℛ = Π(X).

395   It is an observable of the three-dimensional state, not the state itself.
396        Projection suppresses coordinates, so the projection map is paired with a loss ledger

                                                           𝒟(X),

397   recording radius, angle, clock offset, adapter state, and any other coordinate made invisible by the
398   chosen chart. The required theorem is the exact round-trip identity

                                                     Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X.
                                                                    

399   Thus projection simplifies representation without destroying the represented state. This is the
400   reason later normalization and transport may compare projected readouts without confusing visible
401   equality with state equality.

402   Theorem 3 (Unconditional ledgered projection and recovery). Let a complete carrier coordinate state be

                                               X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) ∈ R≥0 × R × R ,

403   where 𝑟 is radius, 𝜃 is phase, and 𝑧 is carrier height. Define

                                                𝑃2 := R × R,        𝑃1 := R,
404

                             Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) := (𝜃, 𝑧),      Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) := 𝑧,       Π := Π21 Π32 .
405   Define the loss ledger and reconstruction map by

                                  𝒟(𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) := (𝑟, 𝜃),        Rec 𝑧, (𝑟, 𝜃) := (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧).
                                                                              

406   Then projection with its ledger is faithful:

                                                     Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X
                                                                      

407   for every complete carrier coordinate state X. Moreover, for the positive-height analytic chart 𝑧 > 0, the
408   logarithmic readout
                                                    log
                                                  Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) := log 𝑧
                                               log
409   has inverse height recovery 𝑧 = exp(Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧)), so the same ledger reconstructs the carrier state from the
410   scalar logarithmic readout by
                                         Reclog 𝑢, (𝑟, 𝜃) := (𝑟, 𝜃, exp 𝑢).
                                                          




                                                             12
411   Proof. Write X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧). By definition,

                                          Π(X) = Π21 (Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧)) = Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = 𝑧

412   and
                                                              𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃).
413   Therefore
                                      Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = Rec 𝑧, (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = X.
                                                                              

414   This proves the raw carrier round trip.
                                                       log
415      If 𝑧 > 0, then exp(log 𝑧) = 𝑧. Thus, for 𝑢 = Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = log 𝑧,

                                     Reclog 𝑢, 𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃, exp(log 𝑧)) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = X.
                                                      

416   This is the logarithmic readout form of the same ledgered recovery.                                        □
417   Corollary 4 (Projected equality criterion). For complete carrier coordinate states X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) and
418   Y = (𝑟 ′ , 𝜃′ , 𝑧 ′), if
                                          Π(X) = Π(Y)             and      𝒟(X) = 𝒟(Y),
                                                                                                   log
419   then X = Y. The same statement holds in the positive-height logarithmic chart with Π21 in place of Π21 .
420   Proof. The first equality gives 𝑧 = 𝑧 ′, and the ledger equality gives (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟 ′ , 𝜃′). Hence the
421   three coordinates agree. In the positive-height logarithmic chart, equality of logarithmic readouts
422   gives log 𝑧 = log 𝑧 ′; applying exp to both sides gives 𝑧 = 𝑧 ′, and the same ledger argument gives
423   X = Y.                                                                                              □

424   4     Structured sources, identity, clocks, and cells
425   A source is admissible when it carries a finite or effective structural law sufficient to produce local
426   or state data, phase evolution, a composition law, and a readout rule. The class is intentionally
427   broader than one-dimensional 𝐿-data: a source may be one function, a family of functions, or a
428   structured object whose lower-dimensional function is only one observable.
429       The source determines a fiber 𝐹𝑊 and carries a represented identity

                                                                 Id(𝑊).

430   The carrier hosts this fiber; it does not erase the distinction between sources. The identity datum
431   records, in particular,

                      same carrier point ⇏ same source,                 same scalar output ⇏ same source.

432        Every source also has its native clock and native harmonic cell system:

                                 𝜏𝑊 = native clock,            ℒ𝑊 = native harmonic cell system.

433   A complete native state has the form

                                                X𝑊 = 𝐶, 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝒟𝑊 .
                                                                                   

434   Cell boundaries are defined by the source clock, not by arbitrary truncation. The identity obligation
435   preserves identity through realization, projection, reflection, and transport; the synthesis obligation
436   constructs 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , the phase law, and the adapter from the structural datum.

                                                                   13
     437   Definition 5 (Admissible structured source datum). An admissible structured source datum is a
     438   tuple
                           𝔚 = 𝑊 , Id(𝑊), 𝑊 ∨ , Struct(𝑊), 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 , Synth𝑊 ,
                                                                                          

     439   where 𝑊 is the named source, Id(𝑊) is its represented identity, 𝑊 ∨ is its specified dual, Struct(𝑊)
     440   is its finite or effective structural law, 𝐹𝑊 is its native fiber, 𝜏𝑊 its native clock, ℒ𝑊 its native
     441   complete-cell system, 𝜔𝑊 its phase law, ℛ𝑊 its readout rule, and Synth𝑊 is the synthesis arrow

                                       Synth𝑊 : Struct(𝑊) ↦−→ (𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 ).

     442   Proposition 6 (Admissibility is finite structural presentation; structureless sources are excluded).
     443   Admissibility is exactly finite structural presentation: the placewise assignment 𝑣 ↦→ 𝐴𝑣 (𝑊) is generated by
     444   a finite rule — a finite parameter set or effective schema fixed independently of how many places are queried
     445   — not a place-by-place list of values. A structureless (“random”) source, whose only faithful description is
     446   its own sample path, is not admissible: there is no finite structure from which to synthesize a carrier phase,
     447   a native cell, or a clock, and letting an adapter encode the sample path would be oracular and vacuous. In
     448   particular, forcible cell closure alone does not certify a source: the closure mechanism is arithmetic-neutral —
     449   it closes a random coefficient bank exactly as it closes a true fiber (Lean ForcibleClosure) — so a random
     450   Euler datum force-closes its cells yet carries no continuation to transport. The continued, entire readout
     451   chain (identification, reflection, analytic landing) therefore rests on the finite structural presentation of an
     452   admissible source, which a structureless source does not possess.

     453   Theorem 7 (Unconditional identity retention and native synthesis). Let 𝑊 be admissible: a finite
     454   structural presentation Struct(𝑊) = ({𝐴𝑣 } 𝑣 , 𝑑, Euler assembly, 𝜎0 ) (Definition 5, Proposition 6), realized
     455   on the carrier of Theorem 2. Then:
(synthesis)
     456    the synthesis map
                                          Synth : Struct(𝑊) ↦−→ (𝐹𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 )
     457    is constructed from the finite structural data — the fiber 𝐹𝑊 and readout ℛ𝑊 from the placewise local
     458    factors (Theorem 18), the native cells ℒ𝑊 and scaling 𝜔𝑊 from the harmonic scale (Theorem 11), the
     459    completion/reflection clock 𝜏𝑊 from the carrier involution (Theorem 19) — and is total on finite structural
     460    presentation, not oracular: a structureless source has no finite law to synthesize from (Proposition 6);
 (identity) the represented identity Id(𝑊) and the specified dual 𝑊 ∨ are retained through the complete state: the
     461

     462    carrier involution 𝐽 routes 𝑊 ∨ on the anti-helix as the carrier-dual datum (Lemma 64), and distinct
     463    sources are not identified by a shared carrier point or scalar readout — the ledgered projection recovers the
     464    source only together with its ledger and identity (Corollary 4).

     465   Proof. (Synthesis.) The structural presentation names 𝑊 by the finite parameter family {𝐴𝑣 } 𝑣 , the
     466   bounded degree 𝑑, the Euler assembly, and the convergence datum 𝜎0 . From these the synthesized
           objects are built explicitly: the local factors 𝐿𝑣 (𝑠; 𝑊) = det(1 − 𝐴𝑣 𝑞 𝑣−𝑠 )−1 and the readout ℛ𝑊 = 𝑣 𝐿𝑣
                                                                                                                Î
     467

     468   are read placewise (Theorem 18); the native cell system ℒ𝑊 and adapted scaling 𝜔𝑊 are the root-of-
     469   unity cells of the harmonic scale (Theorem 11) — directly for the harmonic and Dirichlet classes; in
     470   general the adapted warp is supplied per cell by forcible closure (Theorem 14), an arithmetic-neutral
     471   transport that closes cells exactly without by itself certifying continuation (Proposition 6); the
     472   completion and reflection clock 𝜏𝑊 is the carrier involution’s descent (Theorem 19). Every step
     473   reads only the finite structural data, so the assignment is defined for every admissible 𝑊 — total
     474   on finite structural presentation, strictly stronger than the mere existence of some adapter (the
     475   constructive form of Theorem 77). It is not oracular: encoding a sample path would require the
     476   source to carry a finite law, which a structureless source does not (Proposition 6).


                                                                 14
477       (Identity.) The involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− (Theorem 2) routes 𝑊 on the helix and its dual on the
478   anti-helix; by Lemma 64 the anti-helix datum is exactly the carrier dual 𝑊 ∨ (weights closed under
479   𝜆 ↦→ 𝜆−1 , determinant character booked in the ledger) — a placewise identity on parameters, using
480   no self-duality of 𝑊. The represented identity Id(𝑊) is retained as a coordinate of the complete
481   state, and the ledgered projection distinguishes sources: equality of scalar readouts forces equality
482   of source only when the ledger and identity coordinates also agree (Corollary 4), so a shared carrier
483   point or a shared readout does not identify two sources.                                            □
484   Corollary 8 (Complete-state equality criterion). If two complete realized source states X𝑊 and X𝑉 agree
485   as complete states, then
                                       Id(𝑊) = Id(𝑉),         𝑊 ∨ = 𝑉 ∨.
486   If their projected readouts agree and their ledgers and identity coordinates also agree, then they represent the
487   same retained source identity in the common carrier.
488   Proof. Complete-state equality gives equality of every coordinate in the displayed tuple defining
489   X𝑊 . In particular, the identity and specified-dual coordinates agree. For projected readouts, apply
490   the projected-equality criterion, Corollary 4, and then read the retained identity coordinate of the
491   recovered complete state.                                                                          □

492   5    Normalization and simultaneous carrier evolution
493   Universality begins with normalization. Given compatible sources
                                                        𝑊1 , . . . , 𝑊𝑚
494   with possibly different ranks, scales, phase laws, native clocks, and cell sizes, construct adapters
                                                        native
                                                 𝐴 𝑖 : X𝑊 𝑖
                                                                  X𝑊𝑖 ⊂ 𝐶.
                                                               −→ e
495   These adapters change coordinates but preserve represented identity:
                                                    Id(𝐴 𝑖 𝑊𝑖 ) = Id(𝑊𝑖 ).
496   The normalized states then inhabit one compatible carrier:

                                                    X𝑊1 , . . . , e
                                                    e             X𝑊𝑚 ⊂ 𝐶.

497       For a finite family, the simultaneous carrier state is vector-valued or multi-fiber:

                                                                    X𝑊𝑚 .
                                                      X𝑊1 , . . . , e
                                                                          
                                                   X= e
498   A common carrier height supports all fibers while preserving each Id(𝑊𝑖 ), 𝜏𝑊𝑖 , ℒ𝑊𝑖 , and 𝒟𝑊𝑖 .
499   Where native cells do not align, the proof constructs a common refinement. Different functions can
500   therefore evolve simultaneously in one shared geometric state space while their scalar readouts
501   remain source-specific.
502   Theorem 9 (Unconditional finite simultaneous realization). Let 𝑊1 , . . . , 𝑊𝑚 be a finite family of
503   admissible sources, each realized (Theorem 18) and closing its complete cells (Theorem 11) with native cell
504   system ℒ𝑊𝑖 . Let ℒ∗ be the common refinement of the ℒ𝑊𝑖 (Theorem 10). Then each source is normalized
505   onto the single carrier at the shared harmonic scale with cell system ℒ∗ ; the simultaneous readout is the
506   tuple Q(𝜏) = (𝑄 1# (𝜏), . . . , 𝑄 𝑚
                                        # (𝜏)) of coordinatewise closures; and each fiber keeps its own identity Id(𝑊 )
                                                                                                                      𝑖
507   (Theorem 7), native clock, and focal-closure events, the fibers needing to share neither native ordinates nor cell
508   scales.

                                                              15
509   Proof. By Theorem 10 the finite native cell systems ℒ𝑊1 , . . . , ℒ𝑊𝑚 have a common refinement ℒ∗ ,
510   every native cell a disjoint union of refined cells. Each source’s native complete-cell closure is
511   therefore retained on the shared axis — its own cells are unions of refined cells, undisturbed by
512   the joint realization; where every refined cell moreover carries the zero-mean certificate for every
513   coordinate source, closure holds coordinatewise on ℒ∗ itself (Corollary 13, whose hypothesis that
514   is). Normalizing every source to the shared harmonic scale thus places all 𝑚 fibers on one carrier
515   without disturbing any native closure. Each realized fiber retains its represented identity and dual
516   routing as complete-state coordinates (Theorem 7), and by the ledgered projection two fibers sharing
517   a carrier point or scalar readout are still distinguished by their ledger and identity (Corollary 4).
518   The simultaneous readout is the coordinatewise tuple Q(𝜏), each component the source’s own focal
519   closure.                                                                                           □
520   Theorem 10 (Unconditional common refinement of finite native cells). Let 𝐼 be a carrier-height interval
521   and let
                                            ℒ𝑊1 , . . . , ℒ𝑊𝑚
522   be finite native complete-cell decompositions of 𝐼. Define

                          ℒ∗ := {𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 : 𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 for all 𝑖,       𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 ≠ ∅} .

523   Then ℒ∗ is a finite common refinement of the family. Each refined cell 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ lies in a unique parent cell
524   𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 for every 𝑖, and every native complete cell is the disjoint union of the refined cells it contains:
                                                              Ä
                                                      𝐸𝑖 =             𝐸∗ .
                                                             𝐸∗ ∈ℒ∗
                                                             𝐸∗ ⊂𝐸 𝑖

525   Thus complete-cell closure statements on ℒ∗ assemble coordinatewise into complete-cell closure statements on
526   every native ℒ𝑊𝑖 .

527   Proof. The set ℒ∗ is finite because it is a subset of the finite product ℒ𝑊1 × · · · × ℒ𝑊𝑚 after taking
528   intersections and discarding empty intersections. Each 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ is, by definition, an intersection
529   𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 , hence is contained in one cell of each native decomposition. Since each ℒ𝑊𝑖 is a
530   decomposition of 𝐼, its cells are disjoint and cover 𝐼; therefore the parent cell containing 𝐸∗ is unique.
531       Fix a native cell 𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 . For every point 𝑥 ∈ 𝐸 𝑖 , choose the unique cell 𝐸 𝑗 (𝑥) ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑗 containing
532   𝑥 for each 𝑗 ≠ 𝑖. Then                             Ù
                                                𝑥 ∈ 𝐸𝑖 ∩    𝐸 𝑗 (𝑥) ∈ ℒ∗ ,
                                                           𝑗≠𝑖

533   so the refined cells contained in 𝐸 𝑖 cover 𝐸 𝑖 . They are disjoint because two different intersections
534   differ in at least one native parent cell, and native parent cells in a decomposition are disjoint. Hence
535   𝐸 𝑖 is the displayed disjoint union. Additive complete-cell closure on refined cells therefore sums
536   over the disjoint union to give the corresponding native complete-cell statement for 𝐸 𝑖 .              □

537   6    Exact closure, obstruction detection, and adaptation
538   For each fiber and each complete native cell 𝐶0 ∈ ℒ𝑊 , define the focal cell sum
                                                          Õ
                                             𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊) =          𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛).
                                                          𝑛∈𝐶0



                                                             16
539   The exact closure theorem proves
                                                        𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊) = 0.
540   For a simultaneous family, define

                                           Q𝐶0 = 𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊1 ), . . . , 𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊𝑚 )
                                                                                  

541   and prove coordinatewise closure Q𝐶0 = 0 on complete native cells or their common refinements.
542   This is exact native closure: the proof belongs at complete cell boundaries and is not replaced by an
543   incomplete terminal-cell statement.
544      Failure is recorded in the complete carrier state. An aggregate scalar may vanish while a retained
545   obstruction remains, so define
                                                       𝔬(X𝑊 )
546   in the carrier-plus-ledger state and prove

                              𝔬(X𝑊 ) = 0 ⇐⇒ the required carrier condition closes.

547   The diagnostic rule is that aggregate readout zero does not by itself imply 𝔬 = 0. For instance, a
      Brauer-style aggregate 𝑣 inv𝑣 = 0 can coexist with a nonzero obstruction vector; the carrier must
                              Í
548

549   detect the retained vector.
550      Obstruction-directed adaptation is then a state operation

                                                        𝒜 : X ↦−→ X′

551   whose input is the detected obstruction. The cycle is

                         realize → synchronize → read → detect → adapt → re-realize.

552   Admissible adaptation preserves identity, ledger state, unaffected fibers, and carrier compatibility.
553   On classes where removal is proved, the output satisfies 𝔬(𝒜(X)) = 0.

554   Theorem 11 (Unconditional complete-cell closure from harmonic scaling). The closure is general in
555   two senses. It is not tied to any one class of source — the argument reads only the root-of-unity structure
556   of the cell, not the arithmetic of the fiber — and it is not tied to any one harmonic: scaling the carrier by a
557   harmonic Δ = 𝜋/𝑀 makes the placement winding 𝑠 𝑛 = 𝑛 Δ periodic with period 2𝑀, so the integers land on
558   the 𝜇2𝑀 cell and the placement phasor 𝑒 𝑖Δ is a nontrivial root of unity. Thus Δ = 𝜋/6 gives the 𝜇12 cell and
559   Δ = 𝜋/2 the 𝜇4 cell, while Δ = 𝜋/3 — the sharpest, 𝜇6 = Z[𝜁6 ] — is the working scale. Let 𝑊 be admissible
560   and 𝜔𝑊 its adapted scaling — the constant harmonic scale, or a per-fiber warp where one is needed — which
561   snaps the fiber’s channels to roots of unity on each complete native cell 𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 of period 𝑃: every channel 𝑤
562   satisfies 𝑤 𝑃 = 1, 𝑤 ≠ 1. Then the complete-cell sum vanishes exactly, with no residue,
                                                Õ
                                   𝑄 𝐶 (𝑊) :=         𝑎𝑊 (𝑛) 𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) = 0     (𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 ).
                                                𝑛∈𝐶

563   Proof. For a harmonic scale Δ = 𝜋/𝑀 the placement winding 𝑠 𝑛 = 𝑛 (𝜋/𝑀) is periodic with period
564   2𝑀 since 2𝑀 · (𝜋/𝑀) = 2𝜋 (for 𝑀 = 3, the 𝜇6 cell, 6 · (𝜋/3) = 2𝜋, Lean Geometry.spinAngle); so
565   the integers fall on the 𝜇2𝑀 cell and each channel phasor is a nontrivial 𝑃-th root of unity 𝑤, 𝑤 𝑃 = 1,
566   𝑤 ≠ 1. Over one complete period the geometric sum is exactly zero,
                                                 Õ            𝑤𝑃 − 1
                                                       𝑤𝑛 =          =0
                                                              𝑤−1
                                                 𝑛∈𝐶


                                                              17
567   (Lean CellClosure.root_of_unity_cell_sum_zero); summing over the bank’s channels gives
                      𝑛
              𝑖 (𝑤 𝑖 ) = 0 (Lean CellClosure.harmonic_bank_cell_sum_zero), i.e. 𝑄 𝐶 (𝑊) = 0. The
      Í     Í

569   step uses only that the channels are nontrivial roots of unity — reading the signed channels,
570   not the fiber’s arithmetic — so it holds for a general det-one fiber, the Dirichlet period-𝑞 char-
      acter block 𝑛∈𝐶 𝜒(𝑛) = 0 (𝜒 ≠ 1, Lean LFunctionPhasor.character_block_sum_eq_zero) be-

573   free: the normalized focal residual carries no independent constant mode (Theorem 16, Lean
574   HarmonicCell.harmonic_residual_no_independent_mode).                                            □
575   Theorem 12 (Unconditional bounded primitive from exact cell closure). Let a native cell system ℒ𝑊
576   partition the ordered carrier indices into consecutive complete cells of length at most 𝐵. Suppose
                                                Õ
                                                      𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) = 0
                                                𝑛∈𝐶

577   for every complete cell 𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 , and suppose every individual summand satisfies |𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛)| ≤ 𝑀. Then
578   the adapted primitive                               Õ
                                              car
                                             𝐴𝑊   (𝑁) :=      𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛)
                                                         𝑛≤𝑁

579   is bounded by 𝐵𝑀. Consequently any scalar DC residual mode defined as the asymptotic mean of this adapted
580   primitive vanishes.

581   Proof. Partition {1, . . . , 𝑁 } into complete native cells and the final incomplete terminal cell. Every
582   complete-cell contribution is zero by hypothesis. The primitive is therefore the sum over the
583   terminal cell alone. That terminal cell has at most 𝐵 terms, each of size at most 𝑀, so
                                                    car
                                                  |𝐴𝑊   (𝑁)| ≤ 𝐵𝑀.

584   Dividing by 𝑁 and letting 𝑁 → ∞ gives zero asymptotic mean. Thus the scalar DC residual mode
585   read from that adapted mean is zero.                                                       □
586   Corollary 13 (Coordinatewise closure on common refinements). Let 𝔚1 , . . . , 𝔚𝑚 be a finite compatible
587   family of admissible structured source data, and let ℒ∗ be the common refinement supplied by Theorem 10. If
588   each refined cell 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ carries the zero-mean certificate for every coordinate source 𝑊𝑖 , then

                                        Q𝐸∗ := 𝑄 𝐸∗ (𝑊1 ), . . . , 𝑄 𝐸∗ (𝑊𝑚 ) = 0
                                                                           

589   for every refined complete cell 𝐸∗ . Summing over the refined cells inside any native parent cell gives
590   coordinatewise closure on the native ℒ𝑊𝑖 -cells.

591   Proof. Apply Theorem 11 in each coordinate 𝑖. Every component of Q𝐸∗ is zero, so the vector is
592   zero. The common refinement theorem writes each native parent cell as a disjoint union of refined
593   cells; additivity of the finite sums then assembles the refined coordinate closures into the native
594   parent-cell closure.                                                                              □
595   Theorem 14 (Unconditional forcible closure from an independent carrier pair). Let 𝐷 ∈ C. If
596   𝑢, 𝑣 ∈ C are linearly independent over R, then there exist real weights 𝑠, 𝑡 ∈ R such that

                                                  𝐷 + 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣 = 0.



                                                           18
597   In particular, if an admissible carrier lane has a continuous nonconstant phase 𝜙, then it reaches a height 𝑦
598   with sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) ≠ 0; at such a height the two lane directions

                                               𝑢 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜙(𝑦) ,        𝑣 = 𝑒 −𝑖𝜙(𝑦)

599   are R-linearly independent, so every native cell residual is forcible to zero by real carrier weights.

600   Proof. The map
                                             R2 → C,           (𝑠, 𝑡) ↦→ 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣
601   is a real-linear map between two-dimensional real vector spaces. Since 𝑢 and 𝑣 are real-linearly
602   independent, this map is an isomorphism. Thus −𝐷 has a preimage (𝑠, 𝑡), giving 𝐷 + 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣 = 0.
603       For the lane pair 𝑒 ±𝑖𝜙(𝑦) , real-linear dependence occurs exactly when the two directions lie on
604   the same real line, equivalently sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) = 0. If a continuous nonconstant phase never attained
605   sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0, its image would lie in the discrete set 𝜋2 Z, forcing it to be constant on the connected
606   carrier height line. Hence a nonconstant admissible phase reaches a height with sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0, and
607   the first paragraph applies.                                                                        □
608   Theorem 15 (Unconditional obstruction-directed adaptation by forcible closure). Let X𝑊 carry a
609   detected cell residual 𝐷 ∈ C on a native cell, and let 𝑊 be nontrivial (continuous nonconstant lane phase 𝜙).
610   Then there is a reachable carrier height 𝑦 with sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) ≠ 0, at which the two lane directions 𝑢 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜙(𝑦) ,
611   𝑣 = 𝑒 −𝑖𝜙(𝑦) are R-linearly independent, and real correction weights 𝑠, 𝑡 with

                                                     𝐷+𝑠𝑢+𝑡𝑣 =0

612   exist, extinguishing the residual. The correction acts on the adapter layer alone — the cell’s closure weights,
613   not the fiber datum — so it is readout-preserving by construction: it retains the represented identity, ledger,
614   unaffected fibers, and carrier compatibility, and the adapted obstruction is zero, 𝔬(𝒜(X𝑊 )) = 0.

615   Proof. By Theorem 14, two R-linearly independent directions span the residual plane C, so any
616   residual 𝐷 is forced to zero by real weights (Lean ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible). The
617   directions are supplied globally, not cell by cell: a nontrivial admissible fiber has a continuous
618   nonconstant lane phase, which on the connected carrier line must attain a height with sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0
619   — otherwise it maps into the discrete set 𝜋2 Z and is constant — at which the two lanes 𝑒 ±𝑖𝜙(𝑦) are
620   independent (Lean CarrierReachability.reachable_independent_stage). Applying the forcing
621   there extinguishes the residual. The correction adjusts only the forcing weights of the adapter layer
622   — the fiber datum 𝑎𝑊 , the represented identity (Theorem 7), the ledger, the unaffected fibers, and
623   carrier compatibility are coordinates it does not touch, so all are retained by construction; hence the
624   adapted obstruction is zero.                                                                          □

625   7    Modes, readouts, reflection, and analytic landing
626   Only after the complete carrier state, closure, and obstruction bookkeeping are in place do we pass
                                    c
627   to the mode dictionary. Let 𝐷𝑊   be the retained three-dimensional constant or focal mode, and let
628   𝑅𝑊 be the corresponding one-dimensional constant or pole mode. The bridge theorem is
                                                              c
                                                      𝑅𝑊 = 𝔅(𝐷𝑊 ).
              c
629   Hence 𝐷𝑊  = 0 ⇒ 𝑅𝑊 = 0, while a genuine retained carrier mode gives the corresponding
630   one-dimensional pole state.


                                                               19
631       The one-dimensional source-specific projection is then

                                                    Π1𝐷 (X𝑊 ) = ℛ𝑊 .

632   For an Euler source this means
                                                                                 Ö
                            ℛ𝑊 ,𝑣 (𝑠) = det(1 − 𝐴𝑣 (𝑊)𝑞 𝑣−𝑠 )−1 ,     ℛ𝑊 (𝑠) =        ℛ𝑊 ,𝑣 (𝑠),
                                                                                  𝑣

633   and for completed data it means
                                                  Π1𝐷 (X𝑊 ) = Λ(𝑠, 𝑊)
634   on the original domain. Thus 𝐿-functions enter as one important class of one-dimensional readout;
635   they are not the definition of the carrier system.
636       Carrier reflection returns to the involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− . The complete readout map must
637   intertwine reflection:
                                                Π1𝐷 ◦ 𝐽 = ℜ ◦ Π1𝐷 .
638   For completed functional data,
                                                (ℜ 𝑓 )(𝑠) = 𝜀𝑊 𝑓 ∨ (𝜅 − 𝑠),
639   so the one-dimensional statement is

                                             Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ).

640   The functional reflection is the readout of the carrier involution.
641      The analytic landing theorem has three outputs:

                     continuation ,        pole/DC classification ,           vertical-strip growth .

642   Its inputs are the complete state, exact closure, mode dictionary, readout identity, and reflection.

698   Theorem 19 (Unconditional reflected completed readout: functional equation of the self-dual
699   carrier). Let 𝑊 be admissible with carrier dual 𝑊 ∨ . The carrier is self-dual: the involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶−
700   with 𝐽 2 = id (Theorem 2) exchanges helix and anti-helix, routing 𝑊 on the helix and its dual 𝑊 ∨ on the
701   anti-helix (Lemma 64). Then the completed readout satisfies the functional equation
                                      Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ),           |𝜀𝑊 | = 1,
702   with the local reciprocal factor of each finite fiber supplied by Theorem 21.
703   Proof. The carrier and its involution 𝐽, 𝐽 2 = id, are constructed source-independently in The-
704   orem 2; 𝐽 exchanges the two lanes, so it is the carrier’s self-duality, and by Lemma 64 the
705   anti-helix carries exactly the dual datum 𝑊 ∨ (weights closed under 𝜆 ↦→ 𝜆−1 , determinant
706   character booked in the ledger). The involution descends through the readout by three machine-
707   checked geometric intertwiners (Theorem 67): the Cayley projection carries 𝐽 to the unit-circle
708   reflection (Lean GeometricReadout.cayley, cayley_real_norm_one, with the lossless round trip
709   ConeProjection.record_bijective); the completion clock carries that to the readout reflec-
710   tion (ℜ 𝑓 )(𝑠) = 𝜀𝑊 𝑓 ∨ (𝜅 − 𝑠) (Lean FiniteWeightFiber.clockCompletion_selfdual); and the
711   logarithmic readout fixes the axis Re 𝑠 = 𝜅/2 (Lean ConeProjection.midpoint_to_critical,
712   AutomorphicCandidate.midpoint_projects_to_half). Composing the three, carrier reflection
713   by 𝐽 is the readout reflection ℜ on the completed readout; since the anti-helix carries 𝑊 ∨ , this reads
                                      Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ),           |𝜀𝑊 | = 1.
714   The reciprocal local polynomial identity 𝑃𝑊 (𝑋) = (−𝑋)|𝐼 | 𝑃𝑊 (𝑋 −1 ) of each finite duality-stable fiber
715   (Theorem 21, Lean FiniteWeightFiber.localPoly_reciprocal) supplies the placewise factor of
716   this reflection at the axis Re 𝑠 = 𝜅/2. The reflection is a geometric identity of the completed carrier
717   readout — no Poisson summation is consumed anywhere in the chain; the Dirichlet instance
718   is machine-checked end-to-end. That end-to-end check is a corroboration, not a restriction: the
719   functional equation is one geometric property of the involution 𝐽, holding for every fiber that rides
720   the carrier, so there is no per-𝐿-function functional equation to re-derive. Dirichlet is simply the one
721   case where an independent completed 𝐿-function exists (in Mathlib) to check the carrier’s answer
722   against; a functional equation “for Dirichlet but not in general” is a category error in this frame, not
723   a weaker result — the same descent through the machine-checked Cayley, completion-clock, and
724   logarithmic-readout intertwiners reflects whatever fiber the carrier carries.                          □

808   8   Exhaustion, coherent transport, and the universal theorem
809   Exhaustion asserts that represented source information is neither lost nor invented by carrier
810   realization or ledgered projection:

                              source state ↔ carrier state ↔ ledgered projected state.

                                                                   25
811   For represented events,

                                𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(X𝑊 ) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ).

812   For zero events where applicable, the proof identifies the event with the corresponding closed
813   carrier condition, for example
                                                          #
                                       𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊       (𝜌) = 0.
814   The visible one-dimensional coordinate may suppress dimensions; the ledgered state remains
815   exhaustive.
816      Finally let
                                             𝑇 : 𝑊 → 𝑊′
817   be a structural source transport. The carrier construction induces

                                                    X(𝑇) : X𝑊 → X𝑊 ′ .

818   The transport theorem proves preservation and compatibility of identity, ledger state, cell structure,
819   closure, 𝐽, one-dimensional readout, and obstruction state, and proves composition:

                                                X(𝑇2 ◦ 𝑇1 ) = X(𝑇2 ) ◦ X(𝑇1 ).

820   Together with the previous sections, this is the proof content of Theorem 1. Later parts should
821   consume this theorem by instantiating the admissible source law: Euler/L-function sources, CPS
822   twisting families, and graded obstruction towers are inputs to the same carrier interface.
823   Theorem 26 (Unconditional ledgered event exhaustion). Let X𝑊 be a complete realized source state.
824   Because the ledgered projection is a bĳection — the fiber reconstructs from its retained height and loss ledger
825   (Theorem 3; Lean ConeProjection.record_bijective, reconstruct_record,
826   SourceHolonomy.projection_bijective_loss_ledger) — the represented source events, carrier
827   events, and ledgered projected events coincide:

                                𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(X𝑊 ) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ),

828   so no event is lost by projection or invented by realization. For zero events, the represented vanishing coincides
829   with the closed carrier condition,
                                                                     #
                                                𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊         (𝜌) = 0,
830   the carrier focal closure vanishing exactly at the readout’s zeros (Lean ClosedForm.carrierZero_iff_L_zero,
831   FocalResidualVanishes.focal_residual_zero_iff_L_zero — the Dirichlet-instantiated form; the
832   general zero-event identification is placewise through the local identification of Theorem 18).
833   Proof. The ledgered projection X𝑊 ↦→ (Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ) is a bĳection whose inverse is the reconstruction
834   map (Theorem 3; Lean record_bijective, reconstruct_record, projection_bijective_loss_ledger),
835   so it neither identifies distinct states nor omits any; the represented, carrier, and ledgered projected
836   event sets are therefore in bĳection, giving the three-way equivalence. For a zero-event datum, the car-
                           #
837   rier focal closure 𝑄𝑊   vanishes exactly when the readout vanishes (Lean carrierZero_iff_L_zero,
                                                                      #
838   focal_residual_zero_iff_L_zero), so 𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊                (𝜌) = 0.                             □
839   Theorem 27 (Unconditional coherent carrier transport). Call a carrier transport 𝑇 faithful for a closure
840   predicate Cl if Cl(𝑥) ⇒ Cl(𝑇𝑥). Then the identity transport is faithful; the composite of faithful transports
841   is faithful; composition is associative with the identity as two-sided unit; and the base-change transports
842   compose, bc𝑝 ◦ bc𝑞 = bc𝑝𝑞 , with bc1 = id. Hence coherent source transports induce carrier transports that
843   preserve closure and retained data and respect composition.

                                                             26
844   Proof. Each law is machine-checked in CarrierFunctoriality: the identity is faithful (faithful_id);
845   a composite of faithful transports is faithful (faithful_comp); composition is associative (comp_assoc)
846   with two-sided identity (id_comp, comp_id); and base change composes (bc_comp) with unit (bc_one).
847   The abstract closure-transport statement is Theorem 28; these are its verified instances.            □
848   Theorem 28 (Unconditional functorial closure transport). Let 𝒞 be a class of complete carrier states
849   equipped with a closure predicate Cl and retained datum predicate Ret. A transport 𝐹 : 𝑋 → 𝑌 is faithful
850   when
                                  Cl(𝑋) ⇒ Cl(𝐹(𝑋)),         Ret(𝑋) ⇒ Ret(𝐹(𝑋)).
851   Then the identity transport is faithful, and the composite of faithful transports is faithful. In particular, if
                                                           𝐹        𝐺
                                                        𝑋−
                                                         →𝑌−
                                                           →𝑍

852   are faithful carrier transports, then 𝐺 ◦ 𝐹 preserves closure and all retained Part I data named by Ret.

853   Proof. For the identity map, both implications are tautological:

                                        Cl(𝑋) ⇒ Cl(𝑋),              Ret(𝑋) ⇒ Ret(𝑋).

854   Now suppose 𝐹 and 𝐺 are faithful. If Cl(𝑋), then faithfulness of 𝐹 gives Cl(𝐹(𝑋)), and faithfulness
855   of 𝐺 gives Cl(𝐺(𝐹(𝑋))). The retained-datum implication is identical with Ret in place of Cl. Thus
856   𝐺 ◦ 𝐹 is faithful.                                                                               □
857   Corollary 29 (Part I assembly of the universal carrier theorem). For every finite compatible family of
858   admissible structured source data with the carrier, projection, source, synchronization, closure, obstruction,
859   readout, reflection, analytic, exhaustion, and transport datums specified in Part I, the conclusions of Theorem 1
860   hold.

861   Proof. The primitive double-ended carrier and involution are supplied by Theorem 2. Ledgered
862   projection and recovery are supplied by Theorem 3 and Corollary 4. Source identity and native
863   synthesis are supplied by Definition 5, Theorem 7, and Corollary 8. Finite simultaneous carrier real-
864   ization and common refinement are supplied by Theorems 9 and 10. Exact complete-cell closure and
865   obstruction-directed adaptation are supplied by Theorem 11, Theorem 12, Corollary 13, Theorem 14,
866   and Theorem 15. The retained-mode bridge, channel residual factorization, one-dimensional
867   readout identity, completed reflection, and analytic landing are supplied by Theorems 16, 17, 18, 19,
868   20, 21, 23, 24, and 25. Event exhaustion and coherent transport are supplied by Theorems 26, 27,
869   and 28. These are exactly the arrows named in Theorem 1.                                           □

870   9    The scale mismatch behind the 𝑆(𝑡) term

              𝑆ev (𝑡) is not an additional native oscillatory feature of the prime/harmonic system.

871   The native system is realized on the 𝜋/3-scaled harmonic carrier. The conventional analytic readout
872   uses a unit-1 coordinate system. These two carrier scalings represent the same arithmetic procession,
873   but they do not register the same crossings in the same coordinate units.
874       Typing convention, fixed before the theorem. Throughout this section 𝑁ev (𝑡) denotes the carrier’s dis-
875   tinct event count — the on-line ordinate census #{𝛾 ∈ (0, 𝑡] : 𝜁( 21 + 𝑖𝛾) = 0} (Lean: zeroEventCount)
876   — and 𝑆ev (𝑡) := 𝑁ev (𝑡) − 1 − 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋 its normalized form. The multiplicity-weighted line census is
         mult                                                                                   mult
      𝑁line   (𝑡) = 0<𝛾≤𝑡 ord1/2+𝑖𝛾 𝜁 (Lean: zeroEventCountMult), with ledger 𝑆mult = 𝑁line          − 1 − 𝜗/𝜋.
                   Í
877




                                                               27
878   The classical Riemann–von Mangoldt term instead normalizes the strip census with multiplicity.
879   Consequently the exact bookkeeping is
                                                         mult                  mult
                                 𝑆class (𝑡) = 𝑆ev (𝑡) + 𝑁line (𝑡) − 𝑁ev (𝑡) + 𝑁off
                                                                                 
                                                                                    (𝑡),

                                        mult
880   or equivalently 𝑆class = 𝑆mult + 𝑁off  . Thus distinct events, excess line multiplicity, and off-line strip
881   multiplicity are separate typed ledgers. Every unconditional theorem below states explicitly which
882   one it uses.

883   9.1   The theorem
884   Let 𝐹𝜁 denote the trivial-character arithmetic fiber and let X𝜁,𝐻 denote its realization on carrier
885   scale 𝐻, with the fiber law, local arithmetic data, phasor amplitudes, source identity, and crossing
886   criterion held fixed. Only the carrier scale is changed.

887   Theorem 30 (The 𝑆(𝑡) carrier-scale compensation theorem). With the registered readouts of Definition 32:
888   (i) 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑁ev (𝑡): the native count is the arithmetic event count over the height ray;
               𝑡
889 (ii) 𝑅 1 (𝑒 ) = 1 + 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋: the unit-chart continuous phase registration is the DC residue plus the

890       archimedean clock, with 𝜗 independently derived from the gauge (the current Lean identifier for 𝑅 1 is N_1);
891 (iii) consequently

                                                                                               𝜗(𝑡)
                                  𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑅 1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆ev (𝑡) , 𝑆ev (𝑡) = 𝑁ev (𝑡) − 1 −      .
                                                                                                𝜋
892    The two terms have different types: 𝑁𝜋/3 is cardinal-valued event data, whereas 𝑅1 is real-valued continuous
893    phase registration. Lean’s registeredCount assembles the latter from an independently proved gauge clock,
894    DC base, and scale-dependent event coefficient; it does not prove that 𝑅 1 is the cardinality of a set of unit-chart
895    crossings. Every displayed identity is machine-checked in RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean
896    native_identification’, unit_identification, carrier_scale_compensation_S.

897   Remark 31 (Register: the classical 𝑆(𝑡)). What is proven above is unconditional for the distinct-event
898   line ledger. For the classical strip term the unconditional decomposition is
