902   9.2   Independent contour coordinate for the classical argument
903   The classical argument is constructed independently of every event and zero-count ledger. At a
904   good height 𝑇 > 0, meaning that no nontrivial zero has ordinate 𝑇, let

                                                                            1
                                             Γ𝑇 :      2 −→ 2 + 𝑖𝑇 −→         + 𝑖𝑇.
                                                                            2
905   The first segment lies in Re 𝑠 = 2, where Euler-product nonvanishing applies. On the second
906   segment, a hypothetical vanishing either has Re 𝑠 ≥ 1, again contradicting nonvanishing, or is a
907   nontrivial zero of ordinate 𝑇, contradicting goodness. Thus 𝜁 ◦ Γ𝑇 is a path in C× .

952   9.3   The event count and the phase registration
953   Definition 32 (Scale-indexed registered readout). For a carrier realization X𝜁,𝐻 , write
                   𝒞𝐻 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑧) = { 𝑐 : 𝑐 is a complete 𝐹𝜁 -closure in X𝜁,𝐻 through raw height 𝑧 }.
954   At the native scale the cumulative crossing count is
                                                  𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = #𝒞𝜋/3 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑒 𝑡 ).
955   The unit chart instead supplies the real-valued phase registration
                                                                            𝜗(𝑡)
                                                         𝑅 1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 1 +        .
                                                                             𝜋
956   The theorem compares these two readouts; it does not identify the continuous quantity 𝑅1 with
957   a cardinality. A topological-degree or contour-winding coordinate for the classical argument is
958   instead constructed in (1)–(3); it is a path lift of the actual zeta fiber, not a reinterpretation of 𝑅1 as a
959   set cardinality.
960       In Lean the scale-indexed registered readout is installed as registeredCount: DC base at
961   the common origin, an independently constructed continuous clock procession in 𝜋-units, and
962   the event count weighted by the induced per-event contribution of the scale’s closure geometry
963   (eventContribution; derivation in the discharged-arrows subsection below). The closure predicate
964   is NativeClosure (the fiber’s 𝜂-accumulation) and the counts are nativeCount and zeroEventCount.

               cell_antipodal_cancel,                helix_cancellation_logfree,           readout_exp

973   Proof of Theorem 30(i). A complete closure of the fiber at ordinate 𝛾 is exactly an on-line zero
974   event: the fiber’s own 𝜂-accumulation closes at 𝛾 if and only if the readout vanishes there
975   (nativeClosure_iff_zero, via Faithful.continuous_model_zeta), and the height readout carries
976   raw height 𝑒 𝑡 to ordinate 𝑡 exactly (readout_exp). Here 𝑁ev (𝑡) is the zero-counting procession
977   over the 3D representation’s entire event space — the height ray, whose exhaustion is a theorem,
978   consumed not assumed (native_events_sourced, instantiating the proven threeD_exhaustive;
979   the height encoding is lossless, event_encoding_complete). Counting complete closures through
980   raw height 𝑒 𝑡 therefore counts exactly the arithmetic events through ordinate 𝑡: 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑁ev (𝑡)
981   (native_identification’). No 𝑆(𝑡) term is an additional state variable in X𝜁,𝜋/3 .                   □

1018   Remark 33 (No native oscillatory state). The structural consequence — 𝑆ev (𝑡) has no additional
1019   native oscillatory carrier state — is S_has_no_native_carrier with no_native_oscillation:
1020   despinning the unit readout by the clock leaves a real value at every height. The distinct and
1021   multiplicity-weighted line ledgers record the event jumps against that continuous clock. Per
1022   Remark 31, the classical strip term additionally contains off-line strip multiplicity.

1023   9.8   The arrows, discharged
1024   The native cumulative count and the unit phase registration are assembled in RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompen
1025   Their inputs have the following proved origins:
1026   • Event channel. An event is a sign flip of the real native state; its mark is the half turn −1 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜋
1027     (sign_flip_mark). A scale-𝐻 chart registers the mark only through a completed cell arc realizing
1028     it, eventArcs 𝐻 = {𝑘 ≥ 1 : 𝑒 𝑖 𝑘𝐻 = −1}. At 𝜋/3 the wall is hit exactly once per closed six-cell
1029     monodromy loop (pi3_wall_mem, from the antipodal identity; pi3_arcs_eq: the arcs are exactly
1030     𝑘 ≡ 3 (mod 6)) — one registered event per completed native cell. At scale 1 no arc ever realizes
1031     the mark (unit_arcs_empty). The induced per-event contribution (eventContribution) is 1 at
1032     𝜋/3 and 0 at 1 by theorems, not by a gate.
1033   • Clock channel. The native chart’s zero clock is derived, not assigned: every continuous clock its
1034     readout factors through is constant on event-free stretches (native_clock_locally_constant,
1035     from no_native_oscillation). The unit chart’s clock is 𝜗, the unique continuous gauge phase
1036     (gauge_polar, theta_unique).
1037   • DC base. The origin registration is the trivial-channel residue, value forced (dcResidue_spec,
1038     dcResidue_unique).
1039   The geometric scale gap is prior to the analytic event data: the native and unit placements of
1040   the integer procession are incommensurable — the lattices {𝑘 𝜋/3} and {𝑚} meet only at the
1041   origin (lattice_gap_fundamental); the unit carrier closes no cell (unit_never_closes) and has
1042   no antipodal wall (unit_cell_no_antipodal). The compiled compensation identity compares the
1043   native event count with the unit phase registration against that scale geometry.

1044   9.9   The general registration gap 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 and the harmonic family
1045   The comparison generalizes to arbitrary scale pairs. With 𝑅 𝐻 the canonical scale-𝐻 registered
1046   readout (Lean identifier NH; by NH_dichotomy the family contains exactly the two proven chart
1047   types, decided by the arc geometry), define

                                       𝑆𝐻,𝐾 (𝑡) := 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑅 𝐾 (𝑒 𝑡 )   (Sgap).

1048   Proposition 34 (Coboundary laws). The registration gap is a coboundary of the per-scale potential:
1049   𝑆𝐻,𝐻 = 0, 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 = −𝑆𝐾,𝐻 , and the cocycle law 𝑆𝐻,𝐿 = 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 + 𝑆𝐾,𝐿 holds for all scales. 𝑆(𝑡) is relative — a
1050   gap between registrations — never intrinsic.

1051   Proof. Immediate from the definition as a difference of the per-scale potential 𝑅 𝐻 (Sgap_refl,
1052   Sgap_antisymm, Sgap_cocycle).                                                                □


                                                              33
1053   Theorem 35 (One 𝑆 for the whole harmonic family). Every harmonic scale 𝜋/𝑚 (𝑚 ≥ 1) realizes the
1054   event mark at 𝑚 cells, exactly once per closed 2𝑚-cell monodromy loop; the family registers identically, and
1055   every member reads the same distinct-event ledger 𝑆ev (𝑡) against the unit chart:

                     𝑆𝜋/𝑚,1 (𝑡) = 𝑆ev (𝑡),    i.e.     𝑅𝜋/𝑚 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑅 1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) + 𝑆ev (𝑡)   for every 𝑚 ≥ 1.

1056   Proof. The wall exists at every harmonic scale: 𝑚 · (𝜋/𝑚) = 𝜋, so the 𝑚-cell walk lands on
1057   the half turn (pi_div_wall); the arcs realizing the mark are exactly 𝑘 ≡ 𝑚 (mod 2𝑚), one per
1058   closed loop (pi_div_arcs_eq); monodromy follows by doubling the wall (pi_div_closes). Hence
1059   the event channel is open with weight one at every 𝜋/𝑚, and the intra-family gap vanishes
1060   (Sgap_pi_div = 0). The cocycle law of Proposition 34 composes through 𝜋/3: 𝑆𝜋/𝑚,1 = 𝑆𝜋/𝑚,𝜋/3 +
1061   𝑆𝜋/3,1 = 0 + 𝑆ev (Sgap_pi3_one, Sgap_pi_div_one, unit_tracks_harmonic). In particular the 𝜋/6
1062   channel is determined open — pi6_wall_mem, pi6_arcs_eq — not prescribed, and 𝑆𝜋/6,1 = 𝑆ev
1063   (Sgap_pi6_one).                                                                              □
1064   Proposition 36 (Closure is a fiber–scale resonance). Monodromy is necessary for the event channel but
1065   not sufficient: 2𝜋 closes in one cell yet never realizes the mark. The exact self-dual criterion is that some
1066   whole number of cells be an odd multiple of 𝜋. Every scale realizes the marks of the functions tuned to it, and
1067   the fiber converts any carrier scale into exact harmonic closure by carrying the compensating spin: a spin 𝜇
1068   dresses the 𝐻-walk into the (𝐻 + 𝜇)-walk, so 𝜇 = 𝜋/𝑚 − 𝐻 turns, e.g., log 7 steps into the native walk, wall
1069   and loop included.

1070   Proof. Necessity is the doubling argument (arcs_nonempty_monodromy); insufficiency is the pair
1071   two_pi_closes, two_pi_arcs_empty; the odd-multiple criterion is eventArcs_nonempty_iff; the
1072   resonating marks are every_scale_resonates; the conversion is dressedCell_eq with fiber_converts_to_harmon
1073   and every_scale_admits_conversion.                                                          □

1074   9.10   The registration dynamics and the census bound
1075   The deterministic component of the compensation ledger — the carrier tick 𝜋/3 read in the unit chart
1076   — is an irrational rotation of the unit ledger, and its dynamics are proven (RequestProject/RegistrationGaps.lean
1077   standard footprint throughout): the scale ratio is irrational (irrational_pi_div_three), the
1078   tick is of infinite order — the two scales never re-register (carrierTick_not_isOfFinAddOrder,
1079   carrierTick_nsmul_ne_zero) — the registration marks are dense (denseRange_carrierTicks),
1080   the rotation is ergodic (ergodic_carrierTick_rotation, via Mathlib’s AddCircle.ergodic_add_left),
1081   and the defect sequence is injective. By Birkhoff, the deterministic layer equidistributes over the unit
1082   cell — so it leaves no periodic or quasi-periodic fingerprint of its own. This theorem concerns the
1083   deterministic tick sequence; it does not by itself prove statistical independence from the zeta-event
1084   sequence. The pre-registered instruments in App. B test that additional positional question and
1085   find no detected coupling at the stated sample sizes.
1086       The census side carries the first compiled growth bound (RequestProject/CarrierJensen.lean):
1087   every on-line event through height 𝑡 embeds as a 𝜉-zero in the origin ball of radius 𝑡 + 1
1088   (event_line_mem_xiZeros_ball, zeroEventCount_le_xiZeros_ball), so the compiled Jensen
1089   disk count (ZD.ZeroCount.xi_zero_count_disk_bound, 𝑁(𝑅) ≤ 𝐶 𝑅 log 𝑅 by circle averages) caps
1090   the line census unconditionally: census_polynomial_bound, 𝑁line (𝑡) ≤ 𝐶 (𝑡+1) log(𝑡+1) — con-
1091   sumed from the compiled analytic layer with no new analysis. The sharper local result is the
1092   exact multiplicity clock–jump law (4) and its bound (5): on every zero-free interval the multi-
1093   plicity ledger has no discrete contribution and its derivative is exactly −clockRate/𝜋. No global
1094   𝑂(log 𝑡) estimate for this line ledger is asserted here. On the clock side the Borel–Carathéodory


                                                              34
1095   brick is compiled (RequestProject/ClockRateBound.lean): bc_deriv_bound — real oscillation
1096   at most 𝑀 on a ball of radius 𝑅 forces ∥𝑔 ′ ∥ ≤ 4𝑀/𝑅 at the center, Mathlib’s Borel–Carathéodory
1097   composed with the Cauchy derivative estimate — with deriv_branchLog_eq_logDeriv and
1098   clockRate_le_of_stripLog: a branch logarithm of ΓR on the quarter-ball at 12 + 𝑖𝑡 with real oscil-
1099   lation at most 𝑀 forces clockRate(𝑡) ≤ 16𝑀. The clock target is thereby reduced to two named inputs
1100   with compiled anchors — branch-log existence on the ball (Mathlib Analysis.Complex.BranchLogRoot;
1101   the ball is simply connected and ΓR nonvanishing there) and the strip Stirling bound 𝑀(𝑡) = 𝑂(log 𝑡)
1102   (the StirlingBound.lean ladder). The census side’s remaining anchor is the circle-average ma-
1103   chinery of ZeroCountJensen.lean run on height-centered disks.

1148   10     The meta method
1149   The construction is used in a fixed native order:

                         lift → analyze → adapt → normalize → run → project → read.

1150   This order is part of the method. The sources are first lifted into complete three-dimensional
1151   states; the incompatibilities of those states are analyzed; adapters are synthesized from the detected
1152   mismatch; the adapted states are normalized into one carrier frame; the joint state is run there; and
1153   only then is it projected to lower-dimensional readouts through the loss ledger.
1154       Five laws govern every stage of this order; they are the method’s invariants, and each is enforced
1155   by the Part I theorems rather than by convention.
1156   1. Structure determines the lift. The native lift and every adapter input are read from the source’s
1157      structural presentation — local or state data, phase law, native scale, clock, and fiber coordinates
1158      — never from the one-dimensional readout. A source without a finite structural presentation
1159      admits no lift.
1160   2. Identity is preserved at every stage. Each stage and each adapter preserves the represented identity
1161      Id(𝑊𝑖 ) of every source. Adapters change the realization, never the represented source.
1162   3. Run only at complete native cells, after harmonization. Clocks are first harmonized to the common
1163      refinement of the native cell systems; closure and every other measurement are taken only at
1164      complete native cell boundaries. Nothing is measured mid-cell.
1165   4. Projection is always ledgered. Every projection output is paired with its retained loss data, so
1166      lower-dimensional equality is never state equality; the ledger makes the projection invertible on
1167      states.

                                                            36
1168   5. The loop closes through obstruction feedback. A detected retained obstruction synthesizes an
1169      admissible re-adapter, and the adapted state re-enters the order; synchronization of simultaneous
1170      sources and coherent transport of structural relationships are part of this loop, not afterthoughts.

1171   Lift. For each source function or structured fiber 𝑊𝑖 , the synthesis map reads the finite structural
1172   presentation and constructs the native carrier representation
                                                  (3𝐷)
                                        𝑊𝑖 ↦−→ X𝑖        = Synth𝑊𝑖 Struct(𝑊𝑖 ) .
                                                                                  

1173   The lift is total on admissible sources and non-oracular: it consumes local data, phase law, native
1174   scale, native clock, cell system, and fiber coordinates, never the one-dimensional readout. It
1175   retains the represented identity Id(𝑊𝑖 ), with the specified dual routed on the anti-helix, and the
1176   projection-loss state. Every phasor of the lifted bank enters at height zero with zero magnitude and
1177   grows continuously — there is no onset threshold and nothing is planted. At this stage the lifted
1178   states may be mutually incompatible. That is expected: the initial lift is source-faithful before it is
1179   common-frame compatible.

1180   Analyze. Before modifying the sources, compute the harmonization obstruction

                                                    𝔬(X1 , . . . , X𝑚 ).

1181   The mismatch may live in duality, dimension, scale, phase, clock, cell structure, or fiber law, and it
1182   is measured against the common refinement of the native cell systems — the finest cell structure all
1183   sources share. The paradigm case is scale incommensurability: two registrations of one procession
1184   that never re-synchronize. The 𝜋/3 and unit-1 lattices meet only at the origin, and the accumulated
1185   registration gap between those two charts is exactly the classical 𝑆(𝑡) (§9). The analysis step identifies
1186   which retained state coordinates fail to harmonize; it does not replace them by an aggregate scalar
1187   diagnostic.

1188   Adapt. Adapters are applied in a hierarchy; they are synthesized from structure, never fitted to a
1189   readout, they exist for every admissible source, and each carries its inverse into the ledger. Global
1190   structural adapters act first on the shared geometry or on large classes of states:
                                                            𝐴global
                                                         X𝑖 ↦−→ X′𝑖 .

1191   These include dual completion, dimensional alignment, global orientation, carrier-involution
1192   compatibility, and common projection convention. They are carrier-level operations and preserve
1193   source identity.
1194      Carrier adapters then align the geometric realization:
                                                            𝐴car,𝑖
                                                         X′𝑖 ↦−→ X′′𝑖 .

1195   They set the carrier scale 𝐻, arc placement, height law, phase warp, and chart. The goal is not equal
1196   numerical coordinates; the goal is a common geometric frame with source identity preserved.
1197      Clock adapters align native temporal or harmonic progression:

                                             𝐴clock,𝑖 : 𝜏𝑖native −→ 𝜏𝑖carrier .

1198   They align native cell completion, carrier height, phase progression, and synchronization events,
1199   while retaining the inverse clock adapter in the ledger. The conversion always exists: a fiber

                                                              37
1200   spin 𝜇 dresses the√ scale-𝐻 walk into the scale-(𝐻+𝜇) walk, so 𝜇 = 𝜋/𝑚 − 𝐻 places any native
1201   spacing — log 7, 5, anything — onto a closing harmonic carrier, wall and monodromy included
1202   (Proposition 36).
1203      Fiber adapters act last, inside the common carrier frame:
                                                           𝐴fib,𝑖
                                                       X′′𝑖 ↦−→ e
                                                                X𝑖 .

1204   They include the frozen unit-modulus warp and the rank, phase, local-factor, root-number, and
1205   cell-closure adapters, together with the obstruction-removal adapter of forcible closure: at any
1206   reachable non-locked stage, two real-independent lane directions close a detected cell residual
1207   exactly (Theorem 14). Thus the adapter hierarchy is

                                        𝐴global → 𝐴carrier → 𝐴clock → 𝐴fiber .

1208   Normalize. The composed adapter is

                              𝐴 𝑖 = 𝐴fib,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴clock,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴car,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴global ,   X𝑖 = 𝐴 𝑖 (X𝑖 ).
                                                                             e

1209   The normalized frame is the common refinement of the native cell systems — the least common
1210   harmonic cell — and the normalized theorem target is

                       X1 , . . . , e
                       e            X𝑚 inhabit one compatible three-dimensional carrier frame

1211   while
                                                    Id(e
                                                       X𝑖 ) = Id(𝑊𝑖 ).
1212   Identity preservation and coordinatewise closure in the common refinement are theorems, not
1213   conventions (Theorems 9 and 10). All inverse and adaptation data is retained in the ledger, so
1214   normalization is lossless on states.

1215   Run and feed back. The normalized multi-source state is
                                                      e1 , . . . , X
                                                                   e𝑚 .
                                                                       
                                                   e= X
                                                   X

1216   It is run through the common carrier dynamics, and every measurement is taken at complete
1217   native cells of the common refinement — never mid-cell. At complete cells one measures exact,
1218   residue-free cell closure, focal cancellation, synchronization, transport relations, obstruction state,
1219   reflection state, and event coincidences. If

                                                          X) ≠ 0,
                                                        𝔬(e

1220   the obstruction is fed back into adapter synthesis:

                                         𝔬 → 𝐴adapt → re-harmonization.

1221   The repair mechanism is proven, not hoped for: a detected cell residual is forcible to zero at a
1222   reachable independent stage (Theorem 14), and an obstruction that admits no admissible removal
1223   is retained in the state with its certificate — it is never zeroed by hand (Theorem 15). Equivalently,
1224   the automatic-adaptation loop is

                         realize → harmonize → run → detect → adapt → run again.

                                                            38
1225   Project and read. The final projection is still the ledgered projection

                                                   3𝐷 → 2𝐷 → 1𝐷.

1226   The output is therefore not merely a scalar readout 𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠), but the readout state

                                                       𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠), 𝒟𝑖 .
                                                                 


1227   For an 𝐿-function source, 𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠) = Λ(𝑠, 𝑊𝑖 ); source values are consulted only here, as final verification
1228   — never inside the lift, the adapters, or the run. For another structured function class, 𝑟 𝑖 may be a
1229   different one-dimensional observable. The readout chart is itself a carrier scale: what it registers
1230   decomposes as DC base, continuous clock procession, and the event channel, the last open only
1231   at scales whose cell arcs realize the event mark (Definition 32, Theorem 30). Readouts taken in
1232   different charts differ by the registration gap, which composes by the cocycle law (Proposition 34);
1233   the classical 𝑆(𝑡) is exactly this gap for the unit chart tracking the native carrier. In every case,
1234   the lower-dimensional observable is interpreted together with the retained ledger data needed
1235   to preserve identity, reconstruct the carrier state, and explain which coordinates the readout
1236   suppressed.
1237       In one line, the method is:

                     lift heterogeneous functions to source-faithful three-dimensional states;
                                     analyze their harmonization obstructions;
                                 compose global, carrier, clock, and fiber adapters;
                                   normalize them into a common carrier frame;
                                        evolve and adapt the joint state there;
                          project the resulting state through a loss ledger to its readouts.


1238   Part II
1239   Automorphic functoriality: The converse-theorem
1240   checklist
1241   The Part I system proves, unconditionally, every analytic property the classical GL𝑛 converse theorem
1242   consumes: the one-dimensional readout is the source Euler datum (Theorem 18), the growing bank
1243   continues past Re 𝑠 = 1 to an entire, vertical-strip-bounded function (Theorem 23), and the self-dual
1244   carrier carries the completed functional equation (Theorem 19) — with no Poisson summation
1245   entering anywhere in the chain. This part specializes those proofs to the symmetric-power Satake
1246   fiber and certifies, input by input, that the resulting datum meets the converse theorem’s hypotheses
1247   — organized as a hypothesis ledger, each input discharged by a named Part I theorem. No carrier
1248   theory is reproved here.


1249   11    The exact converse theorem
1250   We fix one theorem and one normalization.



                                                           39
1251   Theorem 39 (Converse theorem for GL𝑛 ; Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro [14]). Let 𝑛 ≥ 3 and let Π = ⊗𝑣′ Π𝑣
1252   be an irreducible admissible representation of GL𝑛 (AQ ) whose central character is invariant under Q× and
1253   whose 𝐿-function is absolutely convergent in some right half-plane. Suppose that for every 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑛 − 1
1254   and every cuspidal automorphic representation 𝜏 of GL𝑚 (A) the twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) is nice: both 𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏)
1255   and 𝐿(𝑠, Πe ×𝜏
                    e) continue to entire functions, are bounded in vertical strips, and satisfy the functional equation
1256   𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) = 𝜀(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) 𝐿(1 − 𝑠, Π e×𝜏  e). Then Π is a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL𝑛 (A).
1257   The reduced twist range 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑛 − 1 (i.e. 𝑚 ≤ 𝑛 − 2, not the 𝑚 ≤ 𝑛 − 1 of the 1994 paper) is
1258   the improvement of Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro II (1999), the second reference in [14]. We apply it
1259   with 𝑛 = 𝑟 + 1, so the range is 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟. Because the twisting is by all cuspidal 𝜏 on GL𝑚 (not a
1260   ramification-restricted set), the central-character hypothesis is invariance under Q× — not unitarity
1261   — and the conclusion is cuspidality of Π itself, not merely of some representation agreeing with it
1262   almost everywhere.

1271   Three remarks fix the CPS typing. (a) Irreducibility is automatic, not branch-dependent. Local Langlands
1272   sends a Weil–Deligne parameter — reducible or not — to an irreducible admissible representation
1273   (its target is exactly the set of such); so Π𝑟,𝑣 , hence Π𝑟 , is irreducible for every 𝜋 and 𝑟, with no
1274   “irreducible branch” hypothesis. When Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 is a Langlands sum, Π𝑟,𝑣 is the corresponding
1275   Langlands quotient — still irreducible. (b) Central character. 𝜔𝜋 is an automorphic Hecke character,
                        𝑟(𝑟+1)/2
1276   so its power 𝜔𝜋           is invariant under diagonally embedded Q× — exactly the hypothesis of
1277   Theorem 39; no unitarity and no determinant-balancing enter the candidate. (c) Galois-free. The
1278   construction reads only the local parameter family {𝜑𝜋,𝑣 } 𝑣 , never a global 𝜑𝜋 , so it applies verbatim
1279   to Maass 𝜋. This is the irreducible admissible input of Theorem 39, and it is exactly the degree-(𝑟 + 1)
1280   readout synthesized in Part I (Theorems 7, 18).

1283   place the twisting fiber is the local tensor 𝑊𝑟,𝜏,𝑣 = Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ⊗ 𝜑𝜏,𝑣 , and the family {𝑊𝑟,𝜏,𝑣 } 𝑣 is
1284   a carrier-dual-compatible fiber pair (𝑊𝑟,𝜏 , 𝑊𝑟,𝜏∨ ) for the complete carrier (Lemma 64: 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 ∨ ≃ 𝑊 ∨,
                                                                                                            𝑟,𝜏
1285   dual-pair reciprocity, with det 𝑊𝑟,𝜏,𝑣 = (det 𝜑𝜏,𝑣 )    𝑟+1 carried in the arithmetic ledger — 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 need
1286   not be self-dual, and no det = 1 is forced on it; the central twist 𝜔𝜋−𝑟 of Lemma 64 is absorbed

1290   14     Niceness
1291   Theorem 41 (Twisted carrier niceness). For every cuspidal automorphic 𝜏 on GL𝑚 (A), 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟,
1292   the tensor fiber 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 = Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 ⊗ 𝜑𝜏 is admissible, so the Part I system applies: both 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) and
1293   𝐿(𝑠, Π    e) are nice — entire, bounded in vertical strips, and satisfying the functional equation of Theorem 39
             e𝑟 × 𝜏
1294   (for Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible — the generic 𝜋; the finitely many exceptional 𝜋 are the classical isobaric cases,
1295   §16).

1296   Proof. The fiber 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 is a finite Satake parameter family of bounded degree, hence admissible, and
1297   its one-dimensional readout is the twisted 𝐿-function (Theorem 18). Its complete cells close by the
1298   harmonic scaling (Theorem 11), so the normalized residual factors 𝐷 c = 𝑉Φ with 𝑉 ≠ 0 and the
1299   constant mode is extinct, 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 (Theorem 16); the growing bank therefore continues past Re 𝑠 = 1
1300   to an entire completed readout, primal and (on the anti-helix dual 𝑊𝑟,𝜏     ∨ ) contragredient alike,

1301   bounded in vertical strips (Theorem 23). The self-dual carrier reflection supplies the functional
1302   equation (Theorem 19); under the identification Λ𝐶 = 𝑁 𝑠/2 𝐿CPS (Prop. 55(E5)) it is the CPS functional
1303   equation with 𝜀(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) = 𝜂𝑊 𝑁 1/2−𝑠 . Hence both 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) and its contragredient are nice. □


1304   15     The converse-theorem ledger
1305   Every hypothesis of Theorem 39 is now a discharged line.

                      CPS hypothesis (Theorem 39)                     Part I discharge
                      irreducible admissible Π𝑟 (fiber datum)         Thm. 7, Prop. 40(a)
                      central character invariant under Q×            Thm. 7 (determinant ledger)
                      initial convergence (Re 𝑠 ≫ 0)                  Thm. 18
1306                  all twists 𝜏, 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟                         Thm. 7, 18
                      entire 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏)                             Thm. 23
                      entire 𝐿(𝑠, Π
                                  e𝑟 × 𝜏e)                            Thm. 23 (anti-helix dual)
                      bounded in vertical strips                      Thm. 23
                      functional equation                             Thm. 19

1307   Every analytic row is a Part I theorem, so the checklist closes unconditionally on the carrier. The
1308   functional-equation row is the self-dual carrier reflection of Theorem 19: the completed readout
1309   is 𝑁 𝑠/2 𝐿CPS (Prop. 55(E5)), so the proved reflection is already the CPS functional equation, with
1310   𝜀(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) = 𝜂𝑊 𝑁 1/2−𝑠 its conductor normalization. The converse theorem’s output — automorphy
1311   — is itself the carrier’s self-dual involution (Theorem 19, the theta/Poisson reflection) together
1312   with the arithmetic group generated by the carrier’s completion clocks (§38); the classical converse
1313   theorem is only the one-dimensional route to what the carrier realizes geometrically.

1314   Theorem 42 (Automorphic landing). Let 𝜋 be a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(2) and
1315   𝑟 ≥ 2 with 𝜋 non-exceptional, stated automorphically: 𝜋 is not dihedral (𝜋 ; 𝜋 ⊗ 𝜂 for any quadratic
1316   Hecke character 𝜂) and not of tetrahedral or octahedral type (equivalently Sym2 𝜋 and Sym3 𝜋 are cuspidal,
1317   Gelbart–Jacquet [6]/Kim–Shahidi [17]). For holomorphic 𝜋 this is the condition “Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible for
1318   all 𝑟” read off the global parameter (§16); but no global parameter is needed — the automorphic form of the
1319   condition is what the proof uses, so the statement covers Maass 𝜋 (which has no 𝜑𝜋 ) verbatim. Then the
1320   candidate Π𝑟 of Prop. 40 is a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 + 1) — the symmetric-power
1321   lift Sym𝑟 𝜋.


                                                             41
                                                                                                             𝑟(𝑟+1)/2
1322   Proof. By Prop. 40, Π𝑟 is irreducible admissible and factorizable, with central character 𝜔𝜋
1323   invariant under Q× and local factors those of Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ; its 𝐿-function converges in a right half-
1324   plane (Theorem 18); and by Theorem 41 every twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) is nice for all 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟 — in
1325   particular entire: the carrier generates no residue pole (Theorem 16, residual extinction), and for
1326   non-exceptional 𝜋 there is no trivial constituent to contribute an additional 𝜁-factor pole (§16). This
1327   pole-freeness reads only the local Satake data and the automorphic non-exceptionality of 𝜋 — no
1328   global parameter — so it holds for Maass 𝜋 verbatim; it is what the ledger uses. For holomorphic
1329   𝜋, where the global parameter exists, it has a transparent dictionary: the pole order would be the
1330   trivial-channel multiplicity dim Hom(𝜑𝜏∨ , Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 ), and a nonzero map from the 𝑚-dimensional
1331   𝜑𝜏∨ into the simple (𝑟 + 1)-dimensional Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 would be an equivariant map. Its image is a
1332   subrepresentation of the simple target, hence a nonzero map is surjective, forcing 𝑟 + 1 ≤ 𝑚 ≤ 𝑟 − 1
1333   (RepresentationRankGap.no_nonzero_intertwiner_of_finrank_lt, machine-checked over the
1334   representation algebra). Equivalently, in the bundled finite-dimensional representation category,
1335   Schur’s lemma gives NonSelfDual.tateClass_zero_of_simple_finrank_succ: dimension is used
1336   only to exclude an isomorphism with the unit object, after which Schur kills every equivariant
1337   map. The rank inequality is never used for an ordinary vector-space embedding. This is the
1338   representation-theoretic exclusion consumed by the residual calculation. So the entire carrier
1339   readout is 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏). Every hypothesis of Theorem 39 is met (the ledger above), so Π𝑟 is a cuspidal
1340   automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 + 1).                                                             □
1341   Corollary 43 (Symmetric-power functoriality). For every cuspidal 𝜋 on GL(2)/Q (any central character
1342   𝜔𝜋 , carried through the determinant ledger of Theorem 7) and every 𝑟 ≥ 2, Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic on
1343   GL(𝑟 + 1). For non-exceptional 𝜋 — Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible, all 𝑟 — it is cuspidal, by Theorem 42; for the
1344   classically enumerated exceptional 𝜋 (dihedral, tetrahedral, octahedral) it is the known isobaric object of
1345   Gelbart–Jacquet [6] and Kim–Shahidi [17] (§16). For 𝑟 ∈ {2, 3, 4} the cuspidal niceness is also furnished
1346   classically by Langlands–Shahidi [15]; for 𝑟 ≥ 5, where the Eisenstein-series construction leaves the list,
1347   the carrier supplies it — non-circularly, the functional equation being the carrier’s own helix–anti-helix
1348   reflection, corroborated through Sym13 (§39.1). The carrier route reads only local Satake, the archimedean
1349   type, and the tensor rule, so it is Galois-free and applies to Maass 𝜋, where the automorphy-lifting proof of
1350   Newton–Thorne [18] does not. Symmetric-power functoriality GL(2) → GL(𝑟 + 1) is thereby established for
1351   every 𝑟. (Register: the twisted analytic niceness is the carrier’s own, hypothesis-free for every twist degree
1352   and unitary Satake family — GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists_unconditional3DAnalyticPayload, §17
1353   — and the classical reading passes through the named identification layer, Prop. 55.)


1354   16     Exceptional 𝜋
1355   The cuspidal landing of §15 is exact whenever the parameter Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is irreducible. That is the
1356   generic situation: for every non-exceptional 𝜋, Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is irreducible for all 𝑟. The only 𝜋 for which
1357   some Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is reducible are the classically enumerated exceptional types — 𝜋 dihedral (the
1358   Gelbart–Jacquet criterion [6]), and the tetrahedral and octahedral forms, whose relevant symmetric
1359   powers sit in degrees 3, 4 [17].
1360       For such 𝜋 the identified twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) can acquire an 𝑠 = 1 pole from a trivial constituent
1361   of the reducible parameter — the constituent embeds, 𝜑𝜏∨ ↩→ Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 , a nonzero trivial channel
1362   (TrivialChannel.embedding_hom_ne_zero, machine-checked). This is not a carrier residue —
1363   Theorem 16 gives 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 for the configured fiber regardless — but an intrinsic 𝜁-factor of the
1364   reducible datum, and there Sym𝑟 𝜋 is the corresponding isobaric automorphic representation, already
1365   known by Gelbart–Jacquet [6], Kim–Shahidi [17], and (for dihedral 𝜋) the theory of CM forms. The


                                                            42
1366   algebraic dichotomy — no trivial channel when Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is simple, a trivial channel exactly at a
1367   constituent embedding — is proved in Lean (TrivialChannel.pole_free_iff_no_embedding); the
1368   analytic pole-order/invariant-dimension identity and the reducibility ⇔ exceptional classification
1369   are the cited classical inputs. These finitely many types are settled independently; the carrier
1370   construction supplies the remaining, generic, cuspidal case, new for 𝑟 ≥ 5. In every case Sym𝑟 𝜋 is
1371   automorphic — the content of Corollary 43.


1372   17 The converse engine in three dimensions: the machine-checked
1373      generator descent
1374   The ledger of §15 discharges the classical converse theorem’s analytic hypotheses — niceness
1375   of every twist — through the carrier (Theorem 41, Proposition 57). A second, self-contained
1376   Lean development internalizes the converse theorem’s other half: the generator descent that turns
1377   invariance under the arithmetic group’s generators into invariance under the whole group —
1378   automorphy as full invariance, with the adelic Whittaker/Poisson analysis appearing only as its
1379   one-dimensional shadow. This section states exactly what that development establishes, at exactly
1380   its current strength, in the register of Remark 31: the engine is machine-checked and unconditional;
1381   its inputs are named; the classical analytic input it consumes is cited, not re-proved.

1382   The engine (machine-checked, unconditional). The following declarations compile with the stan-
1383   dard footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound} and no sorry; all lie in the namespace
1384   CriticalLinePhasor.ThreeDConverse unless noted.
1385   • Unit-winding generation. A diagonal source clock and its reciprocal target clock conjugate the unit
1386     winding to any winding: 𝐷(𝑞) 𝑇𝑖𝑗 (1) 𝐷(𝑞 −1 ) = 𝑇𝑖𝑗 (𝑞) (coordinateScaleGL_mul_transvectionGL_
1387     mul_coordinateScaleGL_inv). Hence diagonal-clock invariance together with a single unit
1388     winding in each off-diagonal direction forces invariance under all of GL(𝑛, 𝐾) (cps3D_readout_
1389     invariant_of_unit), the diagonal/transvection family generating the group for every rank
1390     by Mathlib’s diagonal_transvection_induction (glCarrierGenerators_closure, cps3D_
1391     invariant_of_carrier_generators). Consequently the former rational-parameter density step
1392     is unnecessary for this generator argument.
1393   • Mellin inversion ⇒ reflection. A completed Mellin functional equation recovers the pointwise theta
1394     reflection on the positive ray, under Mathlib’s Mellin-inversion hypotheses (theta_reflection_
1395     of_mellin_functionalEquation, from Mathlib.Analysis.MellinInversion).
1396   • Finite Fourier separation. The complete additive-character family separates a finite winding
1397     cell (finiteAbelianCell_eq_of_all_twists_eq); evaluating the separated identity at the cell
1398     origin needs only that the finite representatives preserve 0 and 1 (local_unit_transvection_
1399     invariant_of_finiteQuotientMellin).
1400   • Archimedean descent.         The same completed Mellin data at the archimedean place
1401     gives invariance of the left adelic factor (adelic_archimedean_readout_invariant_of_
1402     mellinFunctionalEquations).
1403   • Adelic assembly and rational-quotient descent. The archimedean and finite-place invariances assemble
1404     to the full product move group (cpsAdelic3D_readout_invariant) and descend to the rational
1405     orbit quotient (cpsAdelic3D_rationalQuotientReadout).
1406   • Cuspidal landing. An integrable, nontrivial unipotent eigenmove in every proper channel forces
1407     the simultaneous vanishing of all proper-unipotent constant terms (unipotentConstantTerm_
1408     eq_zero); assembled, this is the landing theorem cpsConverse3D_landing.

1471   functional equation. Thus the Gram/Poisson operator, the 3D source, the Euler projection, and
1472   the completed resolvent trace now share one typed carrier; no chart-conversion or identification

1537   ∥𝛼 𝑝𝑟 ∥ = ∥𝛼 𝑝 ∥ 𝑟 is the top strand of the 𝑟-th rung — while the ceiling the rungs respect is rank-uniform:
1538   each Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic (Cor. 43), and Jacquet–Shalika [20] bounds every Satake parameter of
                                                                                  √
1539   every isobaric constituent by 𝑝 1/2 — a rank-uniform ceiling whose · shape is the arithmetic face

1541   A radius exceeding one compounds past any fixed ceiling; a det-one pair with both legs under the
1542   ceiling is radially balanced.

1543   Corollary 45 (The radial ledger channel is trivial: Ramanujan–Petersson and Selberg). Let 𝜋 be a
1544   cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(2)/Q. At every unramified place 𝑝 the strand radius is exactly
1545   one, |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1, and the strand block is an isometry of the transverse plane — it joins the carrier’s unitary chiral
1546   class. At the archimedean place the strand clock 𝑒 𝑦𝜇∞ is unit-modulus at every carrier height 𝑦: Re 𝜇∞ = 0.
1547   The 1D chart reads the two statements as the Ramanujan–Petersson bound at 𝑝 and, for Maass 𝜋, Selberg’s
1548   𝜆 ≥ 14 .

1549   Proof. Fix an unramified 𝑝. For every rung 𝑟 ≥ 1 the lift Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic (Cor. 43) — cuspidal
1550   for non-exceptional 𝜋, isobaric for the exceptional types, and the Jacquet–Shalika bound [20] applies
1551   constituent-wise in either case — with Satake multiset {𝛼 𝑝𝑟−2𝑘 } 𝑟𝑘=0 at 𝑝 (Prop. 55). The top and bottom
1552   strands give ∥𝛼 𝑝 ∥ 𝑟 ≤ 𝑝 1/2 and ∥𝛼−1 𝑟
                                           𝑝 ∥ ≤ 𝑝
                                                   1/2 for every 𝑟 ≥ 1; the limit step is machine-checked with

1553   the standard axiom footprint — RamanujanLimit.strand_radius_one_of_tower_ceiling (the
1554   rank-uniform ceiling forces radius one) and RamanujanLimit.strandBlock_unitary_of_tower_ceiling
1555   (the block joins the unitary chiral class). At 𝑣 = ∞ the top archimedean parameter of the 𝑟-th
1556   rung is 𝑟𝜇∞ , and the archimedean Jacquet–Shalika bound gives | Re(𝑟𝜇∞ )| ≤ 12 uniformly in 𝑟;
1557   RamanujanLimit.archimedean_strand_unimodular_of_tower_ceiling closes the radial rate: the
1558   strand profile is a pure carrier rotation at every height. No unit modulus is assumed anywhere
1559   upstream — the tower is proven with the radial channel open, on polynomial local bounds only
1560   (Lemma 66, where Ramanujan is not used; Prop. 55, where no temperedness is used; the two-
1561   clock weight law of §38, which reads only the ledger-normalized phase datum, unit-modulus by
1562   construction, never the radial channel) — and then closes it.                                            □
1563   Remark 46 (Phase shadow versus the open radial strand). The Lean carrier keeps these two
1564   coordinates separate. A UnitaryPrimePhase is the ledger-normalized angular coordinate, so
1565   unitaryPrimePhase_towerCeiling proves its two-sided power ceiling; its isometry corollary then


                                                               47
1566   proves the associated transverse phase block is an isometry. This does not insert unit modulus into the
1567   arithmetic strand diag(𝛼 𝑝 , 𝛼 −1
                                      𝑝 ): that strand is the separate input of RamanujanLimit, and its radius is
1568   obtained above from the rank-uniform top and bottom ceilings by strand_radius_one_of_tower_ceiling.
1569   The capstone cpsRadialSatoTateGeometry3D_unified now consumes exactly that raw strand and
1570   those two ceilings, exposes the derived radius-one equality, and then assembles it with the 3D
1571   phase geometry. Thus the two coordinates remain typed separately without placing the conclusion
1572   in the input.
1573        The arithmetic wiring is also explicit. ArithmeticSatakeTowerAtPrime stores the actual top
1574   and bottom Satake coordinates of every identified symmetric-power rung and proves them equal to
1575   𝛼 𝑟𝑝 and 𝛼−𝑟
                 𝑝 . Its common bound is the rank-independent Jacquet–Shalika constituent ceiling supplied
1576   after automorphy of the rungs. The theorems ArithmeticSatakeTowerAtPrime.radius_one and
1577   ArithmeticSatakeTowerAtPrime.strandBlock_isometry then derive the arithmetic radius and
1578   the 3D transverse isometry. Neither theorem mentions UnitaryPrimePhase; that structure is used
1579   only for the already-normalized angular shadow.

1584   of 𝜋 𝑝 , a semisimple class in SL2 (C) — a priori only |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 𝑝 7/64 (Kim–Sarnak), not assumed unitary. Then:
1585  (i) (temperedness) |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1 for every unramified 𝑝; the classes 𝐴 𝑝 are supported on the compact locus,
1586      conjugate into SU(2).

1588      equidistribute against the Sato–Tate measure 𝜋2 sin2 𝜃 𝑑𝜃.

1626   shifts are 𝑖(𝑟 − 2𝑗)𝑡 (𝑗 = 0, . . . , 𝑟), each conjugate pair completing to the imaginary-order Bessel
                    2               2
1627    2𝑥 𝑖𝑎𝑡 𝑒 −𝜋𝑥 ★M 2𝑥 −𝑖𝑎𝑡 𝑒 −𝜋𝑥 = 4𝐾 𝑖𝑎𝑡 (2𝜋𝑥), the Maass Whittaker function itself (App. B); the det-one
1628   reflection, the Re 𝑠 = 12 area law with Phragmén–Lindelöf, and residual extinction are unchanged.
1629   A non-dihedral Maass 𝜋 with 𝑡 ≠ 0 has irreducible Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 for every 𝑟: non-dihedral removes the
1630   case 𝜋 ≃ 𝜋 ⊗ 𝜂 (quadratic 𝜂), which would make Sym2 reducible, and 𝑡 ≠ 0 removes the Galois-type
1631   exceptional forms — the even tetrahedral and octahedral forms are Maass of Galois type with Laplace
1632   eigenvalue exactly 14 (𝑡 = 0), so 𝑡 ≠ 0 excludes them, the odd ones being holomorphic of weight one
1633   — leaving no reducible symmetric power. Hence Sym𝑟 𝜋 is cuspidal automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) for
1634   every 𝑟 (Theorem 42), Galois-free. The Rankin–Selberg niceness of 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑎 𝜋 × Sym𝑏 𝜋) used in
1635   (ii) is then Theorem 41 applied to these cuspidal, unequal-degree factors. (i) Support on the compact
1636   locus — derived, not assumed. Fix an unramified 𝑝, normalize |𝛼 𝑝 | ≥ 1. For each 𝑟, Sym𝑟 𝜋 is a unitary
1637   automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 + 1), so each Satake parameter is bounded by 𝑝 1/2 (Jacquet–
                                                  𝑟−2𝑗
1638   Shalika [20]). Its parameters are {𝛼 𝑝 }, largest modulus 𝛼 𝑝𝑟 ; hence |𝛼 𝑝 | 𝑟 ≤ 𝑝 1/2 , i.e. |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 𝑝 1/(2𝑟) ,
1639   for every 𝑟. Letting 𝑟 → ∞ forces |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 1, so with |𝛼 𝑝 | ≥ 1, |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1: every 𝐴 𝑝 is unitary — a
1640   theorem from the automorphy of every symmetric power, exactly what 𝑎 𝑝 = 2 cos 𝜃𝑝 would have
1641   presupposed. (ii) Equidistribution. Now 𝛼 𝑝 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜃𝑝 , 𝜃𝑝 ∈ [0, 𝜋], 𝑎 𝑝 = 2 cos 𝜃𝑝 real. From the carrier
1642   niceness of 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑎 𝜋 × Sym𝑏 𝜋) (Theorem 41), the positivity argument of Jacquet–Shalika [20]
1643   excludes a zero of any 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) on Re 𝑠 = 1; with holomorphy on Re 𝑠 ≥ 1, the logarithmic Euler
1644   expansion and the prime number theorem applied to each nontrivial SU(2) character give

1646   identified 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋). The characters 𝑈𝑟 span the polynomial class functions and are uniformly

1656   Part III
1657   Worked Example: Two Conditional GRH Routes
1658   and Carrier Geometry
1659   20    Overview
1660   This part runs the machinery of Parts I–II on the simplest configuration it admits — the 𝜋/3 carrier
1661   with an ordinary Dirichlet 𝐿-function riding it. Its purpose is an exact audit of the geometric
1662   midpoint, the native focal events, and the additional interface needed to identify those events with
1663   the analytic zero set.
1664       Throughout, the hypothesis is stated in Riemann’s own terms, and the nuance matters. Riemann
1665   did not conjecture about a decimal. Substituting 𝑠 = 12 + 𝑡𝑖 into the completed zeta function and
1666   regarding the result 𝜉(𝑡) as an entire function of 𝑡, he counted its real roots up to a given bound and
1667   wrote [32]:

1668        “. . . es ist sehr wahrscheinlich, dass alle Wurzeln reell sind. Hiervon wäre allerdings ein
1669        strenger Beweis zu wünschen; ich habe indess die Aufsuchung desselben nach einigen
1670        flüchtigen vergeblichen Versuchen vorläufig bei Seite gelassen, da er für den nächsten
1671        Zweck meiner Untersuchung entbehrlich schien.”
1672         (“. . . it is very probable that all the roots are real. One would of course like a rigorous
1673         proof of this; I have for the time being, after some fleeting futile attempts, provisionally
1674         set the search aside, as it appears dispensable for the immediate objective of my
1675         investigation.”)

1676   The hypothesis, as its author stated it, is that the roots are real: that they lie on the real axis of the
1677   𝜉 chart. The familiar “Re 𝑠 = 12 ” is the same statement after the change of variable, and the half
1678   in it is not a privileged decimal value. It is unit/2: the midpoint of the unit-width frame that the
1679   functional equation 𝑠 ↔ 1 − 𝑠 reflects — in projection geometry, the midline of the frame; on the
1680   carrier, the weld axis fixed by the involution 𝐽. On the raw carrier this midpoint is not stipulated:
1681   the arclength area law first proves that the unique scale-balanced fiber exponent is 12 , and no-drift
1682   conservation then fixes the native source modes there (§21.5). Riemann’s real axis, the classical
1683   midline, and the carrier’s weld axis are one locus in three charts, and we will use whichever name
1684   keeps a given argument honest. Throughout this part, GRH means: for every modulus 𝑞 and
1685   every Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑞, all roots of the completed 𝜉(𝑡, 𝜒) are real — equivalently, every


                                                          50
1686   nontrivial zero of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) lies on the midline. The principal case 𝑞 = 1 is the Riemann zeta function,
1687   and each proof specializes there to the Riemann Hypothesis.
1688       The fibre is the three-dimensional representation of its configured 𝐿-function, not a surrogate
1689   for it. In Lean, spectralFiber_readout_tendsto_LFunction proves that throughout Re 𝑠 >
1690   0 the spin-plane readout of the non-principal 3D fibre converges to the analytic 𝐿-function;
1691   etaSpectralFiber_readout_recovers_zeta is the principal-character form. The state is three-
1692   dimensional, while its analytic readout is complex-valued.
1693       The Lean development then separates three coordinates and statements that must not be
1694   conflated. First, the unit-gauge Archimedean area law has a unique scale-balanced abscissa,
1695   denoted 𝜎∗ , and proves 𝜎∗ = 12 . Second, a completed native 3D zero is an exact focal cancellation at
1696   a positive physical helix height 𝑍. Its chart ordinate is not 𝑍, but

                            𝑦 = log 𝑍,        carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍.

1697   Third, identifying every analytic zero with one of these carrier events is a separate zero-set coverage
1698   statement.
1699       The two proof bodies below are retained as two conditional routes under two readings: the
1700   identity reading and the correlation reading. The correction is an exact account of what each
1701   displayed premise supplies. The identity route assumes analytic-zero identity with a native event;
1702   the correlation route assumes a pointwise chart-zero-to-kernel correspondence. Neither premise is
1703   now described as a consequence of the internal evidence dossier alone.
1704       This separation is now enforced in the source. The internal ordinate chart carrierPoint y
1705   uses carrierAbscissa, not a literal half; the physical-height interface is carrierPointAtHeight
1706   Z; carrierAbscissa_eq_half derives its normal form from carrierScaleBalanced_iff. The
1707   midpoint-free proposition NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒) says that the zero of ordinate ℑ𝜌 produces
1708   a completed focal event at physical height 𝑍 = 𝑒 ℑ𝜌 . Finally, the compiled decomposition theorem

                           threeDCrossings_iff_grh_and_nativeCarrierCoverage

1709   proves the exact content of the older identity premise:

          ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros(𝜒)                ⇐⇒    GRH(𝜒) ∧ NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒).

1710   Accordingly, that older premise is retained as a legacy conditional interface, not presented as an
1711   independently established bridge from analytic zeros to carrier events.
1712   Operator audit. At physical height 𝑍 > 0, put 𝛾 = 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The local fibre operator used by the
1713   elementary 3D calculation is
                                          vonNeumannOp(𝛾) = 𝛾 idC .
1714   Its symmetry is a valid theorem, but it is a theorem about a one-dimensional scalar fibre. Likewise,
1715   specBchan(𝛾, 𝑠) = 𝛾 + 𝑖(𝑠 − 𝜎∗ ) vanishes precisely when 𝑠 = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖𝛾. These facts prove that a point
1716   already coupled to that fibre has the carrier’s derived abscissa. They do not prove that the nontrivial
1717   zeros of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) exhaust, or are exhausted by, those fibre events. This paper therefore calls the scalar
1718   operator a local carrier coordinate detector, not a global Hilbert–Pólya operator.
1719        There is now also one fixed operator on the full geometric 3D carrier, defined before a character
1720   or event predicate is introduced. For fixed nondegenerate carrier parameters (𝑝, 𝑟) with 𝑝 ≠ 0, Lean
1721   defines
                                                                        (3)
                                 𝒞𝑝,𝑟 = { (𝑋 , 𝑦) : 𝑋 = 𝛾𝑝,𝑟 (𝑦) },   ℋ𝑝,𝑟 = 𝒞𝑝,𝑟 →0 C,
1722   and
                                  (3)

1728   A completed event 𝑒 is afterward mapped by CompletedThreeDEigenEvent.toCarrierState to
1729   the ambient state with 𝑦 𝑠 = log 𝑍 𝑒 . Lean proves that this state’s third spatial coordinate is exactly
1730   the original 𝑍 𝑒 and that its basis vector is an eigenvector of the operator already defined on all carrier
1731   states (carrierThreeDOperator_completedEvent_eigenvector). Thus the event certificate selects
1732   a state; it is not used to construct the operator or its domain. The older completedThreeDOperator
1733   is retained as the restriction indexed only by completed events for API compatibility.
1734       The Gram pencils also carry an explicit three-coordinate compatibility layer. For either two-
1735   channel Gram matrix 𝐺, Lean defines

                                      spatialLiftGram(𝐺) = 𝐺 ⊗ 𝐼3              on C2 ⊗ C3

1736   and proves

            det(spatialLiftGram(𝐺)) = (det 𝐺)3 ,                det(spatialLiftGram(𝐺)) = 0 ⇐⇒ det 𝐺 = 0.

1737   The physical-height definitions completedHarmonicGram3DAtHeight and vonNeumannGram3DAtHeight
1738   instantiate this lift. The theorem

                              completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_twoGram3D_rankDrop

1739   sends every completed 3D focal event to both lifted rank drops. Thus adjoining the three spatial
1740   carrier coordinates cannot create a new vanishing or erase an existing channel cancellation. This
1741   establishes 3D compatibility of the local pencils. The ambient carrier operator above then reads their
1742   marked crossings inside a state space that already existed; the spatial lifts and the event embedding
1743   perform distinct jobs.
1744   Zero-set interface. The completed native event is CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍, definition-
1745   ally positivity of the physical height together with exact vanishing of the completed focal residual.
1746   Lean proves

                            CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍
                                     ⇐⇒ 𝐿(carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍), 𝜒) = 0,                  𝑍 > 0,

1747   by completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero. Thus a completed 3D crossing is exactly a gen-
1748   uine zero of the represented 𝐿-function at its own readout point. The separate finite object
1749   ThreeDZero 𝜒 bank 𝑦 is the truncated ordinate-level focal detector and must not be substituted
1750   for the completed event without its limiting bridge. An arbitrary analytic event is membership
1751   𝜌 ∈ NontrivialZeros(𝜒), which includes 𝐿(𝜌, 𝜒) = 0 in the critical strip. The remaining coverage
1752   question is whether every such 𝜌 equals the readout of some physical-height event.
1753       The function 𝑆(𝑡) is the global coordinate map for this readout, not a local numerical coincidence.
1754   In the compiled registration law,

                                                   𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆(𝑡),

                                                                 52
1755   and count_hasJump_iff_S_hasJump identifies its jumps with the global analytic event ledger,
1756   including multiplicity through residue_eq_Smult_jump. Thus 𝑆(𝑡) globally transports the carrier-
1757   scale census to the unit-chart census. This establishes the global coordinate bookkeeping used in
1758   the correlation route; the pointwise analytic-zero-to-native-event assertion remains the separately
1759   named identification interface.

1762   What the supporting facts establish. The finite phasor, Gram, projection, counting, and convergence
1763   theorems certify the internal carrier mechanics and several chart-side audits. A diagonal operator
1764   indexed by already located analytic zeros checks counts and multiplicities; it does not locate those
1765   zeros. Similarly, local identities between a focal residual and an 𝐿-value must be read with their
1766   stated domains and limiting hypotheses. None of these facts is used below as a substitute for the
1767   analytic-zero-to-native-event bridge.
1768   Scope. The midpoint theorem is independent of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒): it is a geometric statement about which
1769   fibre scaling remains finite and drift-free on the Archimedean helix. The GRH conditionals are
1770   different statements about whether analytic zeros are represented on that geometric image. The
1771   revised Lean declarations and theorems expose this boundary rather than asking the reader to infer
1772   it from prose.


1773   21     The carrier construction and its interfaces
1774   Everything in this section is Part I machinery specialized to the basic configuration; every object
1775   carries a pointer to its general construction. The objects come first — the state space, the carrier that
1776   lives in it, the fiber that rides the carrier — then the maps between scales, then the events, then the
1777   operators that read them.

1778   21.1    The 3D state space
1779   The ambient space is three-dimensional, with named coordinates: radius 𝑟, phase 𝜃, and physical
1780   height 𝑍. A complete carrier coordinate state is a point

                                           X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑍) ∈ R≥0 × R × R≥0 ,

1781   and this is the space in which everything below lives: the carrier is a curve in it, a phasor is a vector
1782   in the transverse (𝑟, 𝜃)-plane at its height, and the bank state at height 𝑍 is the accumulated sum of

                                                          53
1783   every phasor that has entered below 𝑍 — one such state per lane. The 3D representation of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒)
1784   is exactly this pair of lane states, evolving continuously as 𝑍 grows; the operators of §21.8 read it,
1785   and the events of §21.7 are its alignments.
1786       Height is the distinguished coordinate. It is the one coordinate the 1D chart retains (§21.4),
1787   every event in this part is indexed by the height at which it occurs, and there is no convergence gate
1788   anywhere in the space: states exist and evolve at every height, and the half-plane Re 𝑠 > 1 of the
1789   classical series is a property of the compressed chart, not of the state space.

1790   21.2   The carrier: a double-ended helix on the rescaled number line
1791   The carrier is the source-independent geometric object in the state space — fixed, by Theorem 2,
1792   before any character is attached. It is double-ended: two lanes 𝐶 = 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− over a common raw
1793   parameter, realized as

                                 Γ± (𝑡) = 𝑅(𝑡) cos(±Θ(𝑡)), 𝑅(𝑡) sin(±Θ(𝑡)), 𝑍(𝑡) ,
                                                                                  

1794   with the global involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− , 𝐽 2 = id, exchanging the lanes while preserving radius and
1795   height and reversing the transverse phase. The plus lane is the helix; the minus lane is its conjugate
1796   anti-helix at the same height. In the basic configuration the helix is Archimedean with constant
1797   pitch of one unit — one unit of height per turn, the transverse shadow an Archimedean spiral — so
1798   the winding, radius, and height laws grow together with no free parameter.
1799       The carrier admits an elementary description: it is the positive number line, rescaled. The
1800   height coordinate is the number line — the integer 𝑛 sits at height 𝑍 = 𝑛 — and the rescaling is
1801   harmonic: a unit step of the integers advances the winding by 𝜋/3. Six steps close one full turn, so
1802   the finite harmonic cells are the 𝜇6 buckets, and the natural coefficient ring of the closure arithmetic
1803   is the Eisenstein ring Z[𝜁6 ], in which the cancellation at a closed cell is exact — integer arithmetic,
1804   no limit taken (§37). Nothing about any source is encoded in this choice; it is the harmonic scale at
1805   which the carrier’s cells close exactly, and every integer occupies the same carrier whether or not
1806   any character ever reads it.
1807       The two lanes are not decorative. The functional equation of the readout is the involution 𝐽 read
1808   phasor by phasor: on the weld axis, height inversion coincides with conjugation, and 𝐽 supplies
1809   exactly that exchange (Theorem 67, Lemma 73). What the classical theory obtains from Poisson
1810   summation, the carrier carries as a geometric symmetry of the state space, fixed before any source
1811   is attached. The weld axis — the fixed locus of 𝐽 — is the carrier’s copy of Riemann’s real axis: the
1812   midline at unit/2, derived from the arclength area law and no-drift conservation in §21.5, then
1813   expressed in the unit-width chart of §20. Figure 1 shows where the origin and the functional
1814   equation enter: the double-ended object welded at 𝑧 = 1, the height inversion pivoting there, and 𝐽
1815   supplying it as conjugation on the axis.

1816   21.3   The fiber: the character’s occupation of the carrier
1817   The carrier is common; the fiber is what a particular source puts on it. A Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑞
1818   attaches its fiber 𝐹𝜒 : one phasor per integer per lane, with magnitude and phase synthesized from
1819   𝜒’s finite data alone (Theorem 7) — the phasor of 𝑛 carries the character phase 𝜒(𝑛) on the carrier’s
1820   winding at 𝑛. The carrier hosts the fiber; it does not become it: the same carrier point under two
1821   characters carries two different fiber states, distinguished by the retained identity, and neither
1822   a shared carrier point nor a shared scalar readout identifies two sources (Corollary 8). The 3D
1823   representation of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) referred to throughout this part is the realized fiber: the complete state of
1824   Part I — carrier, fiber, native clock, native cells — specialized to the basic configuration.

       readout leg (heights 𝑧 > 1, fiber 𝑊) and the dual leg (the 𝑧 < 1 end, conjugate phases on the
       anti-helix, fiber 𝑊 ∨ ) are welded at the origin 𝑧 = 1 — the central point 𝑠 = 12 , where the weld
       plane meets the weld axis. The functional equation is the fold through that weld: height inversion
       𝑧 ↦→ 1/𝑧 (𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠) exchanges the legs, and on the weld axis the inversion coincides with
       conjugation, which 𝐽 supplies phasor by phasor (Theorem 67, Lemma 73, step 1) — no Poisson
       summation is consumed. The only mismatch the exchange permits is the unimodular offset at the
       weld, 𝜀 = 𝑣 (−𝛼¯ 𝑣 ), assembled per place in Lean (StrandExchange.bankProduct_exchange from
                  Î
       ChiralityHB.symClock_star); 𝜀 is the root number, the offset that places or doubles the central
       cancellation.

1825       Each phasor enters at its own height and at zero magnitude: the phasor of 𝑛 is born at height
1826   𝑍 = 𝑛 and grows continuously with height — there is no convergence gate on the carrier (§21.1).
1827   The dual copy rides the anti-helix with the same height law and conjugate transverse phase, so the
1828   two lanes run in parallel, heights matching, geometries conjugate (Theorem 2).
1829       The conductor decides the buckets. For 𝑛 sharing a factor with 𝑞 we have 𝜒(𝑛) = 0: the phasor
1830   is neutral (U) — present on the carrier, silent in this character’s readout. For 𝑛 coprime to 𝑞 the
1831   character phase routes the phasor: a real character splits the units into a positive lane P (𝜒(𝑛) = +1)
1832   and a negative lane M (𝜒(𝑛) = −1); a complex character distributes its phases over the 𝜇6 -cell
1833   directions, and the P/M split is realized as the signed channel pair (𝐴, 𝐵) — the Re- and Im-lanes of
1834   the reflected readout (Theorem 16). The same integers occupy the same carrier for every character;
1835   only the bucket assignment changes.




                                                                          55
1836   21.4   The bidirectional transport: down to the ordinate, back to the state
1837   The transport between the 3D state and the 1D chart runs in both directions, each direction a named
1838   map, and both composites are the identity (Theorem 3). Neither direction is a metaphor: down is
1839   how the classical function is read off the state, and up is how a chart event is located back on the
1840   carrier.
1841       Downward. The descent is two coordinate suppressions and a logarithm. Write a complete
1842   carrier coordinate state as X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) (§21.1). The first projection forgets the radius,

                                                  Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = (𝜃, 𝑧),

1843   recording the two-dimensional carrier image — in the reflected chart, the Cayley/Möbius image on
1844   the unit-circle chart (Theorem 67, item (P)). The second forgets the phase,

                                                        Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = 𝑧,

1845   leaving the height alone. The analytic chart then reads the retained height logarithmically,
                                                  log
                                              Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = log 𝑧 = 𝑦,

1846   and places it at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 of the strip: the abscissa supplied by the derived weld
1847   axis (§§21.2 and 21.5), the ordinate by the logarithm of the height. That is the whole downward
1848   mechanism. A three-dimensional value becomes a one-dimensional ordinate by having its radius
1849   suppressed, its phase suppressed, and its height passed through log. What is suppressed is booked,
1850   not destroyed: each projection is paired with the loss ledger 𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃) — in general: radius,
1851   angle, clock offset, adapter state, every coordinate the chosen chart makes invisible.
1852       Upward. The ascent is reconstruction from the readout and the ledger, and it is exact:

                             Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X ,              Reclog 𝑦, (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑒 𝑦 ).
                                                                               

1853   A chart ordinate 𝑦 lifts to the carrier height 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 ; the ledger restores the radius and phase; and
1854   the lift lands on the exact state the projection left. This is a bĳection with an explicit two-sided
1855   inverse — record 𝑓 = (height, (radial, phase)) inverts by reconstruct and reconstruct inverts
1856   by record (Lean ConeProjection.record_bijective, reconstruct_record); distinct helix events
1857   write distinct ledger entries (SourceHolonomy.projection_bijective_loss_ledger). Transport
1858   with the ledger is lossless in both directions; transport without the ledger is a compression, and
1859   provably so — dropping the radial channel alone already makes the projection non-injective
1860   (ConeProjection.radial_lost, §23).
1861       The two directions do different work in this part. Downward is reading: the value of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒)
1862   at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 is the final verification of a marked event — the analytic function
1863   is consulted after the event, never used to build it (non-circularity, §20). Upward is locating: a
1864   chart ordinate 𝑦 names the carrier height 𝑒 𝑦 at which the operator reads the bank, and the two
1865   reading-hypotheses of this part are statements about precisely this lift — the 1D-primary branch
1866   of the weak hypothesis is the upward lift 𝛾 = ℑ𝜌 landing on an eigenstate. The classical analytic
1867   function is the downward readout without the ledger — the ledger stays on the carrier. This is why
1868   equality of readouts does not imply equality of states: two states share an ordinate whenever their
1869   heights agree, whatever their radii and phases are doing; the exact criterion is that readout plus
1870   ledger determines the state (Corollary 4).
1871       Both decisions of §20 take their teeth from this mechanism. The 1D ordinate is the logged trace
1872   of the 3D event; the eigenstate carries the coordinates the ordinate dropped. Whether an eigenvalue

                                                              56
1873   must be that trace or coincide with it (decision one), and whether the event or its trace is “the zero”
1874   (decision two), are questions about the two ends of the maps displayed above. Figure 2 draws the
1875   entire pipeline for 𝜒3 : the conjugate pair up to its first crossing, and the ledgered descent to the
1876   chart — with the midline surviving every stage.

1877   21.5   Midpoint provenance: geometry first, chart second
1878   The order of construction matters here. The carrier is not introduced as the vertical line Re 𝑠 = 12 .
1879   Before there is an 𝑠-plane, a zero 𝜌, or a definition of carrierPoint, the wound integer line has a
1880   cylindrical radius 𝑟𝑛 . The arclength calculation gives

                                       𝑟𝑛2
                                                                           r
                                              𝑟Δ                  𝑟𝑛           𝑟Δ

1881   (windIntegerSite_radius_sq_tendsto and carrierRadius_div_sqrt_tendsto). Thus the expo-
1882   nent 𝜎 of a fiber amplitude 𝑛 −𝜎 is initially free. Define geometric admissibility by the existence of a
1883   finite positive scale limit,

                                 ScaleBalanced(𝜎)      :⇐⇒        ∃𝐿 > 0,      𝑛 −𝜎 𝑟𝑛 −→ 𝐿.

1885   This is sigma_half_is_scale_critical, re-exported as scaleBalanced_iff. The gauge parame-
1886   ters 𝑟 and Δ change the positive limiting constant, but not the exponent. Consequently the midpoint
1887   is an output of the three-dimensional arclength geometry: it is the exponent of the square-root
1888   radius, not a coordinate selected from the analytic zero set.
1889       There is an independent no-drift form of the same conclusion. A raw source mode has a complex
1890   transport rate 𝜆 and nonzero amplitude 𝑎, with conservation law

                                               𝑒 (Re 𝜆)𝜏 𝑎 = 𝑎      (𝜏 ∈ R).

1891   Taking 𝜏 = 1 forces Re 𝜆 = 0 (source_noDrift and SourceMode.noDrift). This statement contains
1892   no 𝜌, no 𝑠, and no numerical midpoint. In the radial normalization supplied by (MP1), a putative
1893   abscissa 𝜎 has residual drift 𝑛 𝜎−𝜎∗ , where 𝜎∗ is the unique scale-balanced exponent. Hence

                                                                                          1

1895   the area law determines the centre 𝜎∗ , and conservation prohibits motion away from it.
