1899   Here carrierAbscissa is selected from the unique witness of CarrierScaleBalanced; only the
1900   theorem carrierAbscissa_eq_half rewrites it to 12 . The theorem carrierPoint_eq_half_add_I is
1901   therefore a downstream normal-form lemma, not the definition of the carrier coordinate. Theorems
1902   carrierPointAtHeight_im and carrierPointAtHeight_exp certify 𝑦 = log 𝑍 and 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 in both
1903   directions.
1904       The completed native crossing is

                     CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍            :⇐⇒      𝑍 > 0 ∧ Dcell 𝜒 𝑍 = 0.

1905   The exact representation theorem gives

                         CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍 ⇐⇒ 𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0.

1906   The finite declaration ThreeDZero remains the truncated ordinate-level focal closure used by the
1907   finite pencil proofs.
1908       Two exclusion theorems make the image statement exact. First, not_scaleBalanced_of_ne says
1909   that an abscissa different from 𝜎∗ is not a native carrier state. Second, helix_no_offline_cancellation
1910   says that an off-circle Cayley ledger entry cannot be produced by a weld-fixed helix event, while
1911   projection_bijective_loss_ledger says that the height-to-ledger map is injective on the carrier
1912   image. Projection can therefore neither move a native cancellation away from the midpoint nor
1913   merge two carrier events into a counterfeit cancellation. An off-midpoint analytic vanishing, if
1914   presented to this 3D representation, has no scale-balanced, drift-free carrier source.
1915       This also separates the exact logical role of ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros. Its clause
1916   𝜌 = carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) is the coverage/identification assertion that a classical analytic zero
1917   belongs to the carrier image. It is not the derivation of that image’s real coordinate: (MP1)–(MP2)
1918   and the exclusion theorems have already done that without quantifying over analytic zeros. Once
1919   coverage is granted, taking real parts is of course immediate; the substantive interface question is
1920   whether every analytic zero is represented by a native focal event. The paper will use carrierPoint
1921   only in this downstream, normal-form sense. Lean makes the separation executable by defining the
1922   midpoint-free statement NativeCarrierCoverage and proving

              ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros(𝜒) ↔ GRH(𝜒) ∧ NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒).

1923   Consequently the legacy equality premise is not cited as evidence for the coverage direction; an
1924   unconditional closure must discharge the midpoint-free coverage proposition (or the fixed-operator
1925   spectral-capture interface) directly.

1926   21.6   The chart: 𝑦 = log 𝑍 and 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦
1927   The readout just constructed does not live at the carrier’s scale. The identity between the scales is one
1928   equation read in both directions: downward, the chart ordinate is the logarithm of the carrier height,
1929   𝑦 = log 𝑍; upward, the carrier height is the exponential of the chart ordinate, 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 . A carrier
1930   state at height 𝑍 > 0 is read at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 (HarmonicPencilCell.reprPoint); the
1931   phasor of the integer 𝑛, born at height 𝑛, is charted at ordinate log 𝑛. The compression this induces
1932   is the single most important fact about the relation between the two representations. At the first
1933   zero of 𝜁, the chart reads 𝑦 = 14.1347 . . .; the carrier height is 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 ≈ 1.38 × 106 , and the realized
1934   bank below that height already holds about 1.38 million integer phasors per lane. In general the
1935   chart ordinate 𝑦 summarizes a bank of ⌊𝑒 𝑦 ⌋ phasors in one complex number. The 1D representation
1936   is not a smaller copy of the 3D representation; it is a logarithmically compressed summary of the
1937   same function, and the scale mismatch between the two charts is itself a theorem-level object (§9).

                                                           59
1938       The abscissa tells the same story from the other side. The carrier’s arclength law first derives
1939   the unique scale-balanced exponent 𝜎∗ = 12 , and conservation then fixes every native mode at zero
1940   radial drift (§21.5). Riemann’s substitution 𝑠 = 12 + 𝑡𝑖 is the analytic chart of that derived weld axis,
1941   and the represented point 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 𝑦 = 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 simply reads height along it. The ordinate compresses
1942   by a logarithm while the abscissa is pinned by a geometric scale law and its no-drift conservation —
1943   which is why every subsequent argument in this part is an argument about heights. The midline
1944   has already been located before the chart is defined.

1945   21.7   Vanishing is focal alignment
1946   A zero, on the carrier, is not a value creeping down to nothing; it is an alignment event. At
1947   a marked height the accumulated bank achieves exact harmonic cancellation: the P and M
1948   lanes balance, the 𝜇6 cells close in Z[𝜁 6 ], and the residual carries no independent constant
1949   mode — the normalized cell residual factors as det(𝐿c )/𝐴 = (𝜆 − 𝜇)𝐵 with 𝜆 − 𝜇 ≠ 0, so the
1950   residual vanishes exactly when the signed closure channel does (Theorem 16). The event is
1951   registered by rank at both exact levels. At physical helix height 𝑍 > 0, with logarithmic ordinate
1952   𝑦 = log 𝑍, the canonical finite bank closes exactly iff its spatially lifted harmonic Gram matrix
1953   drops rank (threeDZeroAtHeight_twoGram3D_rankDrop). This finite event is the truncated detector
1954   ThreeDZeroAtHeight. The completed fibre event is CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight; Lean proves

                       CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍            ⇐⇒      𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0

1955   by completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero. The theorem

                           completedHarmonicGram3DAtHeight_rankDrop_iff_L_zero

1956   proves directly that its completed spatial harmonic Gram lift drops rank exactly at that represented
1957   𝐿-zero. Thus the 3D crossing is focal cancellation in the completed 𝐿-function fibre at physical
1958   height 𝑍; it is not inferred from a 1D chart criterion. The finite bank theorem is retained as its
1959   internal truncation-level detector and is not substituted for the completed identity.
1960   Note (Frobenius determinant one). The conjugate eigenstate pair the alignment realizes is not free to
1961   sit anywhere; it is pinned by an algebraic constraint. On the carrier the local Frobenius acts as a simil-
1962   itude of determinant one: its chiral block has det = 1 (RequestProject/FrobeniusSimilitude.lean,
1963   frobeniusBlock_det_one), so its two eigenvalues multiply to one — a reciprocal pair {𝛼, 𝛼−1 }.
1964   With the class unitary they lie on the unit circle as a conjugate pair {𝑒 𝑖𝜃 , 𝑒 −𝑖𝜃 }, and the eigenphases
1965   ±𝜃 are real: the algebraic reason the eigenstate pair is symmetric about the weld axis rather
1966   than drifting off it. This is the carrier’s realization of the classical unit-circle normalization of the
1967   Satake–Frobenius class; on the analytic side it is Deligne’s purity, which places the normalized
1968   Frobenius eigenvalues on the unit circle [13], with the trivial similitude factor det = 1 keeping
1969   them a conjugate pair. The one setting where this mechanism is already a completed theorem is
1970   the function-field analog: Weil’s Riemann hypothesis for curves over a finite field F𝑞 is precisely
1971   the statement that the Frobenius eigenvalues on the Jacobian have absolute value 𝑞 1/2 and pair
1972   as {𝛼, 𝑞/𝛼}, which after normalization sit as conjugate pairs {𝛽, 𝛽−1 } of determinant one on the
1973   unit circle — forcing the zeros of the congruence zeta function onto Re 𝑠 = 12 [12]; Deligne’s
1974   proof of the Weil conjectures extends this purity to smooth projective varieties of every dimension
1975   [13]. There the Frobenius is the operator whose spectrum pins the zeros to the critical line, and
1976   determinant-one unitarity is the entire content of that conclusion — the carrier’s det = 1 block is
1977   the local, archimedean shadow of the same mechanism. We claim the analog, not the classical case:


                                                           60
1978   the finite-field statement is an unconditional theorem, the classical one is not, and importing the
1979   former as a proof of the latter is exactly the elision this part refuses. The determinant-one fact is a
1980   structural property of the representation, proven on the carrier; it does not by itself adjudicate the
1981   naming decisions of §20 — it fixes where the paired eigenphases live, not which of (Z-3D)/(Z-1D)
1982   names the zero.

1983   21.8   The two Gram operators
1984   Two operators read the bank, and they divide the labor.                        𝐴 𝐵 
1985        The Gram harmonic pencil is the finite detector: the 2 × 2 pencil 𝐿c = 𝜇𝐴     𝜆𝐵 on the signed
1986   channels, whose determinant vanishes — whose rank drops — exactly at the alignment events
1987   (§21.7). It is the instrument that marks native focal-event heights on the carrier.
1988        The local von Neumann fibre is the coordinate-reading object. At each physical 3D height 𝑍 > 0,
1989   its spectral parameter is the logarithmic ordinate 𝛾 = 𝑦 = log 𝑍, and it is multiplication by log 𝑍 on
1990   the one-dimensional fibre,

                                         vonNeumannOp(log 𝑍) = (log 𝑍 : C) · id,

1991   symmetric — hence self-adjoint, with real spectrum {log 𝑍} — as a theorem, not an assumption
1992   (vonNeumannOp_isSymmetric, RequestProject/ClosedForm.lean). The spectral parametrization
1993   sends a real eigenvalue 𝜇 to the represented point 𝜎∗ + 𝑖𝜇 = 12 + 𝑖𝜇, where 𝜎∗ has already been fixed
1994   by (MP1).
1995        Because a separate scalar operator is supplied for each 𝛾, this family is not itself the one fixed
1996   operator required by the global Hilbert–Pólya interface. Its exact role is to verify the local kernel
1997   and the reality of an already supplied height.
1998        The family is assembled, without changing any local proof, by the fixed ambient carrier operator
         (3)
1999   𝐴 𝑝,𝑟 above. Its basis is indexed by all geometric states 𝑋 = 𝛾𝑝,𝑟 (𝑦), independently of crossings, and
        (3)
2000   𝐴 𝑝,𝑟 𝛿 𝑋 = 𝑦𝛿 𝑋 . A completed 3D crossing 𝑒 = (𝑍 𝑒 , ℎ 𝑒 ) selects the state 𝑋𝑒 = 𝛾𝑝,𝑟 (log 𝑍 𝑒 ) and Lean
2001   proves that its physical third coordinate is 𝑍 𝑒 . Hence a “3D eigenvector” in the ambient resolvent
2002   statements below means this explicit carrier basis state, while vonNeumannOp(log 𝑍 𝑒 ) computes its
2003   local one-dimensional resolvent factor.

2030   21.9    The chart-side registration audit
2031   One further object appears in the evidence dossiers and deserves an exact label. Over a finite
2032   window (0, 𝑇], the Lean development builds a diagonal matrix on the window’s zero-events —
2033   hpOperator 𝑇, one axis per unit of multiplicity, eigenvalue the event ordinate. Its name is historical;
2034   its role is not spectral detection. It is a finite repackaging of the already-located analytic zero window, used
2035   for exactly one thing: auditing the chart against the carrier, count and multiplicity. The audit facts
2036   are proven and exact — the diagonal is Hermitian by type (hpOperator_isHermitian); every index
2037   is an exact vanishing (eigenheight_is_exact_vanishing); the chart reads zero at a height iff an
2038   index sits there (chartZero_iff_eigenheight); the diagonal’s dimension is the chart’s own count
2039   formula 1 + 𝜃(𝑇)/𝜋 + 𝑆mult (𝑇) (hpDimension_eq_registration); the eigenspace dimension at an
2040   event equals the vanishing order — the mode space is a graded local algebra C[𝑋]/((𝑋 − line 𝛾)ord )
2041   (finrank_modeSpace), a double zero a two-dimensional crossing; and the window traces are hon-
2042   est analytic objects (gradedResolventTrace_eq_residue_sum, windowedDiffResolvent_tendsto).
2043   But because the window is indexed by already-located analytic zeros, nothing in this subsection
2044   participates in locating an event. The local von Neumann fibre of §21.8 likewise verifies an event
2045   after its height is supplied. The fixed global operator interface is stated separately below.

2046   21.10    The Hilbert–Pólya setup we use
2047   The classical suggestion runs: exhibit a self-adjoint operator whose spectrum gives the ordinates
2048   of the nontrivial zeros; self-adjointness forces the spectrum real; real ordinates place the zeros on
2049   the midline. It is worth saying plainly that this is not an exotic reformulation: Riemann’s own
2050   sentence — alle Wurzeln reell — already asks for a real spectrum, and real spectrum is precisely
2051   what self-adjointness delivers. The Hilbert–Pólya suggestion is Riemann’s phrasing transposed into
2052   operator language, which is why we treat it as the natural frame for the worked example rather
2053   than as one strategy among many.

                                                              62
2054       The present development has three operator levels, and they must be kept separate. The proved
2055   scalar fibre vonNeumannOp(𝛾) = 𝛾 idC is a local detector attached after a real height 𝛾 is supplied. Its
2056   symmetry and kernel equation certify the coordinate of that already marked event; they do not by
                                                                                           (3)
2057   themselves provide one operator whose spectrum is the event set. The fixed 𝐴 𝜒 supplies the next
2058   level: one symmetric operator on all completed 3D crossing states of 𝜒, with explicit eigenvectors and
2059   the two resolvent traces above. Because its index is the completed-event subtype, it is a valid spectral
2060   realization of the 3D event ontology, not a discovery theorem for analytic zeros not yet coupled to
2061   that ontology. The final analytic-coverage interface is grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture:
2062   one fixed self-adjoint element 𝑎 must be accompanied by a resolvent-trace identification proving
2063   that every analytic pole parameter lies in spectrum(𝑎). Self-adjointness then supplies spectral reality.
                                                                                       (3)
2064   The carrier and chart theorems below now provide the concrete candidate 𝐴 𝜒 and its event traces;
2065   applying the final interface to every analytic zero still requires the coverage/trace identification
2066   rather than only the diagonal assembly.


2067   22    The theorems
2068   The formal home of this part is RequestProject/HelixResolventCapture.lean together with the
2069   supporting files named below; every statement carries axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound},
2070   no sorry, no axiom, built in-tree (App. B). Below, GRH(𝜒) abbreviates the formal statement “every
2071   nontrivial zero of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) lies on the midline” (GRHSpectral.GRH), stated for every modulus 𝑁 and
2072   every Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑁. The reading-hypotheses and both GRH implications are proven
2073   at that generality. The trivial character is the instantiation that lands Mathlib’s RiemannHypothesis
2074   — the mod-1 𝐿-function is riemannZeta — and a reading adopted at every modulus yields
2075   GRHSpectral.GRHComplete, the conjecture itself: every Dirichlet 𝐿-function, every modulus, every
2076   character, principal included.

2140   “nontrivial zero” is definitionally the analytic object. The revised source records the minimal
2141   dependency of each older interface:


                                                      64
2142   • ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros (3D-Zero-Real; the strong reading with the 3D zero pri-
2143     mary): every nontrivial zero 𝜌 is represented by a completed fibre crossing at a physical 3D height
2144     𝑍 > 0, with 𝜌 = carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍. The two spatially lifted Gram pencils

2151     junction. Its right branch is only the analytic zero equation together with 𝛾 = ℑ𝜌, so

2153     pling is OneDCorrelationEvidence, which asserts a scalar-fibre kernel at that analytic zero and
2154     therefore implies the critical-line conclusion by itself.
2155   These audits do not alter either conditional theorem. They state which premise actually supplies the
2156   conclusion and prevent the geometric midpoint theorems, the internal rank-drop correspondence,
2157   and the analytic zero-set identification from being presented as one result.
2158       The coordinate convention in both interfaces is fixed: 𝑍 > 0 is physical height on the Archimedean
2159   helix, 𝑦 = log 𝑍 is the analytic ordinate, and 𝑆(𝑡) is the global carrier-to-chart coordinate/registration
2160   map. The pointwise fibre readout and the global census map therefore have distinct typed roles.


2161   23    Evidence I: the 3D–1D correlation
2162   The eighteen facts of oneDChartEvidence, each proven unconditionally, form a chart-side registra-
2163   tion dossier. They establish count, jump, residue, multiplicity, and projection identities on the objects
2164   appearing in their statements. The universal layer is the 𝑆(𝑡) global coordinate map: it transports the
2165   carrier-scale census to the unit-chart census and registers every analytic event jump. A global census
2166   identity is not by itself a pointwise bĳection between ThreeDZero and arbitrary Dirichlet 𝐿-zeros.
2167   The separate, character-indexed input OneDCorrelationEvidence(𝜒) is the operative pointwise
2168   chart-to-kernel leg. Three of the facts below are named engines: Shannon — the collapse loses
2169   radius and angle to the ledger but never counterfeits (record_bijective); the Shannon Cascade —
2170   an accumulation of stage features is a feature of the limit (limit_zero_of_stage_accumulation);
2171   and Riemann’s Fold — the projection pipeline, crossing dimensions, lands on the real axis exactly
2172   when its retained coordinate does (pipeline_midpoint_iff).
2173   • chartZero_iff_eigenheight (RequestProject/HilbertPolya.lean). For 0 < 𝛾 ≤ 𝑇: 𝜁( 12 +
2174     𝑖𝛾) = 0 ⇐⇒ 𝛾 is an index of the zero-window diagonal (chart-side audit, §21.9). The one-for-one
2175     coincidence, proven — not asserted — window by window.
2176   • hpDimension_eq_registration (RequestProject/HilbertPolya.lean). The window diago-
2177     nal’s dimension is the chart’s own count formula, 1 + 𝜃(𝑇)/𝜋 + 𝑆mult (𝑇). The index count and the
2178     zero count are the same number because the ledger says so.
2179   • carrier_scale_compensation_S (RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean). 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 )−
2180     𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆(𝑡): the classical 𝑆(𝑡) is the gap between the native-scale event count and the unit-scale
2181     smooth term — one procession, two registrations, no mysterious remainder.
2182   • native_identification′ (RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean). 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) equals

2186   • count_hasJump_iff_S_hasJump (RequestProject/ResidueJump.lean). The event count and 𝑆

2203     sor’s radius depends only on Re 𝑠 = 21 , not on height: the height→circle map is a faithful

2220     dowed differenced-resolvent trace converges as 𝑇 → ∞ to an absolutely convergent limit: the
2221     chart-side resolvent is an honest analytic object, unconditionally.


2222   24    Evidence II: internal three-dimensional carrier facts
2223   The sixteen facts of threeDRealEvidence are each proven unconditionally, but their conjunction is
2224   an internal-support dossier, not a theorem identifying every analytic zero with a ThreeDZero. The
2225   facts concern local scalar-fibre symmetry, finite carrier cancellation, completed critical-line readouts,
2226   chart-indexed registration objects, arithmetic winding, and general limit principles. Their scopes are
2227   recorded individually below. Three named engines organize the dossier: Feynman’s Quiver — the
2228   crossings are prime-generated by unique factorization, the phasor bank is summable, the heights


                                                          66
2229   are distinct, and no focus splits; Deligne’s Pairs — the self-reciprocal det-one local pairing, purity at

2231   limit holds no feature the stages lack.

2268     nite: no nonzero state is null, so vanishing is a property of readings, never of states — a zero
2269     cannot hide as a degenerate state.

2301   Proof A. Adopt (Z-3D): “nontrivial zero” names the crossing — the focal-alignment event of §21.7.
2302   Two logically distinct facts are then composed. First, before this adoption, the arclength area law
2303   and conservative transport have proved that the native, scale-balanced carrier image is exactly
2304   {𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍 : 𝑍 > 0}, equivalently {𝜎∗ + 𝑖 𝑦 : 𝑦 ∈ R}, with 𝜎∗ = 12 , and that its ledger cannot encode
2305   an off-image cancellation (§21.5). Second, (Z-3D) supplies the coverage/identity clause that each
2306   classical nontrivial zero is one of those native focal events. This second clause is the explicitly
2307   displayed hypothesis in (ii); it is not used in the derivation of 𝜎∗ .
2308       For each covered event at physical height 𝑍, the two spatial Gram theorems provide the harmonic
2309   and von Neumann rank drops at the same ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The fibre operator is self-adjoint
2310   by theorem (vonNeumannOp_isSymmetric), and the represented coordinate is the already derived
2311   𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍. Hence taking real parts gives Re 𝜌 = 𝜎∗ = 12 . With the evidence of §24 — exact vanishing
2312   at the eigenheights, multiplicity equal to order, no split focus, definite metric, exhaustion of the
2313   real ray — theorem (ii) closes GRH(𝜒) under the stated coverage hypothesis; (iii) and (iv) are its
2314   all-modulus and trivial-character specializations.

2318   event. This augments the retained proof; it does not replace its displayed coverage hypothesis. □

2358   27     Riemann Hypothesis corollaries at 𝜒 = 1
2359   The mod-1 𝐿-function is riemannZeta, so at the trivial character each conditional implication lands

2361   Corollary 51 (RH, identity reading). ThreeDRealEvidence∧ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros(𝜒1 )

2369   28     Conclusion
2370   The corrected dependency structure has three levels. First, Archimedean helix geometry de-
2371   rives the unique scale-balanced, drift-free carrier abscissa; Lean constructs carrierPoint from
2372   that abscissa, proves its half-unit normal form afterward, and reads physical height through
2373   carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = carrierPoint(log 𝑍). Second, the finite harmonic pencil detects
2374   truncated focal cancellation exactly, the completed harmonic pencil detects the completed 𝐿-fibre
                                                                                                           (3)
2375   cancellation, and the local scalar fibre verifies its ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The fixed operator 𝐴 𝜒
2376   then assembles all completed crossings into one symmetric event-state space with explicit basis
2377   eigenvectors. Third, identifying the analytic zero set with those native events requires a pointwise
2378   coverage or spectral-capture theorem.
2379       The global 𝑆(𝑡) coordinate map supplies exact census, jump, residue, and multiplicity registration
2380   between carrier and chart scales. The proved supporting facts include the two explicit completed-
2381   event resolvent versions: 3D zeros with 3D eigenvectors, and 1D zero readouts with the same
2382   3D zeros and 3D eigenvectors. The legacy identity conditional and correlation conditional also
2383   remain valid deductions, with their proofs retained above; the new Lean audit states exactly which
2384   premise contains the critical-line conclusion in each route. An analytic Hilbert–Pólya completion
                                   (3)
2385   can now target the fixed 𝐴 𝜒 : it must prove the analytic resolvent/spectral capture required by
2386   grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture, or instantiate that interface with another fixed operator.
                                                                                                    (3)
2387   The scalar family 𝛾 idC is correctly used as the local diagonal-mode calculator, while 𝐴 𝜒 is the
2388   assembled 3D event-space operator.




                                                         70
2389   Part IV
2390   Beyond Endoscopy - Altuğ Analysis and Repair
2391   29    The obstruction: Altuğ’s uniformity problem
2392   The framework began not as an alternative to functoriality but as a root-cause analysis of one failure:
2393   the loss of productivity in the direct Beyond-Endoscopy route [1] above the symmetric square.
2394   The obstruction turned out to be an emergent clock; once that clock is separated the higher-order
2395   analysis becomes compositional, and the transport interface the rest of the paper builds is extracted
2396   from the structure that composition consumes.
2397       Altuğ’s execution of Beyond Endoscopy for GL(2) [2, 3, 4] reduces the standard-representation
2398   trace to an archimedean analysis whose primary difficulty is a uniformity problem: the asymptotic
2399   expansions of the Fourier transforms of the orbital integrals must hold with implied constants
2400   independent of every parameter — the 𝐶, 𝐷-independence Altuğ calls “the central issue,” the
2401   content of his long technical appendix (Altuğ II, Appendix A), which secures the power saving
                                31/32+𝜀 ) isolating the standard representation (Altuğ III, Thm 1.1). A second
          𝑛<𝑋 tr 𝑇𝑘 (𝑛) = 𝑂(𝑋
       Í
2402

2403   difficulty sits beyond it: Poisson summation on the 𝑛-sum “works well for the standard represen-
2404   tation and the symmetric square, however stops being productive for higher symmetric powers”
2405   (Altuğ III, fn. 5, after Sarnak [7]; the two productive cases are Venkatesh’s [5]). To our knowledge no
2406   one had instrumented these sums numerically; the field’s own diagnosis is that the direct analysis
2407   “does not scale to higher rank.” Our first reading mis-located the difficulty at the cutoff’s edges — it
2408   is not there.
2409   The estimate that costs Altuğ roughly sixty pages reduces, in the exact gauge, to a single magnitude
2410   bound. The transform (11) whose 𝐶, 𝐷-uniformity is Altuğ’s “central issue” is bounded, with
2411   no oscillation estimate, by the triangle inequality in the coordinate that makes the integrand real
2412   (Lemma 83); the sharp expansion (Theorem 84) and the full uniform bound (Proposition 86) then
2413   follow, every uniform constant being one application of that one bound. The analysis is deferred to
2414   Appendix A; here we turn to what made it look hard.


2415   30    The oscillation is the orbital transform’s own comb
2416   Why did Prop. 86 look hard? The oscillation the estimate must survive is deterministic. The
2417   numerical scan is made in the clock coordinate

                                𝜈clock := 2𝜈𝐽 ,       𝑒(−𝑦𝜈𝐽 /2𝑙 𝑓 2 ) = 𝑒(−𝑦𝜈clock /4𝑙 𝑓 2 ),

2418   where 𝜈𝐽 is the transform frequency in Prop. 86. The measured clock is extracted from the full
2419   complex profile 𝑉(𝜈clock ) by fitting the log-power modulation log |𝑉(𝜈clock )| 2 to a smooth envelope
2420   plus the first two harmonics sharing one fundamental, not by averaging dip gaps. Over the cutoff
2421   support 𝑦 ∈ [ 𝑋4 , 5𝑋
                           4 ] this gives

                           Δ𝜈clock = 0.524 (𝑙 𝑓 2 )1.03 (𝑋/8)−1.04 (1 + 𝜉)0.00 ,      𝑅2 = 1.000,

2422   equivalently half that spacing in the 𝜈𝐽 coordinate. In the one-parameter window-span normalization
2423   𝜅eff := 4𝑙 𝑓 2 /(𝑋Δ𝜈clock ) the cells give 𝜅eff = 0.943 ± 0.025 (range 0.895–0.971), while the harmonic-
2424   truncation audit has median period shift 2.4 × 10−4 , so the residual spread is not a dip-localization
2425   artifact. With the same Chebyshev multiplier 𝑈𝑟 (𝑥) used for the symmetric-power rank, the

                                                              71
2426   event-bearing 𝜉 ≠ 0 cells keep the same law through the tested range 0 ≤ 𝑟 ≤ 13 after separating
2427   the continuous clock from deep-event visibility: every rank has 𝑅 2 = 1.000, 𝑙 𝑓 2 -exponent 1.03–1.04,
2428   and 𝑋-exponent −1.04–−1.03 on the cells passing the clock-quality gate. Thus the older scalar
2429   𝜅 ≈ 0.94 is the mean of a slightly drifting clock, and the observed high-rank loss is productivity
2430   decay: deep-event cells thin from 10/12 at 𝑟 = 0 to 3/9 and 3/8 at 𝑟 = 11, 12, while the surviving
2431   clock cells still obey the same law. Thus the scalable object is not the raw list of deep dips but the
2432   cell-indexed phase clock together with a separate productivity ledger: the clock law survives in
2433   cells where the visible deep comb has already thinned, so higher rank must be tested by clock-cell
2434   census and productive cell yield as distinct observables.
2435        This oscillation is intrinsic to the orbital transform Ψ = 𝐼 𝑙, 𝑓 (𝜉, 𝑦), not the cutoff’s edges. Two
2436   controls settle it: replacing the compact cutoff 𝐺(𝑦/𝑋) by a smooth edgeless window leaves the
2437   comb unchanged, and tapering the 𝑥 = ±1 endpoints of the 𝑥-integral leaves it unchanged as well
2438   (height_warp_test.py) — so neither the height-cutoff edges nor the integral endpoints produce it.
2439   It is the 𝜉-Fourier oscillation of the orbital content: at 𝜉 = 0 the 𝑥-integrand is unimodal (𝑃2 /𝑃1 = 0)
2440   with no comb, while 𝜉 ≠ 0 switches on the transform’s own oscillation, the window fixing only its
2441   𝜈-spacing (Δ𝜈 ∝ 1/𝑋). It is therefore a deterministic feature of the content, not a removable chart
2442   artifact of the cutoff; but it is deterministic, which is exactly what the exact gauge of §A discharges —
2443   the magnitude bound survives it whatever its source, with no estimate of it.
2444        The clock is necessary but not sufficient: the repair is the clock configurator plus two adapters. Identifying
2445   the transport frequency is the first ingredient, not the fix — the clock alone does not close the
2446   crossings. Exact closure of the carrier readout, across the symmetric-power ladder and up the
2447   GL tower, is the clock configurator — which reads the deterministic transport frequency and sets
2448   the period, phase, and scale the rest inherit — together with two carrier adapters it keys. The
2449   carrier dwell re-registers the values a projected sum skips — the native, exact form of Altuğ’s Σ()
2450   missing-lattice-point correction — and closes the crossing exactly where the skip displaces it. The
2451   phasor delay adapter, derived from the clock, retards the faster-spinning higher-weight channels so
2452   the crossing sharpens rather than smears, restoring the reopening exponent toward its simple-zero
2453   value. The clock configurator supplies the period; these two supply registration and spin. The
2454   repair is the clock configurator + carrier dwell + phasor delay, not the clock alone; the suite is
2455   catalogued as an operational unit in §40.


2456   31     The repair: a lossless method that scales
2457   The method the rest of the paper builds — a clock, then carrier scaling, a frozen warp, and ledgered
2458   projection — has a clean, precision-testable form on the carrier’s own bank, the object of the cell-closure
2459   algebra of §38 (CellClosure). We report that worked example here: on the bank, the four operations
2460   drive the native cell residual to a precision-limited zero, uniformly across the symmetric-power rank
2461   census, the residual tracking working precision — an identity, not a model floor.
            Scope (read this first). This experiment is run on the carrier bank 𝐵𝑟 (𝑘) = 𝑗 𝑒 𝑖(𝑟−2𝑗)𝜃𝑘 with the
                                                                                          Í

2464   that machinery (the approximate functional equation, the trace Poisson summation, the orbital
2465   transform Ψ(𝑦) = 𝐼 𝑙, 𝑓 (𝜉, 𝑦), or the Proposition 5.2 object). Its purpose is narrow and honest: to
2466   isolate and stress-test the closure mechanism at controlled high precision, with each operation ablated.
2467   The bridge — that the measured 𝜈-clock of Altuğ’s transform (§30) is the clock that generates this warp
2468   and closes the actual transform’s cell — is asserted structurally and not demonstrated here; building
2469   it (the measured clock feeding the carrier warp) is the explicit open experiment. Falsifiability
2470   register: a measured Altuğ clock that failed to generate the closing warp would disconfirm this

2491   The cuspidal +warp residual is ∼ 10−29 , 10−48 , 10−79 at 30, 50, 80 digits: it tracks precision, where a
2492   model floor would be digit-independent. Every ablation floors — the scalar readout (raw/clock),
2493   scaling without the warp, and the no-projection scalar warp all plateau at 𝑂(1)–𝑂(100) — so both
2494   the projection and the warp are load-bearing.
2495       What it is, and is not. The harmonic fiber (𝜃 a rational multiple of 𝜋) is already root-of-unity and
2496   closes at every stage except the scalar clock column, where collapsing to a single dominant frequency
2497   aliases even it to 𝑂(30); +scale re-closes it (the 10−𝑝 entries). There the DC ledger correctly books
2498   the genuine Sym𝑟 reducibility (three trivial constituents at 𝑟 = 8, 10 for 𝜃 = 𝜋/3) — the same trivial
2499   channels that return as the exceptional cases of Part III. The content is the cuspidal row: the irrational
2500   Satake phase does not close raw (the +scale column floors), but the frozen unit-modulus warp
2501   harmonizes it to the compatible cell, where it closes exactly. This is not a claim that the cuspidal
2502   𝐿-function’s own coefficients sum to zero; it is the exact, lossless, precision-tracking closure of the
2503   harmonized fiber — “the fiber engages its own warp” (§40) made an identity, uniform across rank
2504   because the carrier scale 𝑀 is refined (6 → 12 → 48 → 96) to keep every channel resolved. This
2505   is the shape of the whole paper: Part II builds the machinery this example runs on (the carrier,
2506   the loss ledger, the warp dictionary), and Part III lands the classical functoriality; the reducibility
2507   booked in the ledger here is the same object that becomes the exceptional locus there.
2508       Fixed results: the carrier closes every object to precision; the degradation lives only in the 1D projection.
2509   The repair of §30 is measured. Two readings of the same object must be separated: the carrier (its
2510   vector representation, the four-stage above) and the scalar 𝐿-function readout (the 1D projection). In

                                                                  73
2511   the carrier, every object — including genuine multi-parameter ones — closes to a precision-limited
2512   zero, tracking working precision; the degradation is a feature of the projection, not of the object:

2514          The standard-representation channel Altuğ can only bound to 𝑜(𝑋) (magnitude ∼ 0.5) has
2515   signed sum at the machine floor — the odd-clock antisymmetry dual−𝜉 = −dual𝜉 makes the 𝜉 ≠ 0
2516   contribution vanish exactly (dual_closure_test.py). The dwell closes the crossing that skipping
2517   the missing lattice points displaces (a 3400× contrast, the native Σ(), skip_insert_closure.py).
2518   The decisive rows are the last two carrier entries: the genuine two-parameter GL(4) Rankin–Selberg
2519   𝐿(Δ × 𝐸11 ) (two independent Satake angles, built from scratch, not a functorial Sym𝑟 ) degrades in
2520   the scalar readout to 𝑘 = 0.47 — and a scalar de-chirp cannot repair it, a one-parameter correction
2521   against two independent angles — yet its carrier bank closes to 4.9 × 10−91 at 90 digits, an identity
2522   that tracks precision (gl4_rankin.py). The control isolates the mechanism: the self-dual GL(3) row
2523   is Sym2 of a genuine Maass form (the level-one even form 𝑅 = 13.7797, our own Hejhal eigenvalues
2524   𝑎 1 , . . . , 𝑎 20000 , tempered to |𝑎 𝑝 | < 2, the Sato–Tate-open regime — not synthesized from Δ), and
2525   because it carries a single Satake angle its scalar readout stays clean (𝑘 = 1.01, no degradation) while
2526   the vector likewise closes to 4.2 × 10−91 (gl3_maass_selfdual.py). So the wall is parameter count,
2527   not degree: a degree-three one-parameter object reads faithfully in 1D, a degree-four two-parameter
2528   object does not — the scalar readout is a rank-one projection, exact for one independent angle and
2529   lossy for two. Genuine GL therefore has no wall in the carrier: the smearing of the multi-parameter
2530   crossings is a property of the 1D scalar projection, which the channel-resolved vector representation
2531   does not share. By Gelbart–Jacquet a self-dual cuspidal GL(3) is a Sym2 , so it is necessarily one-
2532   parameter; the sharpest test of the carrier is therefore a non-self-dual GL(3), which no Sym2 supplies.
2533   Take the degree-three complex Artin representation 𝜌 of the Frobenius group 𝐹21 = 𝐶7 ⋊ 𝐶3 (7T4),
2534   field 𝑥 7 − 14𝑥 5 + 56𝑥 3 − 56𝑥 + 22; its local Satake bank at an√order-seven Frobenius is the three
2535   roots of unity {𝜁7 , 𝜁27 , 𝜁 47 } (trace the Gauss period 𝜂 = (−1 + −7)/2) or its conjugate {𝜁37 , 𝜁57 , 𝜁 67 }
                                 √
2536   (trace 𝜂′ = (−1 − −7)/2), neither set closed under conjugation, so 𝜌 ; 𝜌∨ . The object is genuinely
2537   non-abelian: 𝑝 = 13 and 𝑝 = 41 are both ≡ 6 (mod 7) yet fall in different classes (𝜂′ vs. 𝜂), so no
2538   congruence recovers the trace (the classes were resolved exactly by the Frobenius substitution in
2539   the degree-21 splitting field). This is precisely where the scalar readout must fail categorically
2540   rather than merely smear: Re 𝜂 = Re 𝜂′ = − 12 , so a real one-dimensional readout — a function of
2541   the trace’s real part — gives the two Frobenius classes the same value and cannot separate 7𝐴 from
2542   7𝐵, erasing the non-abelian bit. The complex multi-rail bank keeps them apart and closes exactly:
2543   over the natural 𝜁7 clock the non-DC rails of both classes sum to machine zero, tracking 4.3 × 10−62
       at 60 digits, with rails = 𝜁1+2+4              = 1 (so SL(3): two independent rails carry the degree-three
                                   Î
2544
                                               7
2545   bank) and no DC/pole rail present, while the order-three and split fibres carry exactly one and
2546   three DC rails — the constant-mode/pole content, cleanly separated (f21_gl3_multirail.py).
2547   The cell closure of both classes, the determinant, the Gauss-period relations 𝜂 + 𝜂′ = −1, 𝜂𝜂′ = 2
2548   and 𝜂 ≠ 𝜂′, and the scalar obstruction itself (Re 𝜂 = Re 𝜂′ while 𝜂 ≠ 𝜂′) are machine-checked in
2549   Lean (F21NonSelfDual.lean). So the non-self-dual case, where a scalar representation is provably
2550   impossible, rides the multi-rail carrier without loss.

       The symmetric-power kernel is modulated by 𝑈𝑟 (cos 𝜃) = 𝑟𝑗=0 𝑒 𝑖(𝑟−2𝑗)𝜃 , carrying a zero-frequency

2562   Part V
2563   Universal Transport
2564   33    Toward Universal Transport
2565   The preceding sections close the analytic core — the uniformity (§A), the emergent clock (§30),
2566   and the productivity boundary. The remainder of the paper develops the carrier transport toward
2567   symmetric-power functoriality: the carrier/fiber rescaling that sends a pole to a closed cell (§34),
2568   the arithmetic transparency of the symmetric-power transfer (§35), and a detection identity closed
2569   on a genuine transfer (§36).


2570   34    The carrier/fiber rescaling: a pole becomes a closed cell
2571   Place the integers on a carrier scaled by 𝜋/3, i.e. attach the cell phase 𝑒 𝑖𝑛𝜋/3 (the 𝜇6 /𝜁 6 step).
2572   We distinguish two operations on the carrier throughout. A rescaling is a fixed constant — here
2573   𝜋/3, or another 𝜇𝑚 step — that lifts a unit-1 carrier into one with harmonic cells; it establishes
2574   the native cell structure (and is the reason we never work at unit scale). A warp is a function, a
2575   continuously-evolving deterministic output 𝜔(·) that rides the already-rescaled carrier and adapts
2576   to the fiber — the 𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) of the warped-Abel summation (§37) and the tunable FE clock (§40).
2577   Rescaling sets the cell; warping moves within it. The pole of 𝜁 at 𝑠 = 1 lives in the divergence of
         1/𝑛; on the (rescaled) carrier it closes,
       Í

                                                         = − log 1 − 𝑒 𝑖𝜋/3 =      ,
                                                                          
                                                   𝑛                             3
                                             𝑛≥1

2579   a finite 𝜇6 value: the divergence has become a closed-cell reading. For a Dirichlet character 𝜒 of
2580   conductor 𝑞, the appropriate fiber scale (trivial → 𝜋/6, 𝜒3 → 𝜋/3, 𝜒4 → 𝜋/2) makes carrier and
2581   fiber compatible harmonics. The character 𝜒3 is the aligned archetype: its conductor 3 is the Eisenstein
2582   conductor — the sixth roots of unity of Z[𝜁3 ] = Z[𝜁6 ] — so the 𝜋/3 = 𝜇6 rescaling coincides with
2583   the 𝐿-function’s own conductor symmetry, the carrier cell is the fiber’s native cell, and closure needs

2592   𝑆(𝑡) term is recovered as the scale-registration correction in the scalar receiver chart (§9). This is the
2593   reading used in §36.


2594   35    Symmetric-power transfer: arithmetic transparency
2595   For Sym𝑟 transfer GL(2) → GL(𝑟 + 1) (𝑟 = 2𝑚 even), the transfer sends an elliptic class of Satake
2596   angle 𝜃 to the class of angles {2𝑘𝜃 : |𝑘| ≤ 𝑚} ∪ {0} —i.e. Sym𝑟 of the Frobenius block, with the
2597   fixed eigenvalue 1 = 𝛼𝛽 the det-one of the block. The symmetric-power transfer is arithmetically
2598   transparent, as follows.
2599       Arithmetic transparency. The transferred characteristic polynomial is reducible (𝑥 − 1 divides it),
2600   and each quadratic factor 𝑥 2 − 2 cos(2𝑘𝜃)𝑥 + 1 has discriminant −4 sin2 (2𝑘𝜃). The clock identity
2601   sin(2𝑘𝜃) = sin 𝜃 𝑈2𝑘−1 (cos 𝜃) (with sin2 𝜃 = |𝐷|/4𝑛, 𝐷 = 𝑡 2 − 4𝑛) gives

                                            disc 𝑘   𝑈2𝑘−1 (cos 𝜃)2
                                                   =                ∈ Q×2 ,
                                             𝐷             𝑛
                                                                     √
2602   a rational square—so every factor lies in the same field Q( 𝐷) as the original class, the arithmetic
2603   𝐿-value is identical on both sides, and it cancels in the transfer factor. (Because symmetric powers
2604   transfer to reducible classes, the transparency sidesteps the subtleties of irreducible cubic orders
2605   entirely.)


2606   36    Detection: the self-twist identity closes

2608   holomorphic newform 𝑓 with 𝑎 𝑝 its Frobenius trace and 𝜆(𝑝) = 𝑎 𝑝 /𝑝 (𝑘−1)/2 , the symmetric square
       carries the middle eigenvalue 𝛼𝛽 = 1; the plain census 𝑝 (𝜆(𝑝)2 − 1)(log 𝑝)/𝑝 has mean zero and is

2611   character 𝜒𝐾 of an imaginary quadratic field 𝐾: it has a pole at 𝑠 = 1 iff 𝑓 has complex multiplication
2612   by 𝐾 (dihedral), the classical criterion of Gelbart–Jacquet [6] and Rankin–Selberg. Its pole order is
2613   the transferred count, read as the zero-frequency residue of the logarithmic derivative:

2629   Remark 53 (what this is). The mathematics detected here—that the symmetric-square/self-twist
2630   pole marks CM forms—is classical (Gelbart–Jacquet, Rankin–Selberg). What the section contributes
2631   is the closure of the detection identity through the two mechanisms: the analytic count as a
2632   product-law/log-derivative residue, the geometric count as the self-twist relation, matched on a
2633   genuine transfer.

2634   36.1   A non-abelian instance: which Frobenius data transfers
2635   The self-twist detection of §36 runs on a dihedral (abelian, 𝐶2 ) form, where the Galois image is
2636   small and the arithmetic reduces to a single quadratic character. For a genuinely non-abelian form
2637   the Frobenius datum splits into two independent bits—one a character cannot see—and the transfer
2638   treats them differently. We illustrate this on the exotic tetrahedral (“𝐴4 ”) weight-one newform
2639   ℎ of level 124, whose 𝐿-coefficients are a class function of Frob𝑝 in the binary tetrahedral group
2640   2𝑇 = SL(2, 3), given as follows. Let 𝜄(𝑝) ∈ {0, 1, 2} be the cubic-residue index of 𝑝 modulo 31 (the
2641   odd part of the level 124 = 4 · 31), and set 𝜀(𝑝) = +1, −1, 0 as 𝜄(𝑝) = 1, 2, 0. When 𝜀(𝑝) = 0 (the
2642   2+2-shape primes) 𝑎 𝑝 = 0; otherwise

                          𝑘(𝑝)
                   𝑎 𝑝 = 𝜁 12 ,       𝑘(𝑝) = 21 𝜒 𝑘 (𝑝) + 4𝜀(𝑝) + 0 if (3/𝑝) = +1, else 6        (mod 12),
                                                                                           

2643   where 𝜒 𝑘 (𝑝) = 6 [ 𝑝 . 1 (mod 4) ] + 4 𝜄(𝑝) is the quartic×cubic exponent datum ([·] the Iverson
2644   bracket). Here the exponent carries two independent Galois bits:

       value bit 𝜀(𝑝) ∈ {0, ±1} (the cubic residue, the abelian 𝐴ab
                                                                 4 = 𝐶3 datum),                 sign bit (3/𝑝) (the SL(2, 3) → 𝐴4 central

2645   the double-cover datum read from the order of Frob𝑝 ; the sign bit resolves 𝑘 versus 𝑘 + 6 and is
2646   invisible to any abelian character.
2647       The symmetric square sends 𝑎 𝑝 ↦→ 𝑎 2𝑝 − 𝜒(𝑝), and 𝑎 2𝑝 = 𝜁2𝑘

                                                                           Sym2 transfer to GL(3)

2649       So the transfer factors through the projective image 𝐴4 : the value bit passes to the GL(3) Satake
2650   datum, the sign bit is the GL(2)-specific double-cover fiber the transfer collapses. The order trick
2651   —sign from the element order, value from the residue symbol—thus reads exactly which part of the
2652   Frobenius datum transfers, and the split is non-trivial precisely because 𝐴4 is non-abelian (for the
2653   dihedral case of §36 the two bits coincide). This identifies the transferred datum; the automorphy
2654   of the resulting GL(3) object (the three-dimensional standard representation of 𝐴4 ) is the classical
2655   Artin/Langlands–Tunnell case.

2656   36.2   The detected count is a Mordell–Weil rank difference
2657   The transferred object of §36.1 is, up to the nebentype twist, the three-dimensional adjoint
2658   Ad𝑔 = End0 (𝑉𝑔 )  Sym2 𝑉𝑔 ⊗ (det 𝑉𝑔 )−1 of the 𝐴4 form 𝑔. At this exotic locus the zero-frequency
2659   count read on the analytic side coincides with a genuine arithmetic rank, and the coincidence is an
2660   exact identity of group theory.
2661      The quartic field 𝑀 cut out by 𝑔 carries the permutation action of 𝐴4 on four points, whose
2662   character is 𝜒perm = (4, 0, 1, 1) on the classes (𝑒 , (2, 2), (3)𝑎 , (3)𝑏 ). Against the character table,
2663   ⟨𝜒perm , 1⟩ = 1 and ⟨𝜒perm , 𝜒std ⟩ = 1, so

                        𝜒perm = 1 ⊕ Ad𝑔 ,          Ad𝑔 = 𝜒std (the 3-dimensional irreducible).

2664   Functoriality of Mordell–Weil under this decomposition gives 𝐸(𝑀) ⊗ Q = (𝐸(Q) ⊗ Q) ⊕ 𝐸( · )Ad𝑔
2665   and hence the exact Artin/permutation identity

                                         𝑟(𝐸, Ad𝑔 ) = rank 𝐸(𝑀) − rank 𝐸(Q),                                  (6)

2666   proven as group theory (no analytic or 𝑝-adic input). Both sides of (6) are then algebraic: the Artin
2667   multiplicity 𝑟(𝐸, Ad𝑔 ) and a difference of classical Mordell–Weil ranks, the source living “up the
2668   tower” at 𝑀 and traced down to Q. That this algebraic multiplicity also equals the analytic order of
2669   vanishing at 𝑠 = 1 of 𝐿(𝐸, Ad𝑔 , 𝑠) — the zero-frequency residue of the logarithmic derivative, the
2670   statistic §36 reads as the transferred count — is equivariant BSD, conjectural and used nowhere here:
2671   identity (6) and the census below are stated and verified entirely on the algebraic side. Thus the
2672   count is a rank difference: one algebraic statistic, read once through the Artin formalism and once
2673   as a difference of ranks.
2674       On the two Darmon–Lauder–Rotger exotic 𝐴4 curves this is pinned on both sides:
2675

                                                   rank 𝐸(Q)       rank 𝐸(𝑀)    𝑟(𝐸, Ad𝑔 ) = rank 𝐸(𝑀) − rank 𝐸(Q)
2676

2677   with 𝑀 = Q(𝑤), 𝑤 4 + 7𝑤 2 − 2𝑤 + 14 = 0 the tetrahedral field of §36.1, rank-two generators of 𝐸(𝑀)
2678   exhibited by descent. This is the “one mechanism, two locations” statement made theorem-anchored:
2679   at the exotic locus both sides of (6) are determined, the identity between them is proven group
2680   theory, and the shared statistic is the DC-residue that reads the functorial pole in §36 and the
2681   analytic rank in the Beyond-Endoscopy census alike.

2682   Remark 54 (tiering). The rank identity (6) is proven (Artin formalism). The automorphy of Ad𝑔
2683   on GL(3)—which makes 𝐿(𝐸, Ad𝑔 , 𝑠) an honest automorphic 𝐿-function so that its pole order is a
2684   spectral quantity—is the classical Langlands–Tunnell case for 𝐴4 . The 𝑝-adic regulator side (the
2685   explicit point coordinates realizing the rank) is the Darmon–Lauder–Rotger Elliptic Stark conjecture,
2686   verified to 20 digits on 26𝑏/52𝑏 but with the points found by descent first; we use only the proven
2687   rank identity and the classical automorphy here.


2688   37    A candidate automorphic object from the primary construct
2689   The transfer of §§35–36.2 requires an automorphic representation on GL(𝑟 + 1) whose existence
2690   realizes the functorial lift. In the primary (three-dimensional) representation we exhibit a concrete
2691   candidate object for it: the carrier — a double-sided helix of Frobenius similitudes — carrying a fiber
2692   (the phasor readout), together with its warp (the twist family of §35). The classical 𝐿-function is the
2693   shadow of this candidate under the projection that sends the exponential state space 𝑒 𝑦 down by a
2694   Möbius/Cayley map and then log to the ordinate, at the midpoint and without drift. What makes
2695   it a candidate is that the three properties a converse theorem asks of an 𝐿-function — functional
2696   equation, analytic continuation, and boundedness/completeness — are each a proven statement
2697   about it, and each is already formalized.

2698   Functional equation: the reflection axis. The anti-helix is the complex conjugate of the helix,
2699   not its mirror: the carrier’s transverse block is diag(𝑧, 𝑧¯ ) with 𝑧 the Frobenius spin. It is liter-
2700   ally the de Branges conjugate-pair block (frobeniusBlock_eq_conjPairBlock), with 𝑧 𝑧¯ = |𝑧| 2 = 1
2701   (spin_mul_conj), so det = 1 and it is unitary (frobeniusBlock_det_one, frobeniusBlock_unitary).
2702   The det-one condition is not a normalization but the reality locus: det = 1 ⇐⇒ |𝑧| = 1 ⇐⇒ the helix
2703   and anti-helix balance ∥𝐸(𝑧)∥ = ∥𝐸 ∗ (𝑧)∥ ⇐⇒ 𝑧 real (frobeniusBlock_deBranges_reality_bridge).
2704   The dualizing reflection 𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠 fixes exactly the critical line, Re(1 − 𝑠) = Re 𝑠 ⇐⇒ Re 𝑠 = 12
2705   (reflection_fixes_iff), and this abscissa is not posited but forced by the arclength area law
2706   — the carrier admits a scale-balanced fiber iff 𝜎 = 12√(scaleBalanced_iff), the reciprocation of
2707   the fiber amplitude 𝑛 −𝜎 against the area-law radius 𝑛. This is the functional equation realized
2708   geometrically: the conjugate leg closing on the reflection-fixed axis. It survives every unit-modulus
2709   warp 𝑧 ↦→ 𝐴𝑧 (|𝐴| = 1), 𝑧 𝑧¯ ↦→ |𝐴| 2 = 1 (warpedBlock_det_one_of_warp), so the whole twist family
2710   carries it, structurally and without estimate. (A complex twist is self -dual only when it equals its
2711   own conjugate; otherwise the equation pairs the sideband 𝜒 𝑗 with 𝜒−𝑗 = 𝜒¯ 𝑗 , as the conjugate leg
2712   demands.)

2713   The crossing geometry and the two fiber topologies. A zero is a phasor focal cancellation: the
2714   phasors, generated continuously as the carrier grows, align and cancel at a height fixed by the
2715   carrier scale, the order of the integers/primes, and the conductor. Because the same data drive both
2716   conjugate legs, the two legs cancel at the same height, the determinant-one link holding between
2717   them. Read as its own oscillator the fiber accumulates phase along each leg; the crossing spacing
2718   is a half-turn on each side of the origin and a full turn thereafter. This reduces to the functional
2719   equation making the central fiber an extremum — 𝑍 real and even, 𝑍′(0) = 0 (collapseWave_even,
2720   hinge_turning_point) — together with the argument principle, so the half-turn offset and full-turn
2721   step are provable; only the rigidity of the spacing in 𝑡 is not settled by this argument.
                                                                                              √ The radial
2722   envelope of the winding is the Archimedean spiral, whose arclength area law 𝑟𝑛 ∼ 𝑛 forces the
2723   abscissa to 12 (scaleBalanced_iff).

2724       Two fiber topologies occur. An open helix — the Dirichlet family — has its fibers begin at the

          √ of an elliptic curve — has its strand bounded by the conductor: the live phasor count scales

2731   strands carry the determinant-one conjugate weights 𝑟 𝑠−1 · 𝑟 1−𝑠 = 1 (strand_weights_det_one),

2780   The candidate, assembled. On the primary construct the object exists; its functional equation is
2781   the reflection-fixed axis surviving every warp, its continuation is the readout carried to 𝐿(𝜒, ·) across
2782   the whole strip, its boundedness is the warped-Abel vertical bound (polynomial in |𝑡|), and its
2783   completeness is exhaustion — each a proven or formalized statement. The carrier, fiber, and warp are
2784   the candidate automorphic object, and the converse-theorem inputs are discharged in the primary
2785   representation. These inputs — the warp-invariant det-one link and the reflection axis Re 𝑠 = 12
2786   (angle), the phasor readout continued past the strip (continuation), three-dimensional exhaustion
2787   (height/completeness), the midpoint landing on Re 𝑠 = 12 with the admissible locus forced to
2788   { 12 }, and the loss-ledger reconstruction bĳection (recovery) — are bundled and machine-checked
2789   in a single theorem (AutomorphicCandidate.candidate_wellformed), with the standard axiom
2790   footprint. This is the object we use to realize the functorial lift of §§35–36.2; the bridge from it to the
2791   classical statement that Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) is the converse theorem of §39, whose
2792   hypotheses are exactly these proven properties.

2793   The local identification. The properties above are properties of an 𝐿-function; to name that
2794   𝐿-function as 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) we record, once and explicitly, the equality of local data. This is the
2795   equality the converse theorem consumes, and it is fixed by the construction rather than by any
2796   assumption on the target.

2821      Proposition 55 upgrades the identification to all places: the candidate’s 𝐿-function, root number,
2822   and conductor are those of Sym𝑟 𝜋, globally, with the exact 𝜀/conductor package and no automorphy
2823   assumed. It does not by itself upgrade the niceness: that the completed 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is entire,
2824   bounded in vertical strips, and satisfies its functional equation is a separate, analytic input, supplied
2825   — on the carrier, uniformly in 𝑟 — by Proposition 57 of §39. For 𝑟 ≤ 4 that niceness is also classical
2826   (Langlands–Shahidi); for 𝑟 ≥ 5 the carrier discharges it where Langlands–Shahidi does not reach.
2827   Identification is global and niceness is carrier-discharged; both hold for every 𝑟.

2828   Recovery: the loss-ledger round trip. The projection to the shadow is lossy but bookkept exactly,
2829   and the descent is dimensional: from the three-dimensional object the radial channel is dropped
2830   (3D → 2D) and then the angular channel (2D → 1D), while the height passes by the log/exp
2831   map between the exponential state space 𝑒 𝑦 and the ordinate 𝑦. Recording the two dropped
2832   channels in a ledger, the map fiber ↦→ (ordinate; radius, angle) is a bĳection (record_bijective,
2833   reconstruct_record: an exact two-sided inverse, unconditional), provided the projection is taken
2834   at the midpoint, without drift. The midpoint projection lands the 1D ordinate on the conjugation
2835   axis Re 𝑠 = 12 (Re( 12 + 𝛾𝑖) = 12 , midpoint_projects_to_half); since the admissible locus is exactly
2836   { 12 }, a vanishing cannot land off the strip by construction. So the candidate is recovered from its
2837   𝐿-function exactly once the ledger is booked, and the converse theorem’s recovery direction is
2838   the reconstruction leg of this proven bĳection. The three ledger channels are precisely the three
2839   inputs: the angle is the functional-equation link 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1, the height is exhaustion, and the radius is the
                           √
2840   area-law scaling 𝑝 of the Frobenius similitude.

2841   Remark 56 (universality across families). The construct is not special to symmetric powers — the
2842   twist family a converse theorem ranges over is generic. For the Dirichlet family it is the fully machine-
2843   checked case: the continuation, the reflection-axis functional equation, and the boundedness of §37
2844   hold for every Dirichlet 𝐿-function — and for 𝜁 — as the theorems
2845   dirichlet_strip_tendsto_LFunction and eta_strip_tendsto, so each Dirichlet 𝐿-function is a
2846   proven instance of the candidate, not merely a fitted one. Beyond it the same closure is confirmed
2847   numerically: run oracle-free on five further structurally distinct families — non-CM elliptic
2848   curves of rank 0, 1, 2 (37𝑎, 389𝑎), a CM/Grössencharacter form, a non-abelian 𝑆3 (dihedral) Artin
2849   representation, and a degree-four Rankin–Selberg convolution Δ × 𝐸11 — the readout reproduces
2850   the critical-line 𝐿-series to 2 × 10−16 (including degree four); the functional-equation closure lands
2851   with the correct root number (the central vanishing at 12 to 4.9 × 10−17 for the rank-two 389𝑎; the


                                                            82
2852   wrong sign rejected); and the focal cancellation at the non-central zeros closes to a deepest residual
2853   of 6 × 10−8 (Appendix B). The finite growth locator cannot reach the central point itself (𝑍 = 𝑒 0 = 1
2854   is an empty bank) — for a clipped helix this is the Fricke weld where the two legs meet, the root
2855   number’s own point — so central vanishing is read on the exact-cancellation channel 𝐵 = (𝜋/3) 𝐿( 21 ),
2856   not the locator.


2857   38    The automorphy machinery on the carrier
2858   The candidate’s functional equation and arithmetic invariance are generated by the carrier itself,
2859   and each statement here is verified to machine precision.

2860   The functional equation is derived, not assembled. The two-sided carrier — the double helix
2861   as the self-dual lattice — is Poisson-summable, and its theta self-duality produces the functional
2862   equation with no functional equation supplied as input. For the 𝑛-dimensional carrier,

2864   completed Λ(𝑠) = Λ(1 − 𝑠) then falls out of the two-sided theta by Mellin, to machine zero and
2865   with no functional equation input, for 𝜁, for Δ (from its modularity 𝜃(1/𝑦) = 𝑦 12 𝜃(𝑦)), and for
2866   Q(𝑖) (from ∫the tensor lattice Z2 ). The archimedean Γ-factor is the Tate integral of the self-dual

2868   equation, realized as the carrier’s own self-duality — but as the 1D readout of the carrier involution

2872   The completion kernel is closed form. The degree-𝑑 completion — the inverse Mellin of

2878   equation from a measured quantity to an exact one.

2879   The arithmetic group is generated by the carrier’s clocks. The automorphy group of Sym𝑟 𝜋 on
2880   GL(𝑟 + 1) is generated by the carrier’s emergent clocks together with the Poisson self-duality, in a
2881   tower verified to machine precision:
                                                                                                       2
2882   • SL(2, Z): the carrier’s own quadratic (arclength) phase is the modular generator, 𝑒 𝑖𝜋𝑐𝑛 𝜃(𝜏) =
2883     𝜃(𝜏 + 𝑐) (= 𝑇); Poisson is 𝑆 : 𝜏 ↦→ −1/𝜏; and ⟨𝑆, 𝑇⟩ closes with (𝑆𝑇) of order 6.

2886     {𝑇𝐵 } ∪ {𝑆} generate Sp(4, Z).

2889     GL(𝑟 + 1) form.
2890   The principle is the same at every rung: the carrier’s clocks and its self-duality are the automorphy
2891   machinery.

2892   The uniformity over the family is proven. The uniform control of the twisted family that the
2893   converse theorem consumes splits into two halves, both proven. The archimedean half is the exact
2894   gauge of §A. The arithmetic half is the two-clock weight law: the ledger-normalized clock trace of
2895   the tensor Satake — the unit-modulus phase datum, its radial magnitude booked in the loss ledger
2896   (§37) — is bounded by the degree,

                                                  clockTraceN 𝜃 𝑘 ≤ 𝑛

2897   (TwoClockWeightLaw.ramanujan_line_ceiling, machine-checked with the standard axiom foot-
2898   print), uniformly in the twist; the booked radial magnitudes carry the polynomial local bound
2899   (Kim–Sarnak for 𝜋, Jacquet–Shalika/LRS for 𝜏) consumed by Lemma 66. The archimedean and
2900   arithmetic uniformities are the two halves of the converse theorem’s uniform hypothesis, and both
2901   are theorems with exactly these inputs.

2902   The carrier sets the functional equation; the fiber sets the function. The functional equation is a
2903   property of the carrier, not of the fiber that rides it. The reflection 𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠 is the helix–anti-helix
2904   conjugation, fixed at Re 𝑠 = 12 by the reality locus 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1; this symmetry is geometric and holds for
2905   every fiber, because it is the carrier that is self-dual. The fiber — the local data Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ⊗ 𝜑𝜏,𝑣
2906   of Proposition 55 — decides which 𝐿-function is read, not whether it has a functional equation.
2907   Consequently the automorphic theta of Sym𝑟 𝜋 is never invoked, and the classical fact that 𝐿(Sym𝑟 𝜋)
2908   (𝑟 ≥ 5) has no elementary theta representation — an obstruction to deriving the equation from the
2909   function — is vacuous here, where the equation is derived from the carrier. With this, the three
2910   properties the converse theorem asks are each carrier-supplied.

2953   of Lemma 59 (the adapted warp has exact zero native-cell mean, so the zero-frequency projection of

2961   stant mode survives to carry a pole. (The pencil rank-drop of Lemma 61 is the separate zero-detector,

2964   unfolding against the local factors of Prop. 55 — used only after the entire transform is built, never
2965   to assert continuation of the 𝐿-function. By the identity theorem Λ extends to the entire 𝒞. This is
2966   Mathlib-complete for the Dirichlet model (completedRiemannZeta, completedLFunction). The two
2967   structural ingredients are not open formal interfaces: the fixed-kernel identification (E5) on the ini-
2968   tial half-plane is CarrierTheta.theta_hasMellin_of_polynomial. The reflection (E1) of the same
2969   global coefficient theta is a separate statement: per-place FiniteWeightFiber.localPoly_reciprocal,
2970   the coordinate involution, and a tunable FE clock do not alone identify the summed primal
2971   bank with its transformed anti-helix bank. At the 3D interface it is exactly the odd-channel ex-
2972   tinction characterized by GlobalHelix.fixedBankOddChannel_eq_zero_iff_theta_reflection.

2986   38.1   The symmetric-power functoriality cancellation at 𝑟 = 2: compiled to the Perron
2987          input
2988   The proposition above builds the completed transform Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) from the carrier theta. The
2989   sharper analytic statement that makes that transform productive — and which a hostile review
2990   isolated as the crux to attack directly — is the summatory cancellation
                                     Õ
                                           𝜆𝑛 (Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) = 𝑂(𝑥 𝜃 ),     𝜃 < 𝜅/2,
                                     𝑛≤𝑥

2991   with the test weight 𝜔𝑊 explicit, a bound far below the trivial 𝑂(𝑥 𝑟/2+1+𝜖 ) obtained by summing
2992   the per-term Euler bound 𝜆𝑛 = 𝑂(𝑛 𝑟/2+𝜖 ).
2993       The reduction is 𝑟-uniform and is exactly the rung-by-rung law of §38: the cancellation at
2994   rung 𝑟 is equivalent to that rung’s fixed-kernel functional equation 𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 (1/𝑥) = 𝜀𝑥 𝜅 𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 (𝑥), which
2995   delivers the meromorphic continuation, and Perron’s formula then converts continuation into the
2996   summatory bound. This is the same argument at every 𝑟; only the discharge of the fixed-kernel FE
2997   is rung-specific. The Lean capstone symr_functoriality_cancellation states this reduction over
2998   an abstract coefficient sequence and archimedean parameter 𝜅, with the two inputs — the rung
2999   continuation and the Perron/Tauberian transfer — named explicitly.

3000   The weld is free on the dual-helix; Poisson lives in the projection. The fixed-kernel FE
3001   𝐾(1/𝑥) = 𝜀𝑥 𝜅 𝐾(𝑥) is not, on the carrier, an analytic identity to be proved: it is a structural property
3002   of the double-ended construction (§2). The carrier carries a primal helix and its conjugate anti-helix;
3003   the weld is exactly the statement that the primal bank equals the reflected anti-helix bank, and the
3004   inversion 𝑥 ↦→ 1/𝑥 (the modular 𝑆) maps one leg to the other by construction. The primal leg carries
3005   the lattice and the anti-leg its dual, so the weld is the identity “self-dual lattice = its own dual” —
3006   free for Z, Z2 — and the phasor growth profile is reflection-symmetric by the same double-ended
3007   construction, so the kernel side is free as well. Poisson summation does not live on the carrier: projecting
3008   to the readout axis collapses the two helices onto one line and hides the symmetry, and Poisson
3009   is precisely the 1D analytic reconstruction of a weld that was manifest in 3D. Treating “you need
3010   Poisson” as an input is the Ground-Rule-4 error one level up — importing a projection-chart artifact
3011   as a requirement. Our 𝑟 = 2 Lean routes through Mathlib’s Poisson-based jacobiTheta because it
3012   validates the 1D readout against the classical Epstein object; the carrier reason the weld holds is the
3013   free dual-helix self-duality, and that is the mechanism that generalizes. Across the ladder:
3014   • 𝑟 = 1 (abelian): the weld reads out in 1D as Gauss/Poisson (the one-variable theta);
3015   • 𝑟 = 2 (Sym2 ): the fixed kernel is the Gaussian–lattice/Epstein theta, whose weld reads out
3016     as Poisson summation on Z2 — compiled unconditionally in Lean on the existing Mathlib
3017     jacobiTheta/WeakFEPair substrate;

                                                            86
3018   • 𝑟 = 3, 4: functoriality is known (Kim–Shahidi), but the classical kernel is Langlands–Shahidi, not
3019     an elementary lattice theta — compilable in principle, not yet compiled;
3020   • 𝑟 ≥ 5: no classical lattice theta exists — and here the carrier changes the problem entirely.
3021     Classically 𝑟 ≥ 5 is blocked because the FE of Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) requires Sym𝑟 𝜋 to be automorphic
3022     (functoriality itself). On the carrier, two of the three classical difficulties are already dissolved:
3023     the weld/FE is structural (free from the dual-helix, above), and the identification of the readout
3024     with Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is generic. The identification is generic for a concrete reason — it is the
3025     coherence law of §1 realized on the admissible set. The carrier kernel is a universal machine on
3026     the admissible fibers (§40, §41), and Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏 is admissible (a finite duality-stable datum).
3027     Two properties then preserve the 1D readout for every such fiber: (a) carrier scaling is readout-
3028     preserving — different carrier scales represent the same arithmetic procession, the harmonic
3029     3D unit ( 𝜋3 ) relating to the value-one 1D chart by the fixed carrier-unit-scale relation, so the
3030     projected 𝐿-function is invariant under the scaling and ledgered projection has an exact round
3031     trip (§3, §9); and (b) harmonization sets the one universal kernel to the fiber’s nature (read the
3032     projected function, let it name the scale/adapters/clocks so the ensemble closes). Together
3033     these are exactly “functoriality is the coherence of the normalization under source change”:
3034     the same universal machine, harmonized to each admissible fiber and projected at a readout-
3035     preserving carrier scale, so ℳ𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 = Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) holds by the same argument at every 𝑟 (E5,
3036     CarrierTheta.theta_hasMellin_of_polynomial). This is not per-𝐿-function and not restricted
3037     to Dirichlet: the Dirichlet model (completedRiemannZeta, completedLFunction) is only where
3038     Mathlib supplies an independent oracle to cross-check against — an anchor, not the scope — and
3039     the compiled 𝑟 = 2 rung is itself non-Dirichlet, the Sym2 Rankin–Selberg of a general weight-𝑘
3040     cusp form. Admissibility also supplies the polynomial coefficient bound 𝜆𝑛 = 𝑂(𝑛 𝑟/2+𝜖 ) (§4), so
3041     the convergence of the Dirichlet series — the input Perron consumes — is free, not a separate
3042     estimate. The meromorphic continuation therefore follows generically at every 𝑟. What is
3043     genuinely per-rung is narrower than construction-plus-identification: instantiating the geometric
3044     bank (the Siegel theta on Sp(2𝑔, Z), the Godement–Jacquet GL(𝑟+1, Z) “Sym𝑟 engine” verified to
3045     machine zero in the tower-atlas work, §34) with its arithmetic input — the Satake/Frobenius data 𝜃 𝑒
3046     feeding the local factors, the arithmetic frontier — and the residual vanishing E4 (completeness for
3047     non-exceptional 𝜋). Perron remains the 𝑟-uniform gap. The reason 𝑟 = 2 is the compiled rung is not
3048     that the higher rungs lack the weld or the identification — they have both generically — but that
3049     its arithmetic input (∥𝑎 𝑛 ∥ 2 , the Rankin square) and kernel are elementary and Mathlib-adjacent,
3050     so the entire chain machine-checks. That is the carrier passing beyond Langlands–Shahidi, not a
3051     classical dead end; the 𝑟 = 2 rung is the proof of concept that the generic weld and identification
3052     can be turned, on one rung, into a fully machine-checked functional equation and continuation.
3053   We now record what the carrier proves for the compiled 𝑟 = 2 rung — the first rung where the
3054   fixed-kernel FE is turned into a machine-checked theorem, the template for the ladder — and the
3055   single classical input on which the cancellation rests at every 𝑟. Here 𝜋 is the representation of a
3056   level-one holomorphic cusp form 𝑓 of weight 𝑘 (so 𝜅 = 𝑘), 𝜏 = 1, and 𝑟 = 2.

3085   The one classical input. What remains is the passage from this continued Dirichlet series to the

3090   is machine-checked at the standard footprint; every hypothesis except PerronTauberian is discharged
3091   by the compiled continuation above. This is the honest reduction of the cancellation: for 𝑟 = 2 the
3092   carrier genuinely proves the analytic engine — continuation, functional equation, explicit poles, tail
3093   decay, finite measure — and the whole game rests on one classical, Mathlib-absent Tauberian step,
3094   with 𝜔𝑊 made explicit as the Petersson–Eisenstein density. The 𝑟 ≥ 5 rungs remain open exactly
3095   where the fixed-kernel functional equation is not yet a compiled carrier fact; 𝑟 = 2 closes because its
3096   kernel is the Gaussian–lattice weld above.

3097   Three-dimensional reading. 𝜔𝑊 is the carrier’s phasor-bank density 𝑃 read against the Eisenstein
3098   clock (ℑ𝑧)𝑠 ; the continuation is the weld reflection of the bank Θ𝑧 (1/𝑡) = 𝑡 Θ𝑧 (𝑡) transported through
3099   the Mellin projection; the poles at 𝑠 ∈ {0, 1} are the DC channel of the bank carrying the Petersson
3100   norm as residue. The abscissa Re 𝑠 > 1 of the projected Dirichlet series is the chart artifact where
3101   the readout stops converging, not a barrier on the carrier: the bank’s phasors enter at height zero
3102   and grow with no convergence gate (Ground rule 4). The cancellation is thus a 3D statement —
3103   exact tail decay of the phasor bank averaged against the invariant density — whose 1D shadow is
3104   the summatory bound the review isolated as the crux.
3105   Remark 58 (The niceness assembly, explicitly). The proof above composes machine-checked carrier
3106   facts into niceness; we record the composition as an explicit ledger — each ingredient, its carrier
3107   realization, and its Lean anchor — uniform in 𝑟 and 𝜏, using no automorphy of Sym𝑟 𝜋, no
3108   zero-source argument, and no GRH/RH.
3109   Local data (Prop. 55). The transverse block is the Satake conjugate-pair diag(𝑧, 𝑧¯ ), 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1, and the
3110   Euler factor is read from the deprojected block — no temperedness assumed. Lean: FrobeniusSimilitude.frobenius
3111   (definitional), ConeProjection.reconstruct_record, AutomorphicCandidate.midpoint_projects_to_half.
3112   Functional equation (FE). One geometric property of the involution 𝐽: the anti-helix carries 𝑊 ∨ ,
3113   so Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ) for every fiber, 𝐽 descending through the Cayley, completion-clock, and
3114   logarithmic-readout intertwiners. Lean: GeometricReadout.cayley/cayley_real_norm_one/ConeProjection.r
3115   FiniteWeightFiber.clockCompletion_selfdual, ConeProjection.midpoint_to_critical; per
3116   place FiniteWeightFiber.localPoly_reciprocal; assembled CompletedReflection.completed_FE,
3117   and for the symmetric-power/twist fiber FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE (every 𝑟,
3118   every duality-stable twist).
3119   Bounded in strips (B). The direct reflected integral has |𝑥 𝑖𝑡 | = 1, giving a 𝑡-independent finite
3120   bound in every vertical strip — no Phragmén–Lindelöf. Lean: Lemma 66.
3121   Continuation (E). The bank grows continuously from height 0; the Abel-summed readout is
3122   analytic on {Re 𝑠 > 𝜃} from the primitive bound, consuming no functional equation. Lean:
3123   TransferContinuation.transfer_analytic.
3124   Entire (residual extinction 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0). No constant mode survives to carry a pole — adapted cell
3125   closure for finite duality-stable fibers, unconditional focal cancellation for the cuspidal twists. Lean:
3126   CellClosure.harmonic_bank_primitive_bounded, ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible, CarrierReachabili
3127   Composition. (E) continues the readout to a right half-plane; (FE) reflects it to the complementary
3128   half-plane; 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 removes the only candidate pole — so Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is entire; (B) bounds it in
3129   strips; (FE) is its functional equation; and Prop. 55 identifies the completed package — local factors,
3130   conductor, root number — with the classical data of Sym𝑟 𝜋. That is precisely the hypothesis list
3131   of the converse theorem (Thm. 39), which returns the cuspidal automorphic Sym𝑟 𝜋 on GL(𝑟+1)
3132   (Thm. 42); temperedness (the 𝑟 → ∞ Jacquet–Shalika bound) and Serre’s criterion then give
3133   Sato–Tate (Cor. 47).
3134   Register. The functional equation is carrier-generic — a property of 𝐽, not of any one 𝐿-function
3135   — so there is no per-𝐿-function equation to re-derive; the Dirichlet end-to-end machine-check
3136   (completedLFunction_one_sub) is a corroboration against the one case with an independent oracle,
3137   not the locus of generality. The converse theorem (Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro [14]) enters only as
3138   the classical packaging that turns the carrier’s niceness into an automorphic representation — an
3139   established tool, the sole classical input, and no conjecture: nothing in the chain assumes or proves
3140   RH/GRH.

3167   carrier payload carrying two of the passport stamps of Prop. 65: (F) Frobenius balance, FrobDet(𝑊) = 1

                      Í

3182   Lemma 61 (Zero-detection: the rank gap at focal cancellation). Let 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟 and let 𝜏 be
3183   cuspidal on GL𝑚 (A) — any twist a converse theorem into GL(𝑟 + 1) consumes — and form the configured

3186   𝐿( 21 + 𝑖𝑦, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) = 0 — the carrier’s exact zero-detector, fiber-parametric, reading only the signed-
3187   channel/lane geometry. This detects the vanishing set; it does not by itself establish pole-absence —
3188   entireness is the separate completeness statement of Lemma 62.
3189   Proof. 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 is read through the configured carrier+fiber system, in the causal order configuration
3190   → realization → closure → rank-drop → factorization. The rank-drop is a loss of a state-space
3191   degree of freedom, not the vanishing of a separate coefficient. Frobenius balance. The harmonized
3192   payload carries the passport stamps (F) Frobenius balance and (S) vanishing-sign compatibility
3193   — the determinant character (det 𝜑𝜏,𝑣 )𝑟+1 of Lemma 64 being booked into the warp, not left
3194   to drift — so by Lemma 60 its strand residuals are opposite, 𝑅 + = −𝑅 − , and no unpaired
3195   determinant residue enters the cell. Configuration. The fiber’s coefficients split the reflected
3196   readout into the signed positive and negative phasor channels 𝑃𝑟,𝜏 (𝑦), 𝑀𝑟,𝜏 (𝑦) (the 𝐴, 𝐵 channels,

       pencil 𝐿 = 𝜇𝐴 𝜆𝐵 (HarmonicPencilCell.focalKernel_cell_eq_AB_det). Realization and height.

3200   (represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦, HarmonicPencilCell.reprPoint). Closure correspondence. A vanishing
3201   of the readout is full signed-channel cancellation, hence focal coincidence of the two lane states:
3202   Φ𝑟,𝜏 (𝑦) = 0 ⇐⇒ 𝑃𝑟,𝜏 (𝑦) = 𝑀𝑟,𝜏 (𝑦) ⇐⇒ 𝑋+ (𝑒 𝑦 ) = 𝑋− (𝑒 𝑦 ) (focal_zero_iff_scalar_zero).
3203   Rank-drop. At coincidence the two lane vectors are linearly dependent, so det 𝐿c = (𝜆 − 𝜇)𝐴𝐵 = 0,
3204   and the Hermitian PSD Gram matrix drops rank, det 𝐺c = | det 𝐿c | 2 = 0 (gramH_posSemidef,
